1. Introduction
The NEO Redfish/Swordfish REST API is designed to provide a Redfish/Swordfish based
RESTful interface which will initially be used for cluster monitoring. The API is based on
Redfish, a management standard that uses data model representation with a RESTful interface.
Being RESTful, Redfish is easy to use and implement, being model-oriented, it can express the
relationships between components in the cluster, and the semantics of the Redfish services and
components within them. All components the API manages are represented as "resources", all
resources are accessible through a "resource tree" structure, with a well-known starting URI as
the root. Redfish also provides a model which is easy to extend. By requiring JSON
representation, Redfish enables easy integration with programming environments, and is easy to
interpret by humans. The API is extended by Swordfish, which defines a RESTful interface and
a standardized data model to provide a scalable, customer-centric interface for managing storage
and related data services. Swordfish is an extension to Redfish, and therefore follows the same
model-oriented, JSON represented semantics that Redfish standardizes.



The API is implemented in a way that the URI and "resource tree" structure will always stay the
same, regardless of the backend data sources the API populates the resources with. This model
makes the API easily extendable without changing the overall structure. The initial
implementation of the API will be used for monitoring purposes and is readonly, however, may
be extended in the future for additional management actions.



The following document describes how use the API for ClusterStor monitoring purposes.


2. High Level Usage
The following will describe how to effectively use the NEO Redfish/Swordfish API at a high
level for the purposes of cluster monitoring. Several steps to set up the API for client usage will
be described, as well as suggested methods to inventory all resources provided by the API, and
mechanisms to periodically monitor their state and status. Sections of this document that provide
more detail will be referenced throughout.


2.1. API Access
Access, Deployment and Initial Access Details
The NEO RFSF API main RESTful server listens on port 8081 on the primary MGMT node in a
ClusterStor system and can be accessed either internally OR externally to the cluster. Internally,
the API can be accessed on localhost if running from the primary mgmt node itself, or across the
private mgmt network from any other node in the cluster. Externally, the API can be accessed
across the public or customer network, the same network used for ClusterStor GUI or login, via
the configured public IP addresses for the current primary mgmt node. The API initially will use
https protocol as a read-only first iteration.

The API is deployed as a set of 6 systemd services under HA control that are required to run on
the MGMT primary node which provides access to all databases and other services that are
stored in the md64 shared management array. This set of 6 systemd HA primitive services form a
HA service group called "grp-rfsf-api" that can be failed back and forth between the two mgmt
nodes following the md64-group.

The NEO RFSF API provides only two endpoints that are accessible without an authentication
token granted to a valid ClusterStor admins user. You can either access the ServiceRoot
endpoint, or the endpoint to authenticate a user and create a session. See below for more details.

2.1.1. API TLS/HTTPS details

The API is secured by SSL certificate. It uses the same self signed certificate that Apache is
using for CSM GUI. Customer has the option to upload the certificate signed by a
trusted certificate authority (CA). The API can be accessed using HTTPS. In case of self signed
certificate, "insecure connection" must be accepted, in that, certificate validation is bypassed. For
example, using the "-k, --insecure" option in curl:

       -k, --insecure
              (TLS) By default, every SSL connection curl makes is verified to be secure.
This option allows curl to proceed and
              operate even for server connections otherwise considered insecure.

Certificate validation bypass options should not be necessary if a properly CA signed certificate
specific to that ClusterStor system is uploaded by the customer.

2.2. Session Authentication
By definition of the Redfish Specification, the only endpoints which do not require
authentication if an authentication mechanism is implemented is the /redfish/v1 (also known as
the Service Root endpoint), as well as the /redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions endpoint to create
a Session and authenticate a user. To access the rest of the API, an Authentication Token is
required. To Authenticate a user and receive a token, you must first create a ClusterStor admin
user (that is not the admin user there by default) via the cscli admins command. This user should
have a "readonly" role, and a password that meets the criteria of a user password defined by the
cscli admins command. Once the user is created, a POST request to
/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions which passes user credentials in the body will grant a user
an access token, if the request is valid. A successful POST request will create an active Session
fChasor that user. Section 3 "Token based API Authentication" provides more detail on how
this authentication request and the granted token work.

2.3. Discover details of SessionService
The SessionService resource provides more detail about Sessions that are created, as well as a
list of created Sessions. To view details of the SessionService resource, run a GET request to
/redfish/v1/SessionService. Section 3.4 "SessionService Resource" provides more detail on
this.

2.4. Discover Active Sessions
Once authenticated, it is possible to view a list of Active Sessions via a GET request to the
/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions endpoint. To view details of a specific Session, run a GET
request to /redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/{SessionId} for the SessionId of interest. This
will provide detail of which user the Session is active for, as well as information about when the
Session was created, when it expires, and how much time remains. Section 3.5 "Viewing Active
Sessions and Individual Session Details" provides more detail on how to look at active
Sessions.

2.5. Discover details of EventService
The EventService resource provides details about all EventType's and ResourcesTypes that the
API will send Events on. It will also provide a list of active EventService Subscriptions. To view
details of the EventService resource, run a GET request to /redfish/v1/EventService. Section
10.1 "EventService Resource" provides more details on this.

2.6. Event Subscription
Subscribe to Events or MetricReports from EventService

The NEO Redfish/Swordfish API provides an EventService which will receive Events from
various services which describe a change or provide metrics to a service or resource. The
EventService will then Broadcast these Events to all subscribed EventDestinations, which are
then free to do what they see fit with these Events. To subscribe to receive Events from the API
EventService, you must send a POST request to
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId}, where EventDestinationId is some
unique Id. The POST request body must be an EventDestination resource structure, which
provides a Destination field of an endpoint that EventService will broadcast Events to. Section
10.2 "Event Subscriptions" provides more detail on how to subscribe to receive Events from
EventService. Sections 10.4 “IcingaServices Events”, 10.5 “Types of Events”, and 10.6
“Resources Events Can Occur On”, provide additional detail on NEO RFSF specific Events that
may not be contained fully within the EventService resource. Section 11 “MetricReport Event
Subscriptions for Metric Data Streaming” also provides details that differentiate a MetricReport
subscription from a generic Event subscription, including the EventDestination request body
requirements, and full details of how data streaming is achieved. Please see these sections for full
NEO RFSF Event details.

2.7. Setup EventDestination
The EventDestination must implement an Event Receiver service, i.e.,
http/https service.

As mentioned above, once subscribed to receive Events from API EventService at the endpoint
specified in the subscription POST request body Destination field, clients must implement an
Event Receiver service that accepts http POST requests on the specific address and port specified
in that Destination field, in order to receive broadcasts from the API EventService. The API
EventService broadcasts Events simply by sending a POST request with the Event json body it
received as the payload to all Subscribers known to the API in
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions collection. In order to always receive Events, the Event
Receiver service to handle these POST requests must always be running, and the port specified
in the EventDestination must be open to accept tcp connections on the server of the IP address
specified in the EventDestination field. Once clients are receiving Events, it is up to the user
what they would like the Receiver Service to do with them. Section 10.7 "Subscribers
Receiving Events" provides more detail as well as an example on how to set this up.

2.8. Discover Event history
Examine individual historical Events

While it is up to the Event Receiver to decide what they want to do with Events, the NEO RFSF
API will save off history of Events for the runtime of RFSF API service. If the service is
stopped, restarted, or failed over for any reason, all Event runtime history will be lost. For this
reason it is suggested that Event Receiver services save off Events in some persistent manner. To
see all runtime Events that have occurred, you can run a GET request to /redfish/v1/Events. To
see a single runtime Event that has occurred, you can run a GET request to
/redfish/v1/Events/{EventId}. Section 10.3 "Runtime Event History" provides more details
about this, as well as Section 10.3.1 "EventCollection Resource
/redfish/v1/Events" and Section 10.3.2 "Event resource /redfish/v1/Events/{EventId}".

2.9. Event Details
Interpret the details of and react to an Event

Whether looking at the request body received on the Event Receiver side, or re-examining a
particular Event that occurred in the past, there are several useful informational fields in the
Event resource body to describe what the Event was that occurred, when that Event occurred,
what type of Event occurred, and what resource and resource type that Event occurred on.
Reacting to the Event, the Event receiver service will likely send some type of alert itself, such
as an email notification, to whatever client monitoring system may be in use - the details of the
Event resource body can provide content of that email (or whatever) alert that will be useful for
service. The client monitoring process can also be told to go run another GET request to the
resource which the Event occurred on to confirm the status change the Event may have
highlighted. It could continue to monitor the status of that resource until it returns to
"Ok". Section 10.3.1 "Event resource /redfish/v1/Events/{EventId}" and Section 10.7
"Subscribers Receiving Events" provide more detail on this topic.

2.10. ServiceRoot
Discover ServiceRoot to determine all resource service entry points

The ServiceRoot request serves as a top-level entry point to access all API resources. It displays
the sub-section Service entry points where all underlying resources exist, which shows the start
of the various paths of the API to traverse when discovering resources. As mentioned before, by
definition, the ServiceRoot request does not require an authenticated Session, but anything below
the ServiceRoot (except for Session creation endpoint) does. To view the ServiceRoot, run a
GET request to /redfish/v1. Section 4 "Redfish/Swordfish API Service Root" provides more
details on this.

2.11. Available Resources
Discover top-level resource collections and determine what they represent

As mentioned above, all of the sub-service entry points shown in the ServiceRoot resource
provide paths to all underlying resources that exist in the API. These top-level service entry
points are known as Collections, which provide a collection of all resource URIs of that
collection type that exist in the API. Also seen in the ServiceRoot resource, are the EventService
and SessionService entry point, which are not necessarily collections, but provide the paths to
collections of EventDestinations and Sessions respectively. The next step to discovering all API
resources after looking at the ServiceRoot, is to discover all resources that exist in these top-level
Collections. Below are the top-level Collections offered by the NEO RFSF API.

/redfish/v1/Events - EventCollection

   ▪   Section 10.3 "Runtime Event History" - provides more details on this

/redfish/v1/StorageSystems - the ComputerSystemCollection resource

   ▪   Section 5 "Cluster StorageSystems - StorageSystemCollection Resource
       /redfish/v1/StorageSystems" - provides more details on this

/redfish/v1/StorageServices - the StorageServiceCollection resource
   ▪   Section 8 "Cluster StorageServices - StorageServiceCollection Resource
       /redfish/v1/StorageServices" - provides more details on this

/redfish/v1/Chassis - the ChassisCollection resource

   ▪   Section 7 "Cluster Chassis - ChassisCollection Resource /redfish/v1/Chassis" -
       provides more details on this

/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions - Provides path to the EventDestinationCollection
resource

   ▪   Section 10.1 "EventService Resource" - provides more details on this

/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions - Provides path to the SessionCollection resource

   ▪   Section 3.4 "SessionService Resource" - provides more details on this

2.12. Detailed Resource Discovery
Discover each resource within a top-level resource collection and determine
what it represents, and the data it offers

As mentioned above, all of the top-level Collections resources listed above provide a collection
of all resources URIs of that collection type that exist in the API. All of these individual
resources URIs provide data about the component they represent or some service the component
they represent provides. Because there are multiple top-level resources of the same type in each
collection, each top-level resource must be uniquely identifiable by some Id, which can be
represented as a number of data points taken from the system that identifies the component each
resource represents, for example: node_id, serial_number, etc. The next step to discovering all
API resources after looking at the top-level Collections, is to run GET request to each top-level
resource in each Collection to see the data that it offers. Below are the top-level resources within
each Collection offered by the NEO RFSF API.

/redfish/v1/Events/{EventId} - the Event resource

   ▪   Section 10 "RFSF API EventService and Events" - provides more details on this

/redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{ComputerSystemId} - the ComputerSystem resource

   ▪   Section 5.1 "Storage Node Representation - ComputerSystem
       Resource: /redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{ComputerSystemId}" - provides more
       details on this

/redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId} - the StorageService resource
   ▪   Section 8.1 "Enclosure Representation - StorageService - StorageService Resource:
       /redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}" - provides more details on this

/redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId} - the Chassis resource

   ▪   Section 7.1 "Enclosure Representation - Chassis Resource:
       /redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}" - provides more details on this

/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} - the EventDestination resource

   ▪   Section 10.2 "Event Subscriptions" - provides more details on this

/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/{SessionId} - the Session resource

   ▪   Section 3.5 "Viewing Active Sessions and Individual Session Details" - provides
       more details on this

2.13. Resource Cross Referencing
Determine how top-level resources are linked to or associated with each other

The main link of top-level resources to highlight here is the ability to associate a
ComputerSystem resource (which represents a Storage node) to the Chassis and StorageService
resources it is attached to (which represents the physical Storage enclosure(s) the Storage node is
attached to). There are two main associations to highlight which can be seen within the
ComputerSystem json structures:

   ▪   ComputerSystem.HostedServices.StorageServices - shows the associated StorageService
       resources with this ComputerSystem
   ▪   ComputerSystem.Links.Oem - shows the associated Chassis resources with this
       ComputerSystem
   ▪   Section 6 "ComputerSystem Relationships to Top-level service Resources" provides
       more details

Another important piece to highlight which is all Chassis resources have a matching
StorageService resource where ChassisId == StorageServiceId. This is because both resources
represent the same Storage enclosure, but different services and sub-structure resources are
provided under each service entry point: /redfish/v1/Chassis and /redfish/v1/StorageService
respectively. Sections 7.1.2 ChassisId and 8.1.1 StorageServiceId provide more detail on this.




2.14. Resource Collections
Discover all resources which exist within sub-structures of each resource
within a top-level resource collection

Much like the cluster components the above top-level resources represent, i.e. a Storage Node or
Storage Enclosure, each of these top-level resources contain several resources within themselves
to represent additional software and hardware components provided by that cluster component.
For example, a Storage Node may contain NetworkInterface cards, and a Storage Enclosure may
contain several Drives which provide software components such as Volumes or FileSystems.
After discovering all individual top-level resources as mentioned above, the next step to
discovering all API resources is to examine the data available within each top-level resource and
continue to traverse the paths down their endpoints to discover all resources which exist within
sub-structures of these top-level resources. Below are all resource which exist within the sub-
structures of these top-level resources which represent cluster components - ComputerSystem,
StorageService and Chassis resources:

ComputerSystem sub-structure resources:
/redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{ComputerSystemId}/NetworkInterfaces - the
NetworkInterfaceCollection resource

   ▪   Section 5.2 "NetworkInterfaces - NetworkInterfaceCollection
       Resource /redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{ComputerSystemId}/NetworkInterfaces" -
       provides more details on this

/redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{ComputerSystemId}/NetworkInterfaces/{NetworkInterfaceId} - the
NetworkInterface resource

   ▪   Section 5.3 "NetworkInterface Resource
       - /redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{ComputerSystemId}/NetworkInterfaces/{NetworkInte
       rfaceId}" - provides more details on this

       Resource /redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/FileSystems" - provides
       more details on this

/redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/FileSystems/{FIleSystemId} - the FileSystem
resource

   ▪   Section 8.11 "FileSystem
       Resource /redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/FileSystems/{FileSystemId
       }" - provides more details on this
/redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/Volumes - the VolumeCollection resource

       Resource /redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/Volumes" - provides more
       details on this

2.15. Resource Dynamics
Determine how various fields for each resource change when back-end cluster
components change
All the various resources in the NEO RFSF API are intended to represent actual cluster
components that exist in a ClusterStor system. The resource fields not only show static
information to identify a cluster component, but most of them also contain dynamic fields that
represent the state or status of that cluster component at the time the GET request is run. For all
the individual resources identified above, each section has a "Details of the response" section to
highlight important fields and what they represent / are populated with, as well as a "Dynamic
Fields" section, which highlights the specific fields for each resource that can change when the
backend cluster component they represent changes. Often, an Event is broadcasted when these
dynamic fields change, indicating to the client that they should run another GET request on that
resource to see the change in the data. Not all "Dynamic fields" currently have Events
implemented for them. Please view the "Details of the response" and "Dynamic
Fields" section of each resource for more detail, as details will differ from resource to resource.

2.16. Connecting Events to API resources
One good way to determine the different types of Events that NEO RFSF API EventService can
be sent and broadcast to subscribers is by looking at the EventService resource, section 10.1
"EventService Resource" provides more details on this. Not all Events that the RFSF API
supports may be seen in the EventService resource however, as some are extensions for
ClusterStor specific Events, for example, we extended the EventService to handle Icinga2 alert-
based Events, section 10.4 "IcingaService Events" provides more details on this. Sections 10.5
“Types of Events”, and 10.6 “Resources Events Can Occur On”, also provide additional details
on the Events that RFSF API supports.

2.17. Resource tracking
Determine mechanism to periodically inventory all resources

While it is up to the client implementation, one example monitoring use case to periodically
inventory all resources is as follows (See some examples using the rfsf-api-client libraries in
section 12):

   1) General inventory loop monitoring: Client discovers full resource tree and runs GET
      requests to all resource endpoints in that tree, saving off the “cached” state of the
      resource. Periodically, another inventory of GET requests is done where the fresh data is
       compared against the cached data if anything has changed – notify of the change and on
       what resource it occurred.

2.18. Inventory resources using Events
While it is up to the client implementation, one example monitoring use case to receive and react
to Events that occur on resources is as follows (See some examples using the rfsf-api-client
libraries in section 12):

   1) Event based monitoring: Client subscribes to receive Events from API EventService at
      some EventDestination. Each time an Event is received, the client code reacts to the
      Event by parsing out the ResourceId the Event occurred on from the Event body. The
      client code then runs a GET request to that resource endpoint to determine what data has
      changed in the resource.

2.19. API Session Termination
While Sessions by default last 12 hours, and the time left shows in GET request
to /redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/{SessionId} endpoint for a particular session, it is
standard to provide a logout mechanism that immediately expires the Session and authentication
token. To do this, a DELETE request should be
sent to /redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/{SessionId}. Section 3.6 "Deleting active Session
to log user out from API" provides more details.

2.20. Unsubscribe an EventDestination
When clients want to stop receiving Events, generic or MetricReports, on a particular
EventDestination, a DELETE request can be sent to the
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} endpoint for some
EventDestinationId that was created earlier to subscribe. Section “10.8 Deleting
EventDestinationId subscription to no longer receive Events at some EventDestination” provides
more details on unsubscribing from generic Events. Section 11.6 “Send DELETE request to
cancel MetricReport EventDestination Subscription” provides more details on unsubscribing
from a MetricReport subscription, though the DELETE request is the same, the two actions
differ in their own ways.


3. Token based API Authentication
Users can access the Neo Redfish/Swordfish REST API via a JWT (JSON Web Token) which is
granted to a user via a POST request to /redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions endpoint. The
POST request must pass UserName/Password credentials in the request body which will be
checked against local cluster LDAP and validate that request was made for an existing admins
user created with the standard method to add an admin user in NEO with "cscli admins add". If
user credentials are validated, a JWT token is returned in the header of the response to the POST
request, which returns a Session resource. By default, a Session is valid for 12 hours - we may
support a configurable session time in the future.

Session resource schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/Session.v1_4_0.json

Redfish session login authentication details can be found in section 14.3.3 of the spec
here: https://www.dmtf.org/sites/default/files/standards/documents/DSP0266_1.11.1.pdf

The following provides an example of authenticating an existing admin user on the cluster to use
the API via JWT based access - this example is using the "external" server kjlmo12-oem to
access API running on kjlmo12, over the kjlmo1200 pub0 address 172.26.137.72 on dp-api-
server port 8081:

3.1. Access Denied Before Authenticating
Before authenticating, a user will only be exposed to the login endpoint:
/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions - if a request is sent to the API trying to access anything
else, a http 401 Unauthorized will be returned.

401 Unauthorized response before authenticating
 # curl https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/StorageServices | jq
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                       Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 146 100 146 0 0 142k               0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 142k
 {
     "error": {
       "code": "401",
       "message": "No Auth Token found in request header. User is NOT AUTHORIZED to use the API."
     }
 }


3.2. Login POST request
Target /redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions to authenticate a user

To authenticate an existing admin user, a POST request to /redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions
endpoint must be sent, passing the UserName / Password fields in the request body. These user
credentials will be validated against local cluster LDAP instance, to ensure the user is an existing
admin user on the cluster - created by NEO standard method to add an admin user, "cscli admins
add".

POST request body must contain the following fields:

      ▪    UserName: <username>
      ▪    Password: <password>

Sessions POST request body example
 {
     "UserName": "<username>",
     "Password": "<password>"
 }


Example POST request seen with error response if user information cannot be validated against
local cluster LDAP when user doesn't exist:

Details of the response:

      ▪    Id matches the SessionId in /redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/{SessionId} endpoint
    ▪   UserName is the authenticated User
    ▪   Oem
           ▪ StartTime: Time Session was created
           ▪ ExpirationTime: Time Session expires
           ▪ TimeLeft: Time until session expires

Note the following important information returned in the header:

    ▪   Location: /redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/dk9eDAWu4eCBZxLZabv6HC

             o   This is the location of the active Session resource with 12-hour expiration period
                 on it. Once session expires and / or dp-api.service is failed over or restarted, this
                 session will be automatically purged.

    ▪   X-Auth-Token:
        eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJVc2VyTmFtZSI6ImRtYXR0aGV3cyIsImV4cCI6MTY1NDc3M
        zE4N30.3YRjS-3TANRqjfxjhjQoys_C-9iF0PPhZP2p_pXtAZ0

             o   This is the authentication token string, which must be passed in the header of any
                 subsequent request to access the API.
             o   More details on passing the X-Auth-Token in the header seen below

3.3. Authentication Token Use
If user information is successfully validated and a valid JWT token is returned in the X-Auth-
Token field of the header of Sessions POST response, as well as a valid Session is created, the
user can then access the rest of the API using the JWT token.

The token string generated and returned in X-Auth-Token field, must be passed in subsequent
GET requests in the header in the same way it was returned:

    ▪   A key, value pair as follows:
             ▪   '{"X-Auth-Token": "<tokenString>"}'




    ▪   Best practice is to set an env variable AUTH="<tokenString>" for subsequent authorized
        requests:
    ▪   Example: export
        AUTH="eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJVc2VyTmFtZSI6ImRtYXR0aGV3c
        yIsImV4cCI6MTY1NDc3MzE4N30.3YRjS-3TANRqjfxjhjQoys_C-9iF0PPhZP2p_pXtAZ0"

Example GET request passing granted X-Auth-Token in header:

GET request authenticated with X-Auth-Token
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/StorageServices | jq
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed

     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices",

     "Description": "Collection of references StorageService Resources.",
     "Members": [
      {
              "enclosure_id: 6": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00A"

The X-Auth-Token string must be an exact match for the session created, if the string is off by
any characters - the following error response will be seen:

GET request with invalid X-Auth-Token
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/dk9eDAWu4eCBZxLZabv6HC | jq
     % Total  % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                      Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 128 100 128 0 0 125k             0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 125k
 {
   "error": {
    "code": "401",
         "message": "User is NOT AUTHORIZED to use the API. signature is invalid"
     }
 }
If the JWT token has expired, the following error response will be seen when trying to make a
request using the expired token, and the session will be automatically purged.

GET request with expired X-Auth-Token
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/dk9eDAWu4eCBZxLZabv6HC | jq
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                      Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 128 100 128 0 0 125k              0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 125k
 {
     "error": {
       "code": "401",
       "message": "User is NOT AUTHORIZED to use the API. token is expired by 5m24s. Deleting Session!"
     }
 }


If dp-api service is restarted or failed over to another node, because all Session resources are
tracked in memory all previous existing sessions will be gone and the following error response
will be seen:

GET request with X-Auth-Token that dp-api.service is no longer aware of
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/StorageServices/lustre-
 kjlmo12/FileSystems/kjlmo12 | jq
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                     Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 157 100 157 0 0 153k             0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 153k
 {
     "error": {
       "code": "401",
       "message": "User is NOT AUTHORIZED to use the API. No session found to auth token sent with request!"
     }
 }


3.4. SessionService Resource
The SessionService resource lives directly under the ServiceRoot /redfish/v1 can be seen by
issuing a GET request to /redfish/v1/SessionService. It will show a list of active Sessions as well
as details about the SessionTimeout value which will be set for all created Sessions.

SessionService GET request
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://172.26.137.73:8081/redfish/v1/SessionService | jq
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                     Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 457 100 457         0   0 446k      0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 446k
 {
     "@odata.context": "SessionService.SessionService",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/SessionService",
     "@odata.type": "SessionService.v1_1_8.SessionService",
     "Description": "SessionService for RFSF API",
     "Id": "SessionService",
     "Name": "SessionService",
     "ServiceEnabled": true,
     "SessionTimeout": "12h0m0s",
     "Sessions": {
       "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions"
     },
     "Status": {}
 }

and Individual Session Details

 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"

3.6. Deleting active Session
By default, the granted Authentication token from a successful
/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions POST request is set to expire after 12 hours. A user should
also be able to logout at any point before that 12-hour expiration period when they are done
using the API. This can be accomplished via a DELETE request
to /redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/{SessionId} for that active Session.

Details of the response:

      ▪    SessionId must match an active Session in dp-api SessionService
      ▪    There is no request body permitted for the DELETE request
      ▪    Once the DELETE request is sent, the AUTH token will no longer be valid
      ▪    User must re-authenticate to receive a new valid token in order to use the API again

Example - below shows 2 active sessions, one for user dmatthews and one for user dmatthews2:

      ▪    dmatthews is authenticated by ${AUTH} token
      ▪    dmatthews2 is authenticated by ${AUTH2} token

List of active Sessions before:

4. AccountService Resource
The AccountService resource is the redfish service which is used to manage various internal and
external user information, including but not limited to:

      •    Internally managed User accounts in the /redfish/v1/AccountService/Accounts collection
      •    Externally managed User accounts in the
           /redfish/v1/AccountService/ExternalAccountProviders
      •    User roles and privileges in the /redfish/v1/AccountService/Roles collection

The resource lives directly under the ServiceRoot /redfish/v1 can be seen by issuing a GET
request to /redfish/v1/AccountService. Because ClusterStor historically provides its own means
of user management, for initial purposes, the ClusterStor Redfish/Swordfish API will implement
the /redfish/v1/AccountService/Roles and /redfish/v1/AccountService/ExternalAccountProviders
collections only, with future plans to migrate ClusterStor user management more fully into
/redfish/v1/AccountService, including, representing and managing actual users via the
/redfish/v1/AccountService/Accounts collection, as well as other various uses of
ExternalAccountProviders.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/AccountService.v1_18_0.json
Example GET response of the /redfish/v1/AccountService endpoint:

 ~]# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/AccountService | jq
 {
     "@odata.context": "AccountService.AccountService",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/AccountService",
     "@odata.type": "AccountService.v1_9_0.AccountService",
     "Accounts": {
      "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/AccountService/Accounts"
     },
     "ActiveDirectory": {
        "@odata.id": "",
        "@odata.type": "",
        "Authentication": {},
        "LDAPService": {
           "SearchSettings": {}
          },
          "Id": "",
          "TACACSplusService": {}
     },
     "AdditionalExternalAccountProviders": {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/AccountService/ExternalAccountProviders"
     },
     "Description": "AccountService for ClusterStor DP-API",
     "Id": "AccountService",
     "LDAP": {
          "@odata.id": "",
          "@odata.type": "",
          "Authentication": {},
          "LDAPService": {
             "SearchSettings": {}
          },
          "Id": "",
          "TACACSplusService": {}
     },
     "Name": "AccountService",
     "Roles": {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/AccountService/Roles"
     },
     "ServiceEnabled": true,
     "Status": {},
     "TACACSplus": {
        "@odata.id": "",
        "@odata.type": "",
          "Authentication": {},
          "LDAPService": {
           "SearchSettings": {}
         },
         "Id": "",
         "TACACSplusService": {}
     }
 }




4.1 Role Based Access with Role Resource
Role based access for the authenticated Sessions to use the ClusterStor Redfish/Swordfish API is
managed via the redfish Role resource under the /redfish/v1/AccountService/Roles collection.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/Role.v1_3_3.json

For initial implementation, the API will automatically generate Role resources to represent the
ClusterStor admins roles available to the “cscli admins add” command:

 ~]# cscli admins add -h
 usage: cscli admins add [-h] --username USERNAME --role {full,limited,readonly} [--firstname FIRSTNAME] [--
 lastname LASTNAME]
                [--enable-ssh | --disable-ssh] [--enable-web | --disable-web] [--password PASSWD] [--stream-api]
                [--password-policy {strong,weak,default}]


 optional arguments:
 ...
    --role {full,limited,readonly}
                    Displays available roles; Select one from the list:- full: Full admin rights, limited: Provides more
                    restricted access than the Full Admin role, but is not read only and provides greater access to CSCLI
                    commands than the Read Only Admin role, readonly: Provides read only access.
 ...


 As seen above, the available ClusterStor admins user roles are:

          •    full
          •    limited
          •    readonly

 These three ClusterStor admins user roles are all represented as a
 /redfish/v1/AccountService/Roles/{RoleId} resource which are generated on startup and
 cannot be removed or modified. As seen below, these are the only three Roles which exist in
 the /redfish/v1/AccountService/Roles collection:

     ~]# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token":$RFSF_API_TOKEN https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/AccountService/Roles | jq
     {
       "@odata.context": "RoleCollection.RoleCollection",
    "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/AccountService/Roles",
    "@odata.type": "RoleCollection.v1_0_0.RoleCollection",
    "Description": "Collection of Role resources for DP-API AccountService",
    "Members": [
     {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/AccountService/Roles/full"
     },
     {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/AccountService/Roles/limited"
        },
        {
             "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/AccountService/Roles/readonly"
       }
    ],
    "Members@odata.count": 3,
    "Name": "RoleCollection"
}




When a User runs a /redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions POST request with passed in user
credentials, the API SessionService is able to determine the role of that Username via LDAP
lookup, and sets the Role of that User in the
/redfish/v1/Session/SessionService/Sessions/{SessionId} resource for the created Session:

    ~]# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
    https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/gNLfidiiNpc5exFFYuVmkg | jq
    {
      "@odata.context": "Session.Session",
      "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/gNLfidiiNpc5exFFYuVmkg",
      "@odata.type": "Session.v1_7_1.Session",
      "Description": "Session for user apiUser",
        "Id": "gNLfidiiNpc5exFFYuVmkg",
        "Links": {},
        "Name": "apiUser Session",
        "Oem": {
          "StartTime": "Mon Jul 14 15:50:13 MDT 2025",
          "ExpirationTime": "Tue Jul 15 03:59:53 MDT 2025",
             "LastAccessed": "Mon Jul 14 15:59:53 MDT 2025"
        },
        "Roles": [
           "limited"
        ],
        "UserName": "apiUser"
    }
For any subsequent request, when the token passed in the header is checked for a valid
Session (as described above in section 3) – the API SessionService will also verify that the
User Role for the associated Session has the correct privilege level to access the endpoint
and make the request they are attempting to. If the user for that Session does not have the
correct permissions, a 403 permission denied error response will be returned. See below for
more details on what each of the native ClusterStor roles mean for API access.

As mentioned before, because these roles are defined by ClusterStor management software
itself, and not via the API at this time, these Role resources cannot be removed or modified.
In the future once all ClusterStor user management has migrated under API control, we will
support additional management of Roles.

4.1.1 The readonly Role

As the name and cscli admins add help statement suggests, the readonly role is for users
with readonly access. For the API, this means that Sessions for users of this role may only
execute requests which are readonly, so may only execute GET requests. If it is detected
that a Session for a user with readonly Role attempts to run any sort of write request, the
following 403 error response will be seen:

 ~]# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
 https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-event-receiver -d
 @metric_report_subscription.json -X POST | jq
 {
   "error": {
     "code": "403",
     "message": "permission denied: user with readonly Role is forbidden to run requests which are not GET
 requests"
   }
 }



 4.1.2 The limited Role

 As the name and cscli admins add help statement suggests, users with a role of limited
 have less permissions than a full admin user, but more permissions than a readonly user,
 in that – they are not totally restricted to readonly operations. For the API, this means
 that Sessions for users of this role are allowed to make requests which perform write
 operations, but are restricted from some administrative Actions requests which perform
 administrative operations on the backend. If it is detected that a Session for a user with
 limited Role attempts to run such an administrative Action request, the following 403
 error response will be seen:
    ~]# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
    https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo17n:Node-R1C1-18U-A/Actions/Manager.PowerOff -X
    POST | jq
    {
        "error": {
          "code": "403",
          "message": "permission denied: user with limited Role is forbidden to run Manager Action requests"
        }
    }




   4.1.1 The full Role

   As the name and cscli admins add help statement suggests, users with a role of full have
   full administrative access to the system. For the API, this means that Sessions for users of
   this role are allowed to access all endpoints in the resource tree, and execute all requests
   available to the API, there is no restriction.




4.2 External Accounts with ExternalAccountProvider Resource
The /redfish/v1/AccountService/ExternalAccountProviders collection provides a means to
represent users or accounts which are managed by external systems, such as, LDAP, as well as
their means of access to the system managed by the local redfish instance, such as certificates,
credentials, etc. as an ExternalAccountProvider resource.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/ExternalAccountProvider.v1_8_1.json

For the initial purposes of the ClusterStor Redfish/Swordfish API, we will use
ExternalAccountProvider resources to represent S3 gateway user mappings to Lustre users, but
this will be expanded in the future for additional use cases.

4.2.1 S3 Lustre User Mapping Representation and Management

In order to provide users access to the Lustre filesystem via the S3 gateway protocol, user
mappings must be created on the backend S3 API which tie a Lustre username/UID/GID so an
S3 access account. These user mappings are represented as
/redfish/v1/AccountService/ExternalAccountProviders/{ExternalAccountProviderId} resource
which can be created, read, updated and deleted. For more information on the S3 gateway
protocol, please view the ClusterStor S3 network gateway documentation.

4.2.1.1 Creating an ExternalAcountProvider Resource to Represent an S3 User
Mapping

In order to create a User mapping so that lustre users may access the filesystem via S3 gateway
protocol, users may run a POST request to the
/redfish/v1/AccountService/ExternalAccountProviders endpoint with a request such as the
following:

 {
     "AccountProviderType": "S3",
     "Authentication": {
         "Username": "dmatthews"
     }
 }


 NOTE: the AccountProviderType must be set to “S3” and the Autthentication field must have
 a valid Username which you would like to create the mapping for.



 Running the POST request:

     ~]# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
     https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/AccountService/ExternalAccountProviders -d @s3_user_mapping.json -X POST
     | jq
     {
       "@odata.context": "AccountService.ExternalAccountProvider",
       "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/AccountService/ExternalAccountProviders/ZAM4fksvr8A9DDZk2GBeFc",
         "@odata.type": "AccountService.v1_9_0.ExternalAccountProvider",
         "AccountProviderType": "S3",
         "Authentication": {
            "Username": "dmatthews"
         },
         "LDAPService": {
          "SearchSettings": {}
         },
         "Id": "ZAM4fksvr8A9DDZk2GBeFc",
         "TACACSplusService": {}
     }
 This request creates an S3 user mapping via the S3 API on the backend which can be
 represented and accessed as a
 /redfish/v1/AccountService/ExternalAccountProviders/{ExternalAccountProviderId}
 resource.



4.2.1.2 Getting an ExternalAcountProvider Resource to Represent an S3 User
Mapping

To get information about a previously created ExternalAccountProvider resource which
represents an S3 User Mapping, run a GET request to the desired
/redfish/v1/AccountService/ExternalAccountProviders/{ExternalAccountProviderId} endpoint:

Example GET request:

 ~]# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
 https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/AccountService/ExternalAccountProviders/ZAM4fksvr8A9DDZk2GBeFc | jq
 {
     "@odata.context": "AccountService.ExternalAccountProvider",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/AccountService/ExternalAccountProviders/ZAM4fksvr8A9DDZk2GBeFc",
     "@odata.type": "AccountService.v1_9_0.ExternalAccountProvider",
     "AccountProviderType": "S3",
     "Authentication": {
        "Username": "dmatthews"
     },
     "LDAPService": {
        "SearchSettings": {}
     },
     "Id": "ZAM4fksvr8A9DDZk2GBeFc",
     "TACACSplusService": {}
 }




4.2.1.3 Removing an ExternalAcountProvider Resource to Represent an S3 User
Mapping

To remove an ExternalAccountProvider resource which represents an S3 User Mapping – run a
DELETE request to the desired
/redfish/v1/AccountService/ExternalAccountProviders/{ExternalAccountProviderId} endpoint.
This will remove the resource from the /redfish/v1/AccountService/ExternalAccountProviders
collection, and remove the user mapping via the S3 API on the backend:
~]# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"

5. Redfish/Swordfish API ServiceRoot
5.1. ServiceRoot Resource: /redfish/v1
The ServiceRoot endpoint /redfish/v1 describes the entry points for all resources that exist in the
API. All other resources provided by the API can be found under one of the provided service
Entry points seen in the ServiceRoot resource. Authentication is NOT required to retrieve the
ServiceRoot via a GET request to /redfish/v1.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/ServiceRoot.v1_14_0.json
Example of ServiceRoot GET request:

GET /redfish/v1 Example
 # curl https://172.26.143.246:8081/redfish/v1 | jq
   % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                       Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 839 100 839 0 0 819k              0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 819k
 {
   "@odata.context": "ServiceRoot.ServiceRoot",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1",
     "@odata.type": "ServiceRoot.v1_10_0.ServiceRoot",
     "Chassis": {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis"
     },
     "EventService": {
      "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService"
     },
     "Id": "ServiceRoot",
     "Links": {},
     "Name": "NEO RedfishSwordfish API ServiceRoot",
     "Oem": {
        "Events": {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Events"
        }
     },
     "ProtocolFeaturesSupported": {
      "DeepOperations": {}
     },
     "SessionService": {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/SessionService"
     },
     "StorageServices": {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices"
     },
     "StorageSystems": {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageSystems"
     },
     "UUID": "cf5d0f9f-b946-4b77-8975-7994423a8031"
 }


Details of the Response:

       ▪   odata.id is always set to ServiceRoot endpoint
       ▪   Id: name of the resource ServiceRoot
       ▪   Chassis: link to Chassis service entry point
       ▪   Oem.Events: link to Events service entry point
       ▪   SessionService: link to SessionService service entry point
   ▪   StorageServices: link to StorageServices service entry point
   ▪   StorageSystems: link to StorageSystems service entry point

Dynamic Fields:

   ▪   No dynamic fields



Service Entry Points:

   ▪   /redfish/v1/Chassis
           ▪ Resources: Assembly, Power, Thermal, AssemblyData, PowerSupply, Fan
   ▪   /redfish/v1/EventService
           ▪ Resources: EventDestinationCollection, EventDestination
   ▪   /redfish/v1/Events
           ▪ Resources: EventCollection, Event
   ▪   /redfish/v1/SessionService
           ▪ Resources: SessionCollection, Session
   ▪   /redfish/v1/StorageServices
           ▪ Resources: StorageServiceCollection, FileSystemCollection,
               StoragePoolCollection, VolumeCollection, FileSystem, StoragePool, Volume,
               CapacitySourceCollection, CapacitySource, DriveCollection, Drive
   ▪   /redfish/v1/StorageSystems
           ▪ Resources: ComputerSystemCollection, ComputerSystem,
               NetworkInterfaceCollection, NetworkInterface


6. Cluster StorageSystems
StorageSystemCollection Resource /redfish/v1/StorageSystems
From a Redfish/Swordfish (rfsf) REST API perspective, a NEO based ClusterStor cluster will be
represented by a StorageSystemCollection Resource:

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/swordfish/StorageSystemCollection.json:

This Collection represents a set of Storage based ComputerSystem resources, which represent
ClusterStor Storage nodes themselves (seen below).

Each StorageSystemCollection resource, uniquely identified by some Id, will be the main
ServiceRoot entry point for 5the Neo RFSF REST API. The requirements for each
StorageSystemCollection resource from the specification state that:
       ▪      StorageSystemCollection.Members: The value of each member entry shall reference a
              ComputerSystem resource that shall have a HostingRoles entry with a value of
              ‘StorageServer’.
       ▪      These ComputerSystem resources represent storage servers that support Swordfish
              storage management services
       ▪      Example StorageSystemCollection.Members URI:
              /redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{StorageSystemId}/{ComputerSystemId}



Populated StorageSystemsCollection resource to represent a cluster
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/StorageSystems | jq

                     Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed

Details of the response:

       ▪      @odata.id: the UUID of the cluster
   ▪    Members: Collection of OdataId which represent endpoints of the Storage based
        ComputerSystem resources that exist in the cluster
   ▪    Members@odata.count: the total count of ComputerSystem resources that exist in the
        cluster
   ▪    Name: the name of the cluster

Dynamic Fields:

   ▪    Members may add or remove a member from the list if a Storage node is replaced, added
        or removed
   ▪    Members@odata.count will change with the Members list

6.1. Storage Node Representation
ComputerSystem Resource:
/redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{ComputerSystemId}

From a Redfish/Swordfish (rfsf) REST API perspective, a NEO based ClusterStor Storage Node
will be represented by a ComputerSystem Resource with a HostingRoles entry with a value of
‘StorageServer’. This will in turn represent a Storage node in the Cluster:

Schema: http://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/ComputerSystem.v1_17_0.json#/definitions/Comput
erSystem

6.1.1. ComputerSystem Collections resources

   •    /redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{ComputerSystemId}/NetworkInterfaces

6.1.2. ComputerSystemId

Must be uniquely identifiable at the storage node level - will use node_id:

   •    node_id: id field from t0db.node table will be the ComputerSystemId for each
        ComputerSystem resource
   •    Example: kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-40U-A

Details of the response:

      •   Each ComputerSystem resource will be uniquely identified by some Id.
      •   Each ComputerSystem resource will contain a set of HostedStorageServices
          identified by: /redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}. Each StorageServiceId
          will represent an enclosure that provides a set of Storage Services.
      •   Each ComputerSystem resource will contain a set of Links to Chassis resources identified
          by: /redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}. Each ChassisId will represent the physical HW
          components and FRUs contained in an enclosure.
      •   Each storage enclosure will have a /redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}
          and /redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId} where StorageServiceId and ChassisId are defined
          by the same enclosure serial number.
      •   Each ComputerSystem resource will contain a Set of NetworkInterfaces to represent the
          available Network Interface Connections on the node.
      •   Each ComputerSystem resource will contain a set of IcingaServices with applicable
          Icinga Service output, name, and status.
      •   Each ComputerSystem resource will contain a PowerState field to represent the Power
          state of the node

Dynamic Fields:

      ▪   HostedServices.StorageServices - StorageService endpoints may change their
          StorageServiceId if an enclosure replacement occurs
      ▪   Links.Oem - Chassis endpoints may change their ChassisId if a enclosure replacement
          occurs
      ▪   NetworkInterfaces - list may grow or shrink if interfaces are added or removed upon
          controller replacement (only HSN interfaces typically)
      ▪   Oem.IcingaServices.Services - any IcingaService State and Output fields may change
          depending on the status of the actual Icinga service
   ▪    PowerState - may change between On, Off and Unknown depending on whether the
        node's BMC response
   ▪    SerialNumber - may change if a node gets replaced

6.2. NetworkInterfaces – NetworkInterfaceCollection
Resource
/redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{ComputerSystemId}/NetworkInterfaces
Each ComputerSystem will have a NetworkInterfaceCollection resource that lists all the
available NetworkInterface resources for that node. This includes details about external-facing
interfaces, internal-facing interfaces, and public-facing interfaces on management nodes, like
pub0, which is used for login and other external cluster tasks. Currently, there are no
NetworkInterface resources for IPMI interfaces.



Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/NetworkInterfaceCollection.json

/redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{ComputerSystemId}/NetworkInterfaces GET request

   ▪    Name: highlights the name of the ComputerSystem this collection belongs too.

Dynamic Fields:

   •    Members - list may grow or shrink if interfaces are added or removed upon controller
        replacement (only HSN interfaces typically)
   •    Members@odata.count - will grow or shrink with Members list

6.3. NetworkInterface Representation
NetworkInterface Resource
- /redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{ComputerSystemId}/NetworkInterfaces/{Netwo
rkInterfaceId}

Each NetworkInterface available in a ComputerSystem's NetworkInterfaceCollection can be
queried to get hardware, virtual, state, configuration, and other details about the interface.
Resources can either represent a physical Network Interface Card contained within a Storage
Node or a virtual network interface made up of one or more underlying physical members, as
seen below.
Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/NetworkInterface.v1_2_0.json

6.3.1 NetworkInterface Representation for a Physical Interface

As mentioned above, NetworkInterface resources can represent either a physical single interface
or a virtual interface made up of one or more physical underlying members. The response of the
NetworkInterface request which represents a physical interface contains details about that
interface only, whether it is part of an over-arching virtual interface or not. The following
example shows a NetworkInterface response which represents a physical network interface card.

/redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{ComputerSystemId}/NetworkInterfaces/{NetworkInterfaceId}
GET request
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/StorageSystems/kjlmo5:Node-R1C1-
 34U-A/NetworkInterfaces/heth0 | jq
  % Total  % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                      Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 1102 100 1102 0 0 5565            0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 5565
 {
 "@odata.context": "NetworkInterface.NetworkInterface",
 "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageSystems/kjlmo5:Node-R1C1-34U-A/NetworkInterfaces/heth0",
 "@odata.type": "NetworkInterface.v1_2_1.NetworkInterface",
 "Description": "Network Interface heth0 for ComputerSystem kjlmo5:Node-R1C1-34U-A",
 "Id": "heth0",
 "Links": {},
 "Name": "kjlmo5:Node-R1C1-34U-A heth0",
 "Oem": {
 "MacAddress": "94:40:c9:b3:3b:40",
 "IpAddresses": [
 {
 "Address": "10.230.79.128",
 "SubNetMask": "255.255.224.0",
 "Type": "IPv4"
 }
 ],
 "NetworkType": "System",
 "InterfaceType": "Ethernet",
 "MTUSize": 9000,
 "SpeedMbps": 100000,
 "Statistics": {
 "BytesReceived": "0",
 "BytesSent": "300",
 "DiscardedReceived": "0",
 "DiscardedSent": "0",
 "ErrorsReceived": "0",
 "ErrorsSent": "0",
 "PacketsReceived": "0",
 "PacketsSent": "5"
 }
 },
 "Status": {
 "State": "up"
 }
 }



Details of the response:

    ▪    Id: The NetworkInterface.Id is set to the name of the interface
    ▪    Oem.MacAddress: the mac address of the interface
    ▪    Oem.IpAddresses: the list of IP addresses of the interface if configured
    ▪    Oem.NetworkType: the network type which this interface is connected to
    ▪    Oem.InterfaceType: type of the interface like Ethernet, InfiniBand
    ▪    Oem.MTUSize: maximum transmission unit of the interface
    ▪    Oem.SpeedMbps: speed of the interface
    ▪    Oem.Statistics: various data, settings, and stats about this interface
    ▪    Status.State: the current operstate value of the interface

Dynamic Fields

    ▪    Oem.MacAddress - may change in card is replaced
    ▪    Oem.IpAddress - may change if a new HSN range is configured
    ▪    Statistics - constantly changes based on network traffic across the interface
    ▪    Status.State - may change based on operstate of the interface



6.3.2 NetworkInterface Representation for a Virtual Interface

As mentioned above, NetworkInterface resources can represent either a physical single interface
or a virtual interface made up of one or more physical underlying members. The response of the
NetworkInterface request which represents a virtual interface contains information about what
type of virtual interface it is (teamd or bonded) as well as various configuration details about that
virtual interface, such as, its underlying physical member(s), what physical member is active vs.
standby, and other configuration details specific to the type of virtual interface it is. The
following example shows a NetworkInterface response which represents a virtual bonded
network interface.




NetworkInterface Resource
- /redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{ComputerSystemId}/NetworkInterfaces/{Netwo
rkInterfaceId}
Each Virtual NetworkInterface available in a ComputerSystem's NetworkInterfaceCollection can
be queried to get Bond or Teaming Mode, state, Active Slave, Link to members , and other
details about the interface.



Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/NetworkInterface.v1_2_0.json

/redfish/v1/StorageSystems/{ComputerSystemId}/NetworkInterfaces/{NetworkInterfaceId}
GET request

A/NetworkInterfaces/ib0 | jq

Details of the response:

    ▪    Id: The NetworkInterface.Id is set to the name of the interface
    ▪    Oem.MacAddress: the mac address of the interface
    ▪    Oem.IpAddresses: the list of IP addresses of the interface if configured
    ▪    Oem.NetworkType: the network type which this interface is connected to
    ▪    Oem.InterfaceType: type of the interface like Bond, Team
    ▪    Oem.MTUSize: maximum transmission unit of the interface
    ▪    Oem.Mode: bonding mode or teaming mode
    ▪    Oem.XmitHashPolicy: transmit hash poilcy of the bonding interface
    ▪    Oem.ActiveSlave: active port/ active slave
    ▪    Oem.Statistics: various data, settings, and stats about this interface
    ▪    Status.State: the current operstate value of the interface

Dynamic Fields

    ▪    Oem.MacAddress - may change in card is replaced
    ▪    Oem.IpAddress - may change if a new HSN range is configured
    ▪    Statistics - constantly changes based on network traffic across the interface
    ▪    Status.State - may change based on operstate of the interface
    ▪    Mode – when user changes bonding mode via cscli lustre_network bonding mode set
    ▪    ActiveSlave – when current active slave/port operational status goes down
    ▪    XmitHashPoilcy – when user changes xmit policy via cscli lustre_network bonding hash




7. ComputerSystem and Top-level service
Resources
Each ComputerSystem resource will provide a link to the collection of top-level
/redfish/v1/Chassis and /redfish/v1/StorageServices resources which belong to or are associated
with it. These top-level resources linked to the computersystem represent the enclosure(s) the
ComputerSystem reside in or are attached to (in the case of EBOD enclosures). The association
can be seen as follow:
7.1 ComputerSystem.Links Chassis Collection
All /redfish/v1/Chassis/{Chassis} resources associated with a particular ComputerSystem can be
seen in the ComputerSystem.Links section:

ComputerSystem.Links Chassis Collection
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/StorageSystems/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-
 36U-A | jq '.Links'
     % Total% Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                       Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 3054 0 3054 0 0 3910                0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 3910
 {
   "Oem": {
    "enclosure_id: 3": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00A",
         "enclosure_id: 4": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/SGFGD2044527F7C",
         "enclosure_id: 5": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/SGFGD2044527EF1"
     }
 }


NOTE: each Chassis resource seen in the ComputerSystem.Links section represents a
/redfish/v1/Chassis service entry point for each enclosure that storage node the ComputerSystem
represents is attached to. The ChassisId will be the same as the StorageServiceId for each
enclosure as seen below

7.2 ComputerSystem.HostedServices.Services StorageService
Collection
All /redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId} resources associated with a particular
ComputerSystem can be seen in the ComputerSystem.HostedStorageServices.Services section:

ComputerSystem.HostedServices.Services StorageService Collection
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/StorageSystems/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-
 36U-A | jq '.HostedServices'
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                     Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed

 {
     "StorageServices": {
       "enclosure_id: 3": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00A",
       "enclosure_id: 4": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/SGFGD2044527F7C",
       "enclosure_id: 5": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/SGFGD2044527EF1"
     }
 }
NOTE: each StorageService resource seen in the ComputerSystem.HostedServices.Services
section represents a /redfish/v1/StorageServices service entry point for each enclosure that
storage node the ComputerSystem represents is attached to. The StorageServiceId will be
the same as the StorageServiceId for each enclosure as seen above.


8. Cluster Chassis
- ChassisCollection Resource /redfish/v1/Chassis

The ChassisCollection resource provides a Collection of OdataId's which represent endpoints of
all Chassis resources that exist in the cluster. Each individual Chassis resource within the
ChassisCollection represents a Storage enclosure in the cluster.

Each Chassis resource, uniquely identified by some Id, will be the service entry point to access
several other resources which may represent components of an enclosure, such as Fans, PSU,
Assemblies, etc.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/ChassisCollection.json



/redfish/v1/Chassis GET request
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/Chassis | jq
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                       Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 672 100 672 0 0 328k              0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 328k
 {
   "@odata.context": "ChassisCollection.ChassisCollection",
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis",
   "@odata.type": "ChassisCollection.v1_0_0.ChassisCollection",
  "Description": "Collection of references to storage Chassis resources.",
  "Members": [
   {
      "enclosure_id: 3": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00A"
   },
   {
        "enclosure_id: 1": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00D"
   },
   {
        "enclosure_id: 2": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00E"
   },
   {
        "enclosure_id: 5": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/SGFGD2044527EF1"
   },
   {
        "enclosure_id: 4": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/SGFGD2044527F7C"
      }
     ],
     "Members@odata.count": 5,
     "Name": "kjlmo12 Storage Chassis Collection"
 }


Details of the response:

      •    Members: Collection of OdataId which represent endpoints of the Chassis resources that
           exist in the cluster
      •    Members@odata.count: the total count of Chassis resources that exist in the cluster
      •    Name: contains the name of the cluster

Dynamic Fields:

      •    Members may add or remove a member from the list if a Storage unit, added or removed
      •    Members OdataId fields may change if an enclosure is replaced
      •    Members@odata.count will change with the Members list

8.1. Enclosure Representation as Chassis resource
- Chassis Resource: /redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}

The Chassis resource is a top-level resource that represents a Storage enclosure. It provides the
service entry point to access several other resources and collections of resources which may
represent components of an enclosure. While there are two top-level resources that represent an
enclosure, Chassis and StorageService, the Chassis resource focusing more on Hardware
components of the enclosure in most cases, including FRUs such as Fans, PSUs, and PAB
(Power Assembly’s).

Schema https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/Chassis.v1_19_0.json:

8.1.1. Collections that are offered by a Chassis resource

      •    /redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}/Power
      •    /redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}/Assembly
      •    /redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}/Thermal

8.1.2. ChassisId

      •    ChassisId is represented by an enclosure serial number
      •    ChassisId is the same as /redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}
           StorageServiceId for an enclosure
/redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId} GET request
 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS009 |
 jq
 {
     "@odata.context": "Chassis.v1_16_0.Chassis",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS009",
     "@odata.type": "Chassis.v1_16_0.Chassis",
     "Assembly": [
      {
               "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS009/Power/PowerSupplies/PSU-1/Assembly/PAB-1"
          },
          {
               "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS009/Power/PowerSupplies/PSU-2/Assembly/PAB-2"
          }
     ],
     "ChassisType": "IPMI",
     "Description": "Storage Chassis MXE30000122VS009",
     "Id": "MXE30000122VS009",
     "Links": {},
     "Location": {
          "PartLocation": {},
          "Placement": {},
          "PostalAddress": {}
     },
     "Manufacturer": "Viking Enterprise Solutions",
     "Model": "VSSEP1EC",
     "Name": "Storage Chassis MXE30000122VS009",
     "Oem": {
      "ServerSlots": [
       {
         "ComputerSystemId": "kjlmo17n:Node-R1C1-30U-A",
         "SlotNumber": "0",
                    "Postition": "left",
                    "ServerPresent": true
               },
               {
                    "ComputerSystemId": "kjlmo17n:Node-R1C1-30U-B",
                    "SlotNumber": "1",
                    "Postition": "right",
                    "ServerPresent": true
               }
        ]
     },
     "Power": [
          {
               "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS009/Power/PowerSupplies/PSU-1"
          },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS009/Power/PowerSupplies/PSU-2"
         }
     ],
     "Status": {},
     "Thermal": [
        {
           "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS009/Thermal/Fans/Cooling-1"
        },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS009/Thermal/Fans/Cooling-2"
         },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS009/Thermal/Fans/Cooling-3"
         },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS009/Thermal/Fans/Cooling-4"
         },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS009/Thermal/Fans/Cooling-5"
         },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS009/Thermal/Fans/Cooling-6"
         }
     ]
 }



Details of the response:

          ▪      Assembly: contains collection of OdataId's to access AssemblyData resources which
                 represent PAB (Power Assembly Units) in the enclosure
                     ▪ not all Chassis have Power Assembly FRUs, this Assembly Collection is only
                          seen those that do
                     ▪ For Chassis that do have Power Assembly FRUs, there should be a 1 to 1
                          mapping of each AssemblyData resource to its associated PowerSupply resource
          ▪      ChassisType: This is the type of Chassis the resource represents, can either be: IPMI,
                 SES, or redfish depending on the supported backend monitoring/management interface of
                 the platform
          ▪      Id: This is the enclosure serial number, and must match the ChassisId in the OdataId
                 field: /redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}
          ▪      Manufacturer: the hardware manufacturer of the Storage enclosure the Chassis resource
                 represents
          ▪      Model: the VPD string of the Storage enclosure the Chassis resource represents
          ▪      Oem.ServerSlots: If the platform supports physical enclosure server slot detection
                 sensors, this section will show:
                 ▪  SeverSlot.ComputerSystemId: the Id of the ComputerSystem resource which
                    resides in this enclosure server slot
                 ▪ ServerSlot.SlotNumber: the enumerated slot number in the enclosure
                 ▪ ServerSlot.Position: the physical position of the server slot (left/right or
                    top/bottom depending on the platform)
                 ▪ ServerSlot.ServerPresent: whether the server presence sensor detects physical
                    presence of the server in this slot
      ▪      Power: contains collection of OdataId's to access PowerSupply resources which
             represent PSU (Power Supply Units) in the enclosure
                 ▪ if the Chassis resource contains Assembly FRUs, there should be a 1 to 1
                    mapping of each PowerSupply resource to its associated AssemblyData resource
      ▪      Thermal: contains collection of OdataId's to access Fan resources which represent
             Cooling units in the enclosure

Dynamic Fields:

      ▪      Id - may change if enclosure is replaced
      ▪      Oem.ServerSlots may change as servers are removed or replaced

8.2. The Assembly Resource
/redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}/Assembly

The Assembly resource provides access to the Assemblies list for a Chassis resource which will
contain the individual AssemblyData resources for that Chassis. This represents a set of Power
Assembly Units (PABs) that exist in the Storage enclosure the Chassis represents. If that Storage
enclosure does not contain PAB units as FRUs, then a 404 response will be returned indicating
there are no AssemblyData units for this Chassis.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/Assembly.v1_3_0.json

Example GET request on Chassis that does have AssemblyData resources:

/redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}/Assembly GET request
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00A/Assembly |
 jq
  % Total   % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                       Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 1044 100 1044 0 0 339k             0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 339k
 {
   "@odata.context": "Assembly.Assembly",
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00A/Assembly",
  "@odata.type": "Assembly.v1_3_0.Assembly",
  "Assemblies": [
      {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00A/Power/PowerSupplies/PSU-1/Assembly/PAB-1",
           "Actions": {},
           "Location": {
            "PartLocation": {},
            "Placement": {},
            "PostalAddress": {}
           },
           "MemberId": "1",
           "Model": "00",
           "Name": "PAB-1",
           "PartNumber": "ASM-02904-01-A",
           "Producer": "VikingEnterpriseSolutions",
           "SerialNumber": "MXE3000011TVU098",
           "Status": {
              "State": "Ok"
           },
           "Vendor": "VikingEnterpriseSolutions",
           "Version": "00"
      },
      {
           "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00A/Power/PowerSupplies/PSU-2/Assembly/PAB-2",
           "Actions": {},
           "Location": {
              "PartLocation": {},
              "Placement": {},
              "PostalAddress": {}
           },
           "MemberId": "2",
           "Name": "PAB-2",
           "Status": {
             "State": "Not Installed"
           }
      }
     ],
     "Assemblies@odata.count": 2,
     "Id": "MXE30000122VS00A",
     "Name": "Assembly"
 }


Details of the response:

       •       Assemblies: the list of all AssemblyData resources that exist for this Chassis
                  o Note: by schema definition, this list contains populated AssemblyData resources,
                     not just OdataId's
       •       Each AssemblyData in Assemblies list
                  o Note: not all Assemblies in all enclosures can read the same FRU data, each field
                     varies by enclosure if it exists or not.
                  o MemberId: the FRU index of the AssemblyData unit
               o Model: the HW model of the AssemblyData unit
               o Name: the name of the AssemblyData unit
                     ▪ combination of FRU type and FRU index
              o PartNumber: the HW part number of the AssemblyData unit
              o Producer: the HW manufacturer of this AssemblyData
              o SerialNumber: the HW serial number of the AssemblyData unit
              o Status.State: the over status of the AssemblyData unit
                     ▪ note that for the AssemblyData resource with Status.State of "Not
                        Installed" - the FRU data cannot be read
              o Vendor: the enclosure Vendor that contains this AssemblyData unit
              o Version: the HW revision of this AssemblyData unit
      •    Assemblies@odata.count: total number of Assemblies for that Chassis

Dynamic Fields

      ▪    Assemblies
              ▪ PartNumber, Producer, SerialNumber, Model, Vendor, Version - could all change
                 if a PAB unit is replaced
              ▪ Status.State - could change if status of PAB changes (see section 8.5)




NOTE: GET requests to AssemblyData
/redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}/Power/PowerSupplies/{PowerSupplyId}/Assembly/{Assembly
Data} resources directly may provide more detailed information and statistics for that particular
unit



Example GET request on Chassis that does not have AssemblyData resources:

Example Chassis with no Assembly FRUs
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/Chassis/SGFGD2044527EF1/Assembly | jq
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                     Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 105 100 105 0 0 35000            0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 35000
 {
     "error": {
       "code": "404",
       "message": "No Assembly Units found for ChassisId SGFGD2044527EF1."
     }
 }



Details of the response:

      ▪    A RedfishError response is returned here with 404 response code
   ▪     this is because not Assembly units exist for this enclosure

8.3. The Power Resource
/redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}/Power

The Power resource provides access to the PowerSupplies list for a Chassis resource which will
contain the individual PowerSupply resources for that Chassis. This represents a set of Power
Supply Units (PSUs) that exist in the Storage enclosure the Chassis represents. If that Storage
enclosure this Chassis represents contains AssemblyData resources, each PowerSupply unit will
contain an Assembly list which provides the OdataId of the associated Assembly resource for
that PowerSupply. If the Storage enclosure this Chassis represents does not contain
AssemblyData resources, no Assembly links will be seen in each PowerSupply resource

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/Power.v1_6_3.json

Example GET request on Chassis that does contain AssemblyData resources:

Populated Power Resource
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00A/Power | jq

8.4. Thermal Resource
/redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}/Thermal

The Thermal resource provides access to the Fans list for a Chassis resource which will contain
the individual Fan resources for that Chassis. This represents a set of Fans or Cooling Units that
exist in the Storage enclosure the Chassis represents

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/Thermal.v1_7_0.json
