8.5. Status.State fields
Status.State fields of all individual resources which have them can be mapped to the following
values. Generally, if a resource changes status - and Event will be sent indicating the change.



SES Element Status Table
[root@kjlmo12-oem ~]# mysql -e 'select * from ses_element_status' t0db
+----+---------------+
| id | description |
+----+---------------+
| 2 | Critical   |
| 3 | Non-Critical |
| 7 | Not available |
| 5 | Not Installed |
| 1 | Ok         |
| 6 | Unknown        |
| 4 | Unrecoverable |
| 0 | Unsupported |
+----+---------------+
[root@kjlmo12-oem ~]#


8.6. AssemblyData Resource
/redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}/Power/PowerSupplies/{PowerSupplyId}/Asse
mbly/{AssemblyDataId}

The AssemblyData resource provides access to information on PAB (Power Assembly unit)
FRUs if they exist in the Storage enclosure that the Chassis resource represents. The resource
structure provides data to capture the name and index of the Assembly unit, any hardware data
that is readable from the unit, as well as a Status of the unit which can change, triggering an
Event.

Schema: definition for the AssemblyData schema is seen within the Assembly schema
here: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/Assembly.v1_3_0.json

AssemblyDataId: the Id for this resource is generated from the following:

       ▪    FRU type
       ▪    FRU index
       ▪    Example: FRU type = PAB, FRU index = 1 - AssemblyDataId = PAB-1
       ▪    Note that FRU index for associated Assembly and PowerSupply resources is the same



Example GET request of AssemblyData unit with "Ok" status

Populated AssemblyData Resources
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00A/Power/PowerSupplies/PSU-1/Assembly/PAB-1
 | jq
   % Total  % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                       Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 450 100 450 0 0 146k              0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 146k
 {
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00A/Power/PowerSupplies/PSU-1/Assembly/PAB-1",
     "Actions": {},
     "Location": {
        "PartLocation": {},
        "Placement": {},
        "PostalAddress": {}
     },
     "MemberId": "1",
     "Model": "00",
     "Name": "PAB-1",
     "PartNumber": "ASM-02904-01-A",
     "Producer": "VikingEnterpriseSolutions",

     "Status": {
        "State": "Ok"
     },
     "Vendor": "VikingEnterpriseSolutions",
     "Version": "00"
 }



Details of the response:
    ▪    MemberId: the FRU index of the AssemblyData unit
    ▪    Model: the HW model of the AssemblyData unit
    ▪    Name: the name of the AssemblyData unit which matches the AssemblyDataId
    ▪    PartNumber: the HW part number the AssemblyData unit
    ▪    SerialNumber: the serial number of the AssemblyData unit
    ▪    Status.State: the status of the AssemblyData unit
             ▪ See section 8.5 for details
    ▪    Vendor: the manufacturer of the enclosure the AssemblyData unit is contained in
    ▪    Version: the HW revision the AssemblyData unit

Dynamic Fields

    •    PartNumber, Producer, SerialNumber, Model, Vendor, Version - could all change if a
         PAB unit is replaced
    •    Status.State - could change if status of PAB changes (see section 8.5)

8.7. The PowerSupply Resource
/redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}/Power/PowerSupplies/{PowerSupplyId}

The PowerSupply resource provides access to information on PSU (Power Supply unit) FRUs if
they exist in the Storage enclosure that the Chassis resource represents. The resource structure
provides data to capture the name and index of the PSU, any hardware data that is readable from
the unit, Status of the unit which can change, triggering an Event, as well as various sensor data
and other statistics if it is available.

PowerSupplyId: the Id for this resource is generated from the following:

       •   FRU type:
       •   FRU index
       •   Example: FRU type = PSU, FRU index = 1 - PowerSupplyId = PSU-1
       •   Note that FRU index for associated AssemblyData and PowerSupply resources are the
           same

Example GET request of PowerSupply unit with Ok status

Populated PSU resource
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00A/Power/PowerSupplies/PSU-1 | jq
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                      Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 978 100 978 0 0 4770              0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 4770
 {
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00A/Power/PowerSupplies/PSU-1",
   "Actions": {},
   "Assembly": {
    "PAB-1": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00A/Power/PowerSupplies/PSU-1/Assembly/PAB-1"
  },
  "Location": {
     "PartLocation": {},
     "Placement": {},
     "PostalAddress": {}
  },
  "Manufacturer": "3YPOWER",
  "MemberId": "1",
  "Model": "EM-2A01P10",
  "Name": "PSU-1",
  "Oem": {
   "Statistics": {
       "Power Supply 1 fault_sen": "0",
       "Power Supply 1 manufacturer": "Viking Enterprise Solutions",
       "Power Supply 1 mfg_datetime": "2021.02.10 23:37:00",
              "Power Supply 1 overall_health": "ok",
              "Power Supply 1 part_number": "PCA-01119-01-C",
              "Power Supply 1 powerprst": "1",
              "Power Supply 1 product_name": "1600W PSU Assembly",
              "Power Supply 1 prsnt": "1",
              "Power Supply 1 serial_number": "CNE850000CAVE146",

     "PartNumber": "YSEF1600",
     "SerialNumber": "S0A00A3032029000204",
     "Status": {
       "State": "Ok"
     }
 }

Details of the response:

          •      Assembly: Link to the AssemblyData resource associated with this PowerSupply unit
          •      Manufacturer: the HW Manufacturer of the PowerSupply unit
          •      MemberId: the FRU index of the PowerSupply unit
          •      Model: the HW model of the PowerSupply unit
          •      Name: the name of the PowerSupply unit which matches the PowerSupplyId
          •      Oem.Statistics:
                     o These are additional statistics on the PowerSupply unit pulled as available
                     o This includes several sensor readings, and additional health checks and hardware
                         data
                     o Note: this is not available for all FRUs and is based on what is collected by
                         Zabbix Agents on the nodes
          •      PartNumber: the HW part number the PowerSupply unit
          •      SerialNumber: the serial number of the PowerSupply unit
          •      Status.State: the status of the PowerSupply unit
                     o See section 8.5 for details

Dynamic Fields

          •      Manufacturer, Model, PartNumber, SerialNumber - could all change if a PSU unit is
                 replaced
          •      Status.State - could change if status of PAB changes (see section 8.5)
          •      Oem.Statistics - could change based on the value of PSU sensors, etc.

8.8. The Fan Resource
/redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}/Thermal/Fans/{FanId}

The Fan resource provides access to information on Fan or Cooling unit FRUs if they exist in the
Storage enclosure that the Chassis resource represents. The resource structure provides data to
capture the name and index of the Fan, any hardware data that is readable from the unit, Status of
the unit which can change, triggering an Event, as well as various sensor data and other statistics
if it is available.

FanId: the Id for this resource is generated from the following:

       •    FRU type:
       •    FRU index
      •    Example: FRU type = Cooling, FRU index = 1 - FanId = Cooling-1

Note that most Fans have no readable FRU data such as:

      ▪    SerialNumber
      ▪    PartNumber
      ▪    Manufacturer
      ▪    Model

Example GET request for Fan unit with Ok Status

Populated Fan Resource
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00A/Thermal/Fans/Cooling-1 | jq
     % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                       Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 562 100 562 0 0 2768              0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 2768
 {
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/MXE30000122VS00A/Thermal/Fans/Cooling-1",
   "Actions": {},
     "FanName": "Cooling-1",
     "HotPluggable": true,
     "Location": {
      "PartLocation": {},
      "Placement": {},
      "PostalAddress": {}
     },
     "Manufacturer": "N/A",
     "MemberId": "1",
     "Model": "N/A",
     "Name": "Cooling-1",
     "Oem": {
      "Statistics": {
       "Cooling 1 fan_prsnt": "1",
       "Cooling 1 fan_tach": "9900",
       "Cooling 1 overall_health": "ok",
       "Cooling 1 part_number": "102192600"
      }
     },
     "PartNumber": "N/A",
     "SerialNumber": "N/A",
     "Status": {
        "State": "Ok"
     }
 }

Details of the response:
   •    Manufacturer: "N/A" is set because it is not readable
   •    MemberId: the FRU index of the Fan unit
   •    Model: "N/A" is set because it is not readable
   •    Name: the name of the Fan unit which matches the FanId
   •    Oem.Statistics:
            o These are additional statistics on the Fan unit pulled as available
            o This includes several sensor readings, and additional health checks and hardware
                data
            o Note: this is not available for all FRUs and is based on what is collected by
                Zabbix Agents on the nodes
   •    PartNumber: "N/A" is set because it is not readable
   •    SerialNumber: "N/A" is set because it is not readable
   •    Status.State: the status of the Fan unit
            o See section 8.5 for details

Dynamic Fields

   •    Status.State - could change if status of Fan changes (see section 8.5)
   •    Oem.Statistics - could change based on the value of Fan sensors, etc.

9. Cluster StorageServices
StorageServiceCollection Resource /redfish/v1/StorageServices

The StorageServiceCollection resource provides a Collection of OdataId's which represent
endpoints of all StorageService resources that exist in the cluster. Each individual StorageService
resource within the StorageServiceCollection represents a Storage enclosure in the cluster.

Each StorageService resource, uniquely identified by some Id, will be the service entry point to
access several other resources which may represent storage components of an enclosure, such as
StoragePools, Drives, Volumes, FileSystems, etc.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/swordfish/HostedStorageServices.json



/redfish/v1/StorageServices GET request
 [root@kjlmo17-oem rest_api]# curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/StorageServices | jq
   % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                             Dload Upload Total Spent        Left Speed
 100 812 100 812               0   0 264k    0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 264k
 {
     "@odata.context": "StorageServiceCollection.StorageServiceCollection",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices",
     "@odata.type": "StorageServiceCollection.v1_0_0.StorageServiceCollection",
     "Description": "Collection of references StorageService Resources.",
     "Members": [
      {
         "enclosure_id: 3": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00A"
      },
      {
           "enclosure_id: 1": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00D"
      },
      {
           "enclosure_id: 2": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00E"
      },
      {
           "enclosure_id: 5": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/SGFGD2044527EF1"
      },
      {
           "enclosure_id: 4": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/SGFGD2044527F7C"
      },
      {
           "Lustre Filesystem": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/lustre-kjlmo12"
        }
     ],
     "Members@odata.count": 6,
     "Name": "StorageServiceCollection"
 }

Details of the response:

       ▪      Members: Collection of OdataId which represent endpoints of the StorageService
              resources that exist in the cluster
       ▪      Members@odata.count: the total count of StorageService resources that exist in the
              cluster

Dynamic Fields:

       ▪      Members may add or remove a member from the list if a Storage unit is added or
              removed
       ▪      Members StorageServiceId may change for one Member if enclosure is replaced
       ▪      Members@odata.count will change with the Members list
9.1. Enclosure Services
StorageService Resource: /redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}

The StorageService resource is a top-level resource that represents a Storage enclosure. It
provides the service entry point to access several other resources and collections of resources
which may represent storage components of an enclosure. While there are two top-level
resources that represent an enclosure, Chassis and StorageService, the StorageService resource
focuses more on storage specific components of the enclosure, including StoragePools, Drives,
Volumes, and FileSystems.

Collections that are offered by a StorageService are either all or a subset of the following:

    •    /redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/StoragePools
    •    /redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/Volumes
    •    /redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/FileSystems

9.1.1. StorageServiceId:

    •    StorageServiceId is represented by an enclosure serial number
    •    StorageServiceId is the same as /redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId} ChassisId for an
         enclosure

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/swordfish/StorageService.v1_5_0.json

Example StorageService GET request:

/redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId} GET request
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00A | jq
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                       Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 651 100 651 0 0 317k              0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 317k
 {
   "@odata.context": "StorageService.StorageService",
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00A",
   "@odata.type": "StorageService.v1_5_0.StorageService",
  "Description": "Collection of Storage Services provided by enclosure MXE30000122VS00A id 3",
  "FileSystems": {
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00A/FileSystems"
  },
  "Id": "MXE30000122VS00A",
  "Identifier": {},
  "Links": {},
  "Name": "viking-VSSEP1EC",
  "Status": {},
  "StoragePools": {
         "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00A/StoragePools"
     },
     "Volumes": {
         "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00A/Volumes"
     }
 }


Details of the response:

         ▪      FileSystems: Collection of FileSystem resources available to this StorageService
         ▪      Id: Id of this StorageService that is equal to the StorageServiceId in the resource endpoint
         ▪      Name: the name of the StorageService is set to the VPD string of the enclosure it
                represents
         ▪      StoragePools: Collection of StoragePool resources available to this StorageService
         ▪      Volumes: Collection of Volume resources available to this StorageService

Dynamic Fields:

         ▪      Id - may change if enclosure is replaced

9.2. StoragePoolCollection Resource
/redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/StoragePools

The StoragePoolCollection resource provides a representation of "pools" of available storage
provided by a particular StorageService. For our purposes, each individual StorageService will
have just one available StoragePool that provides a path to see all Drive resources available to
the StoragePool, as well as access individual Drives available to the StoragePool

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/swordfish/StoragePoolCollection.json

StoragePoolCollection GET request
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00E/StoragePools | jq
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                      Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 498 100 498             0   0 243k     0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 243k
 {
     "@odata.context": "StoragePoolCollection.StoragePoolCollection",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00E/StoragePools",
     "@odata.type": "StoragePoolCollection.v1_0_0.StoragePoolCollection",
     "Description": "Collection of StoragePools for StorageService MXE30000122VS00E",
     "Members": [
      {
             "enclosure_id 2": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00E/StoragePools/MXE30000122VS00E"
         }
     ],
     "Members@odata.count": 1,
     "Name": "MXE30000122VS00E StoragePool Collection"
 }


Details of the response:

      ▪    Members: this shows the endpoint to the StoragePool resource within the
           StoragePoolCollection
      ▪    Members@odata.count: this shows the total number of StoragePool resources in the
           StoragePoolCollection
      ▪    Name: the StorageServiceId is contained within the name

Dynamic Fields:

      •    Members - StorageServiceId or StoragePoolId may change if enclosure is replaced

9.3. StoragePool Resource
/redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/StoragePools/{StoragePoolId}

The StoragePool resource provides a representation of a "pool" of available storage provided by
a particular StorageService. While StoragePool resources provide several other things beyond
Drives, for our purposes, the StoragePool will provide access to all available Drive resources for
that enclosure in the StoragePools.CapacitySources.ProvidingDrives section. Each
StoragePool provides a path to see all Drive resources available to the StoragePool, as well as
access individual Drives available to the StoragePool.

StoragePoolId:

      ▪    StoragePoolId will be represent again by the enclosure serial number
      ▪    StoragePoolId will be equal to the higher level StorageServiceId

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/swordfish/StoragePool.v1_7_0.json

StoragePool GET request

9.4. StoragePool CapacitySourceCollection Resource
/redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/StoragePools/{StoragePoolId}/
CapacitySources

The StoragePool CapacitySourcesCollection resource will provide a list of CapacitySources
available for a particularStoragePool. For our purposes, each StoragePool will have only 1
CapacitySource. Each CapacitySource provides access to the ProvidingDrives collection which
lists the OdataId's of all Drive resources available to this StoragePool

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/swordfish/CapacitySourceCollection.json

9.5. StoragePool CapacitySource Resource
/redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/StoragePools/{StoragePoolId}/
CapacitySources/{CapacitySourceId}

The CapacitySource resource provides a representation of the CapacitySource of a particular
StoragePool provided by a particular StorageService. While CapacitySource provides many
things, for our purposes, CapacitySource will provide access to ProvidingDrives of a
StoragePool. The ProvidingDrives list will contain OdataId's for each Drive resource available to
the StoragePool

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/swordfish/Capacity.v1_2_0.json

CapacitySourceId:

      •   CapacitySourceId will be represent again by the enclosure serial number
      •   CapacitySourceId will be equal to the higher level StoragePoolId and StorageServiceId

9.6. CapacitySource ProvidingDrives - DriveCollection
Resource

resources available to the StoragePool.

enclosure drive bay or slot each drive is contained in.

9.7. Drive Resource
/redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/StoragePools/{StoragePoolId}/
CapacitySources/{CapacitySourceId}/ProvidingDrives/{DriveId}

Drive resource will represent an actual enclosure drive available to that StoragePool.

DriveId

          ▪    DriveId will be represented by the Drive Serial Number
          ▪    Drive resource will contain information about which enclosure drive bay or slot the drive
               is contained in

ProvidingDrives Drive GET request
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00A/StoragePools/MXE30000122VS00A/Ca
 pacitySources/MXE30000122VS00A/ProvidingDrives/S4YPNE0NC03831 | jq
   % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                      Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 585 100 585 0 0 142k           0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 142k
 {
   "@odata.context": "Drive.Drive",
  "@odata.id":
 "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00A/StoragePools/MXE30000122VS00A/CapacitySources/MXE30000
 122VS00A/ProvidingDrives/S4YPNE0NC03831",
  "@odata.type": "Drive.v1_12_1.Drive",
  "Id": "S4YPNE0NC03831",
  "Links": {},
     "Manufacturer": "SAMSUNG",
     "MediaType": "NVME",
     "Model": "MZWLJ3T8HBLS-00007",
     "Name": "Drive S4YPNE0NC03831 in bay 2",
     "Oem": {},
     "PhysicalLocation": {
          "PartLocation": {},
          "Placement": {},

Details of the response:

          ▪    Id: Id of the Drive which is equal to the DriveId in the resource endpoint. Set to the Drive
               Serial Number
       ▪      Manufacturer: the HW manufacturer of the Drive
       ▪      MediaType: the drive Media type - i.e. SAS, SATA, NVMe, etc.
       ▪      Model: the HW model number of the Drive
       ▪      Name: contains the Serial number of the drive and the Bay which it resides in
       ▪      Protocol: the Drive controller protocol
       ▪      SerialNumber: the Drive serial number
       ▪      Status.State: the current state of the Drive
                  ▪ see section 8.5 for more details on available states
                  ▪ more drive states may be available in the future, but for now treated as a FRU
                      state

Dynamic Fields:

       ▪      Id - may change if Drive is replaced
       ▪      Status.State - may change depending on state of the Drive (see section 8.5)




9.8. VolumeCollection Resource
/redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/Volumes

The VolumeCollection resource provides a representation of available Volume resources
provided by a particular StorageService. Volume resources represent arrays in NEO RFSF API,
and depending on the type of the ComputerSystem resource pair associated with the
StorageService (any non mgmt types), will have an associated FileSystem resource to represent
the lustre target target that is formatted on the array.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/swordfish/VolumeCollection.json

9.9. Volume Resource
/redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/Volumes/{VolumeId}

The Volume resource will be used to represent, and individual Volume provided by a particular
StorageService, in NEO rfsf API, Volumes represent underlying arrays on the system. If the
StorageService represents a particular enclosure, such as an MDU, then the Volume resources
provided by that StorageService will show data about the underlying arrays assembled on the
drives in that enclosure. Each Volume resource (except for StorageService associated with
ComputerSystem resources which represent mgmt nodes) will have an associated FileSystem
resource which represents the lustre target formatted on the array the Volume resource represent.
This relation can be seen in the Links.Oem.FileSystem section of the Volume resource. Each
should have only 1 associated FileSystem (except mgmt StorageServices which have 0).

VolumeId:

          ▪      The VolumeId of each Volume resource will be represented by the Array or Pool name
                 (ZFS) it represents
                    ▪ Ex: /dev/md65
                             ▪ VolumeId: md65
                    ▪ Ex: pool-mds65/mdt65
                             ▪ VolumeId: pool-mds65

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/swordfish/Volume.v1_7_0.json
Example GET request to md65 Volume resource

/redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/Volumes/{VolumeId} GET request
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00E/Volumes/md65 | jq
   % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                      Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 1367 100 1367 0 0 18226             0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 18226
 {
     "OdataContext": "Volume.Volume",
     "OdataId": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00E/Volumes/md65",
     "OdataType": "Volume.v1_6_2.Volume",
     "Description": "Volume resource to represent Array md65",
     "Id": "md65",
     "Links": {
      "Oem": {
        "FileSystem": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00E/FileSystems/kjlmo12-MDT0000"
      }
     },
     "Name": "Volume md65",
     "Oem": {
      "HomeHost": "kjlmo1202",
      "IcingaServices": {
        "Services": [
         {
           "Name": "Arrays and Disk Status",
       "State": "0",
       "Output": "No arrays found, T10PI: Not relevant on this system\\nTotal number of disk slots available:
 24\\nTotal number of disks found: 24\\nslot: 1, wwn: eui.345950304ea046120025384500000004, cap:
 3840755982336, dev: nvme13n1, parts:        0, status: Hot Spare, t10: 11110711121, type: ssd, sect: 4096, reason:
 normal, dwpd: 1\\nslot: 13, wwn: eui.345950304ea045780025384500000004, cap:             3840755982336, dev:
 nvme11n1, parts:     0, status: Hot Spare, t10: 11110711121, type: ssd, sect: 4096, reason: normal, dwpd:
 1\\n\\nMD RAID to Lustre mapping\\n\\n\\n\\n\\nDegraded Array information:\\n\\nAll arrays are in clean state on
 node kjlmo1202"
         }
       ]
     }
  },
     "RAIDType": "RAID10",
     "Status": {
       "State": "ok"
     }
 }

Details of the response:
   ▪    Id: the Id of the resource which is derived from the array name on the system it represents
        and matches VolumeId in the resource endpoint
   ▪    Links.Oem.FileSystem: link to the associated FileSystem resource which represents the
        target formatted on this Volume
   ▪    Oem
             ▪ HomeHost: the host this Volume should start on by default
             ▪ IcingaServices.Services
                    ▪ Shows Name, State and Output of the Icinga2 "Arrays and Disk Status"
                         service to provide information on the state of the Array and underlying
                         Disks
   ▪    RAIDType: the raid type of the array, i.e. RAID10, RAID6, GRIDRAID dRAID2, etc.
   ▪    Status.State: the current state of the array, based on the Icinga2 "Arrays and Disk Status"
        service state

Dynamic Fields:

   ▪    IcingaServices.Services
            ▪ State and Output of Arrays and Disks Status service will change as the state of
                Array and underlying drives change
   ▪    Status.State - will change as the status of the underlying Array changes



Example GET request to md64 Volume in mgmt node StorageService which shows there is no
associated FileSystem resource

   ▪    this IS because for initial delivery, we are only monitoring Lustre FileSystem resources

9.11. FileSystem Resource
/redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}/FileSystems/{FileSystemId}

The FileSystem resource will be used to represent an individual FileSystem provided by a
particular StorageService. If the StorageService represents a particular enclosure, such as an
MDU, then the FileSystem resources provided by that StorageService will show data about the
individual Lustre targets hosted by the node pair that reside in that enclosure. Each FileSystem
resource will have an associated Volume resource which represents the array the lustre target is
formatted on. This relation can be seen in the CapacitySources.ProvidingVolumes section of the
FileSystem resource. Each FileSystem should only have 1 associated ProvidingVolume.

FileSystemId:

      ▪   the FileSystemId of each FileSystem resource will be represented by:
              ▪ <fsname>-<target name>
              ▪ where fsname == lustre filesystem name
              ▪ target name == lustre target name
              ▪ this should match what is actually formatted on-disk for this lustre target, and can
                  be seen with various tools such as blkid, tunefs.lustre
      ▪   The FileSystemId also provides a means of associating each individual Lustre target
          FileSystem resource to the over-arching Lustre FileSystem resource
              ▪ this will be provided by another StorageService that is not enclosure specific.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/swordfish/FileSystem.v1_2_0.json

FileSystem GET request for resource representing MDT0000
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00E/FileSystems/kjlmo12-MDT0000 | jq
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                      Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed

Details of the response:

         ▪      CapacitySources.ProvidingVolumes.Members: will show a link to the underlying
                Volume resource which represents the array which the target is formatted on
         ▪      CapacitySourcesOdataCount: the number of ProvidingVolumes, should only ever be 1
         ▪      Id: Id of the FileSystem resource which is equal to the FileSystemId in the endpoint
         ▪      Oem.State will show the state of the target: Started, Stopped, Unknown
         ▪      Oem.FsType: the top-level FileSystem type, will be set to Lustre always
         ▪      Oem.Lustre will contain several Lustre specific details about the target including:
                    ▪ MGSNids: lustre nids of the MGS servers who can host MDT0000
          ▪   FailoverNids: lustre nids of the HA partner which this target can failover to
          ▪   TargetType: Lustre target type: MDT, MGT, MGTMDT, OST, etc.
          ▪   TargetIndex: Index of the Lustre target for that Target type in the FileSystem
          ▪   TargetName: blkid name of the Lustre target
          ▪   BackFsType: backing filesystem type of the lustre target: ldiskfs or zfs
          ▪   FsName: top-level lustre filesystem name
          ▪   Device: underlying array or pool device which this target is formatted on
              (represented by Volume resource
              in FileSystem.CapacitySources.ProvidingVolumes.Members)
          ▪   Statistics: various Lustre statistics for this target
          ▪   MountDir: the directory which serves as a mountpoint for the target
          ▪   Hostname: the primary HostName where this target should be started
          ▪   HaPeer: the hostname of the HA peer this target could be failed over to
          ▪   MountedHost: the hostname the target is currently mounted on (if it is started)
          ▪   FailedOver: a Boolean that indicates whether a target is failed over
                  ▪ True if started on its HaPeer host
                  ▪ False if started on its primary Hostname host.

Dynamic Fields:

   ▪   Oem
          ▪   FsName: may change if Lustre Filesystem is renamed
          ▪   State: will change as the lustre target is mounted or unmounted
          ▪   Statistics: will change with changes in I/O activity to the lustre target
          ▪   MountedHost: will change depending which host the lustre target gets mounted
              on
          ▪   FailedOver: will change depending if lustre target is mounted on its primary
              HostName or its HaPeer hostname




10. Cluster Managers
ManagerCollection Resource /redfish/v1/Managers
From a Redfish/Swordfish (rfsf) REST API perspective, a NEO based ClusterStor cluster can
also be represented by a ManagerCollection Resource:

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/ManagerCollection.json

This Collection represents a set of Manager resources which represent ClusterStor Storage
nodes, similar to how a storage based ComputerSystem resource represents a ClusterStor Storage
node, but with a few unique purposes (seen below in this section):

   ▪   Manager resources provide representation of highavailability (HA) storage node pairs
           ▪       Manager resources provide paths to highavailability (HA) resource groups represented as
                   Redundancy resources
           ▪       Manager resources provide Actions to operate on Redundancy resources
           ▪       Manager resources provide Actions to remotely get and operate on storage node power
                   state

Each Manager resource within the ManagerCollection resource must have a unique Id. Each
Manager resource within the ManagerCollection resource will have an Id that matches some
associated ComputerSystem resource in the StorageSystemCollection resource, as they represent
the same underlying ClusterStor storage node.

Populated ManagerCollection resource to represent a Cluster:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers | jq
 {
     "@odata.context": "/redfish/v1/$metadata#ManagerCollection.ManagerCollection",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers",
     "@odata.type": "#ManagerCollection.ManagerCollection",
     "Members": [
      {
               "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-40U-A"
          },
          {
               "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-40U-B"
          },
          {
               "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-38U-A"
          },
          {
               "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-38U-B"
          },
          {
               "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A"
          },
          {
               "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B"
          }
     ],
     "Members@odata.count": 6,
     "Name": "HA Managers"
 }


 Details of the response:

               ▪    @odata.id: the URI endpoint of the resource
               ▪    @odata.type: ManagerCollection type reference
     ▪   Members: Collection of Manager resource odata.id endpoints based on the Manager
         resources that exists in the cluster
     ▪   Members@odata.count: the total count of Manager resources that exist in the cluster
     ▪   Name: name of the ManagerCollection resource (indicative of the highavailability HA
         representation)

 Dynamic fields:

     ▪   Members may add or remove a member from the list if the Storage node is replaced,
         added, or removed
     ▪   Members@odata.count will change with the list


10.1 Storage Node Manager
Manager Resource:
/redfish/v1/Manager/{ManagerId}

From a Redfish/Swordfish (rfsf) REST API perspective, a ClusterStor storage node as part of a
highly available (HA) pair, will be represented as a Manager resource. The ClusterStor RFSF
API implementation has extended the Manager resource schema to represent one node in an HA
pair, so that it can manage underlying Redundancy resources, which represent HA resource
groups (see Redundancy resource section below).

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/Manager.v1_19_1.json

Each resource captures Oem information about the node it represents, as well as its HA partner
node. Each resource also provides a Redundancy list of Redundancy resources it manages, as
well as a list of Action request endpoints which go through this Manager.

Example GET request to a Manager resource:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
 https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A | jq
 {
   "@odata.context": "Manager.Manager",
  "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A",
  "@odata.type": "Manager.v1_12_0.Manager",
  "Actions": {

Details of the response:

          ▪   @odata.id: the URI endpoint of the resource
          ▪   @odata.type: Manager type reference
          ▪   Actions: list of Manager Action request endpoints available (see Manager Actions
              request section below)
          ▪   FirmwareVersion: the BMC firmware version of the underlying storage node’s BMC
          ▪   Id: unique resource Id
          ▪   ManagerType: set to Oem ManagerType “HA” to indicate it represents a node in a
              highly available node pair
          ▪   Manufacturer: Manufacturer of underlying storage node
          ▪   Model: Model of underlying storage node
          ▪   Name: resource name
          ▪   Oem: oem extensions to this resource
          ▪   Oem.IsPrimary: indication whether this storage node is in the primary slot of an
              enclosure or not
          ▪   Oem.Hostname: hostname of the storage node
          ▪   Oem.HostIP: Host IP address and subnet on the LMN network for this storage node
          ▪   Oem.IpmiAddr: primary IPMI address of this storage node
          ▪   Oem.IpmiSecAddr: secondary IPMI address of this storage node
          ▪   Oem.ChassisSerialNumber: Chassis serial number of the enclosure this storage node is
              contained in – used to determine partner node match
          ▪   Oem.PartnerInfo: information about the HA partner of this storage node
   ▪   Oem.PartnerInfo.Hostname: hostname of the HA partner of this storage node
   ▪   Oem.PartnerInfo.HosIP: Host IP address and subnet on the LMN network of the HA
       partner of this storage node
   ▪   Oem.PartnerInfo.Id: resource Id of the Manager resource which represents the HA
       partner of this storage node
   ▪   Oem.PartnerInfo.IpmiAddr: primary IPMI address of the HA partner of this storage
       node
   ▪   Oem.PartnerInfo.IpmiSecAddr: secondary IPMI address of the HA partner of the HA
       partner of this storage node
   ▪   Oem.PartnerInfo.SerialNumber: serial number of the HA partner of this storage node
   ▪   Oem.PartnerInfo.ChassisSerialNumber: Chassis serial number of the enclosure the HA
       partner of this storage node is contained in – used to determine partner node match
   ▪   Oem.NodeRole: list of ClusterStor node roles of this storage node
   ▪   PartNumber: part number of this storage node
   ▪   PowerState: IPMI power state of this storage node
   ▪   Redundancy: List of Redundancy resource endpoints managed by this storage node
   ▪   Redundancy@odata.count: total number of Redundancy resources managed by this
       storage node
   ▪   SerialNumber: serial number of this storage node
   ▪   UUID: universally unique identifier of this storage node

Dynamic fields:

   ▪   FirmwareVersion: subject to change when storage node BMC firmware is flashed
   ▪   Oem.Hostname: subject to change if cluster rename operation is invoked (Same for
       PartnerInfo fields)
   ▪   Oem.HostIP, IpmiAddr, IpmiSecAddr: subject to change if cluster mgmt network is re
       IP’d (same for PartnerInfo fields)
   ▪   Oem.ChassisSerialNumber: subject to change if a Chassis replacement occurs (Same
       for PartnerInfo field)
   ▪   Oem.PartnerInfo.SerialNumber: subject to change if HA partner storage node is
       replaced
   ▪   PartNumber, Manufacturer, Model: subject to change if storage node is replaced
   ▪   PowerState: subject to change as storage node IPMI power state changes
   ▪   Redundancy, Redundancy@odata.count: subject to change as Redundancy resources
       are failed over or failed back (moved) between HA partner storage node, whether this
       happens via Action request (see below) or on the underlying system by HA services
   ▪   SerialNumber: subject to change if storage node is replaced
   ▪   UUID: subject to change if storage node is replaced


10.2 HA Resource Group Representation – Redundancy
Redundancy Resource:
/redfish/v1/Manager/{ManagerId}/Redundancy/{RedundancyId}
 From a Redfish/Swordfish (rfsf) REST API perspective, ClusterStor HA resource groups which
manage both Lustre targets and other management Filesystems and services via underlying HA
services pacemaker and corosync, will be represented as Redundancy resources.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/Redundancy.v1_4_2.json

The ClusterStor RFSF API implementation has extended the Redundancy resource schema in
order to capture information about these underlying HA resource groups, including: status,
primary, secondary and current locations of a resource group, underlying primitive resources
contained within a resource group as well as their status and location, and underlying system
components these HA CRM groups manage, including links to other API resources which
represent these system components in the Redunduncy.RedundancySet field (i.e. Volume and
FileSystem resources). The state of these HA resources groups are constantly being monitored so
that the Redundancy resources, as well as which Manager resource owns them, is constantly up
to date and accurately reflected.

Example GET request to a Redundancy resource currently owned by Manager resource:
kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
 https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group
 | jq
 {
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group",
   "Id": "kjlmo1204_md0-group",
   "MemberId": "",
  "MinNumNeeded": 0,
  "Mode": "",
  "Name": "Redundancy kjlmo1204_md0-group",
  "Oem": {
   "TargetType": "OST",
   "TargetName": "kjlmo12-OST0000",
   "FsName": "kjlmo12",
   "ArrayName": "md0",
   "ResourceGroupName": "kjlmo1204_md0-group",
   "ResourceGroupStatus": "started",
   "PrimaryLocation": "kjlmo1204",
   "SecondaryLocation": "kjlmo1205",
   "Location": "kjlmo1204",
   "FailedOver": false,
   "ResourceGroupAttrs": [
    {
      "Name": "kjlmo1204_md0-wibr",
         "Status": "started",
         "Location": "kjlmo1204",
         "FailedOver": false
    },
              {
                   "Name": "kjlmo1204_md0-jnlr",
                   "Status": "started",
                   "Location": "kjlmo1204",
                   "FailedOver": false
              },
              {
                   "Name": "kjlmo1204_md0-wibs",
                   "Status": "started",
                   "Location": "kjlmo1204",
                   "FailedOver": false
              },
              {
                   "Name": "kjlmo1204_md0-raid",
                   "Status": "started",
                   "Location": "kjlmo1204",
                   "FailedOver": false
              },
              {
                   "Name": "kjlmo1204_md0-fsys",
                   "Status": "started",
                   "Location": "kjlmo1204",
                   "FailedOver": false
              },
              {
                   "Name": "kjlmo1204_md0-stop",
                   "Status": "started",
                   "Location": "kjlmo1204",
                   "FailedOver": false
              }
         ],
         "HaNetworking": {
              "LNetInfo": {}
         },
         "StorageServiceId": "MXE30000122VS00A"
    },
    "RedundancySet": [
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00A/Volumes/md0"
         },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00A/FileSystems/kjlmo12-OST0000"
         }
    ],
    "RedundancySet@odata.count": 2,
    "Status": {}
}
Details of the response

   ▪   @odata.id: the URI endpoint of the resource
   ▪   Id: unique Id of the resource
   ▪   Name: name of the resource
   ▪   Oem: Oem extensions to represent underlying HA resource group
   ▪   Oem.TargetType: the Lustre target type this HA resource group manages
   ▪   Oem.TargetName: the Lustre target name this HA resource manages – NOTE: this will
       match an existing FileSystem resource Id
   ▪   Oem.FsName: the top-level Lustre filesystem name the target this HA resource
       manages is a part of
   ▪   Oem.ArrayName: array or zpool name of the RAID volume this HA resource manages
       – NOTE: this will match an existing Volume resource Id
   ▪   Oem.ResourceGroupName: the actual name of the HA resource group managed by
       corosync/pacemaker
   ▪   Oem.ResourceGroupStatus: the status of the HA resource group (started, stopped)
   ▪   Oem.PrimaryLocation: the primary location this HA resource group should start (if not
       failed over)
   ▪   Oem.SecondaryLocation: the secondary location this HA resource group should start
       (if failedover)
   ▪   Oem.Location: the current location this HA resource group is started, or will start next
       (if currently stopped)
   ▪   Oem.FailedOver: indicates whether this HA resource groups is failed over or not, i.e. if
       Oem.Location != Oem.PrimaryLocation – then Oem.FailedOver: true
   ▪   Oem.ResourceGroupAttrs: collection of underlying HA primitive resources that are
       part of an HA resource group
   ▪   Oem.ResourceGroupAttrs.Name: name of the underlying HA primitive resource
   ▪   Oem.ResourceGroupAttrs.Status: status of the underlying HA primitive resource
       (started, stopped)
   ▪   Oem.ResourceGroupAttrs.ErrorMessage: contains any failed action or error
       information surrounding the underlying HA primitive resource
   ▪   Oem.ResourceGroupAttrs.Location: current location of the underlying HA primitive
       resource
   ▪   Oem.ResourceGroupAttrs.FailedOver: set to true if the Location of the underlying HA
       primitive resource != the HA resource group’s PrimaryLocation
   ▪   Oem.StorageServiceId: The Id of the StorageService resource which represents the
       enclosure the two Manager resources are contained in
   ▪   RedundancySet: resource URI endpoints that represent underlying components this HA
       resource group manages, i.e. Volume and FileSystem resources
   ▪   RedundancySet@odata.count: number of resources in the RedundancySet



Dynamic Fields:
   ▪   ResourceGroupStatus: subject to change as underlying HA resource group is
       started/stopped (Same for ResourceGroupAttrs field for underlying HA primitive
       resources in the group)
   ▪   Location: subject to change as underlying HA resource group is failed over or failed
       back (Same for ResourceGroupAttrs field for underlying HA primitive resources in the
       group)
   ▪   FailedOver: subject to change as underlying HA resource group is failed over or failed
       back (Same for ResourceGroupAttrs field for underlying HA primitive resources in the
       group)

Redundancy resource monitoring behavior:

Because Redundancy resources represent underlying HA resource groups on the system, we
must monitor these HA resource groups in case the HA services that manage them are
instructed to start, stop, or move these resource groups from one host to the another in within
the HA pair. The status and location of these groups may change due to administrative actions
either through the API or other ClusterStor interfaces, or by failover of resources when a node
encounters a problem that prevents it from hosting the resources in the group any longer, also
known as “fencing and stonith” in the pacemaker/corosync world:
https://clusterlabs.org/pacemaker/doc/crm_fencing.html . Additionally, we must capture any
failed action errors in the Oem.ResourceGroupAttrs.ErrorMessage field when a fencing or
stonith occurs.

In order to most accurately reflect the status and location of the underlying HA resource
groups, the ClusterStor RFSF API implements a monitoring thread which will periodically
inventory the state of all HA resource groups, and update each associated Redundancy
resource, as well as the owning Manager resources, via PUT or PATCH requests between
storage nodes in the HA pair as these HA resource groups change status or location.

If a Redundancy resource moves location from one host to another in the HA pair, the
associated Manager.Redundancy lists will be updated to reflect which Manager resource
currently owns that Redundancy resource. An example of this can be seen in below section
explaining the Mangaer.MoveFilesystem action request, but this can also occur as part of the
period monitoring interval. If resources move locations, or change status, an Event will be
broadcasted indicating what happened.




10.3 Manager Action Requests Which Operate on
Redundancy Resources
As previously mentioned, Redundancy resources represent HA resource groups that manage
Lustre targets and their underlying components on the system. These HA resource groups can
be instructed to start, stop, or move from one host in an HA pair to another via the underlying
pacemaker and corosync HA services. ClusterStor RFSF API implements a RESTful interface
to instruct these HA resources groups to start, stop or move locations via the following OEM
extension Manager Action requests:

   ▪   /redfish/v1/Managers/{ManagerId}/Actions/Manager.StartFilesystem
   ▪   /redfish/v1/Managers/{ManagerId}/Actions/Manager.StopFilesystem
   ▪   /redfish/v1/Managers/{ManagerId}/Actions/Manager.MoveFilesystem

By definition of an action request, each of these requests are a POST request. Each of these
Action requests can operate on one or more Redundancy resource, specified by details past
request body. While the Action is being carried out on the system under the hood, any
subsequent GET request to the Redundancy endpoint being operated on will return a Task
resource with details on the status of the underlying operation. More details about redfish
Tasks can be seen in the redfish spec.

Task Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/Task.v1_7_4.json

Additionally, an Event for each Redundancy resource operated on will be broadcasted to
subscribers upon success or failure of the request.

See details below on each of the mentioned requests, including:

   ▪   Request body requirements
   ▪   Manager ownership requirements
   ▪   Current Status and Location requirements for Redundancy resources being operated on
   ▪   Task handling while operation is in progress
   ▪   Events broadcasted for failure and success
   ▪   Redundancy Status and Location change upon success
   ▪   Manager Redundancy list updates (for Redundancy groups being moved)



10.3.1 Manager.StartFilesystem Action Request

/redfish/v1/Manager/{ManagerId}/Actions/Manager.StartFilesystem

The Manager.StartFilesystem Action POST request is used to start a specified set of
Redundancy resources in the request body. This request will instruct the corosync and
pacemaker services to start the target HA resource group that each Redundancy resource
represents.

Request Body:

The Manager.StartFilesystem POST request requires that you pass a set of Redundancy
resource endpoint(s) to operate on. At least one Redundancy resource endpoint is required, but
multiple can be passed to a single request.
Example of a Manager.StartFilesystem request to start three Redundancy resources which
represent Lustre OST targets owned by a Manager resource of a given host:

 {
     "Redundancy": [
      {
         "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group"
      },
      {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md2-group"
         },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md4-group"
         }
     ]
 }


 NOTE: the request body can be derived from the current Redundancy list of the target
 Manager resource:

     # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
     https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A | jq '.Redundancy'
     [
       {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group"
       },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md2-group"
         },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md4-group"
         }
     ]


As noted before, Redundancy Manager Action requests can only operate on Redundancy
resources that a Manager currently owns. For example, if a Manager.StartFilesystem request is
made to a Manager resource which does not own the Redundancy resource(s) passed in the
request body, the following error will be seen:

 # cat start_md0_2_4_group.json | jq
 {
   "Redundancy": [
    {
      "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group"
         },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md2-group"
          },
          {
               "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md4-group"
          }
     ]
 }


 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
 https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B | jq '.Redundancy'
 [
     {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md1-group"
     },
     {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md3-group"
     },
     {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md5-group"
     }
 ]
 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" -d @start_md0_2_4_group.json
 https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B/Actions/Manager.StartFilesystem | jq
 {
   "error": {
    "code": "400",
    "message": "Unable to forward request to host kjlmo1205. Received invalid response code 400 from request
 to endpoint: /redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B/Actions/Manager.StartFilesystem. Failed to find
 Redundancy resource by Id kjlmo1204_md0-group. rpc error: code = NotFound desc = Redundancy Resource
 kjlmo1204_md0-group is not found in Manager kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B Redundancy list {\n\t\"error\":
 {\n\t\t\"code\": \"400\",\n\t\t\"message\": \"Failed to find Redundancy resource by Id kjlmo1204_md0-group.
 rpc error: code = NotFound desc = Redundancy Resource kjlmo1204_md0-group is not found in Manager
 kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B Redundancy list\"\n\t}\n}"
     }
 }


 Because Manager resource kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B did not currently own redundancy
 resources kjlmo1204_md0-group, kjlmo1204_md2-group, kjlmo1204_md4-group – the
 Manager.StartFilesystem request cannot be handled by kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B, so a
 error response indicating so is returned.



Example of a successful Manager.StartFilesystem request to Manager kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-
36U-A which owns the Redundancy resources passed in request body:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
 https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A | jq '.Redundancy'
[
    {
         "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group"
    },
    {
         "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md2-group"
    },
    {
         "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md4-group"
  }
]
# cat start_md0_2_4_group.json | jq
{
  "Redundancy": [

              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group"

# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" -d @start_md0_2_4_group.json
https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Actions/Manager.StartFilesystem | jq
{

  "Description": "This Task Resource defines start Manager.Action: /redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-

    "EndTime": "0001-01-01T00:00:00Z",

    "Messages": [

        "MessageArgs": [
               "kjlmo1204_md4-group"

    "StartTime": "2024-08-09T11:57:12.159797517-06:00",
    "TaskState": "New"
}
When a request is accepted, it begins concurrent redfish Task operations for each of the 3
specified Redundancy groups. NOTE: because more than one Redundancy resource was
specified in the request body, the Task resource of the last Redundancy Task created is
returned as a response. NOTE: All Task resources are created with a TaskState of “New”.

When GET requests are run to each Redundancy resource being operated on while the
underlying operation is still being carried out, a Task resource is returned to indicate the
operation is still in progress:

NOTE: the TaskState has been updated from “New” to “Running” for all Task resources
involved.

completed successfully:

An Event is an indication that a Task has completed for the associated resource. Upon
successful completion of that Task, the Task resource will be automatically removed and
the next GET request to the associated Redundancy resource will return the Redundancy
resource as expected.

Once the Task completes for each Redundancy resource, the state of the HA resources
groups should be accurately reflected in each Redundancy resource GET request to
indicate that they have been started, as well as the location they are started in, if they are
failed over, etc.:

     "StorageServiceId": "MXE30000122VS00A"
    },
    "RedundancySet": [
     {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00A/Volumes/md4"
     },
     {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/MXE30000122VS00A/FileSystems/kjlmo12-OST0002"
     }
    ],
    "RedundancySet@odata.count": 2,
    "Status": {}
}


If a Manager.StartFilesystem request is sent for a Redundancy resource which is
already started, the request will be initially accepted and return a Task resource with
TaskState of new as expected:
# cat start_md0_group.json | jq
{
  "Redundancy": [
     {
      "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-
group"
    }
  ]
}
# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-
A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group | jq '.Oem.ResourceGroupStatus'
"started"
# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" -d @start_md0_group.json
https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-
A/Actions/Manager.StartFilesystem | jq
{
  "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group",
  "@odata.type": "#Task.v1_5_0.Task",
  "Description": "This Task Resource defines start Manager.Action: /redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-
R1C1-36U-A/Actions/Manager.StartFilesystem on RedundancyId kjlmo1204_md0-group.",
 "EndTime": "0001-01-01T00:00:00Z",
 "Id": "start-kjlmo1204_md0-group",
 "Messages": [
   {
     "MessageArgs": [
         "kjlmo1204_md0-group"
      ],
      "MessageId": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Actions/Manager.StartFilesystem
Started"
    }
 ],
    "Name": "start Redundancy kjlmo1204_md0-group",
    "Payload": {},
    "StartTime": "2024-08-09T12:33:04.749543936-06:00",
    "TaskState": "New"
}


However, the Redundancy resource passed will be checked to see the current state of
the underlying HA resource group and notice that it is already started, causing the
next GET request to that Redundancy resource to return the Task resource, but with a
TaskState of “Exception” indicating the operation failed, with a message as to why it
failed:

    # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
    https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-
    A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group | jq
{
 "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-
group",
 "@odata.type": "#Task.v1_5_0.Task",
 "Description": "This Task Resource defines start Manager.Action:

RedundancyId kjlmo1204_md0-group.",
 "EndTime": "0001-01-01T00:00:00Z",
 "Id": "start-kjlmo1204_md0-group",
    "Messages": [
     {
       "MessageArgs": [
          "kjlmo1204_md0-group"
       ],
       "MessageId": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-
A/Actions/Manager.StartFilesystem Started"
  },
  {
     "MessageArgs": [
      "kjlmo1204_md0-group"
     ],
     "MessageId": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-
A/Actions/Manager.StartFilesystem Running"
  },
  {
     "MessageArgs": [
              "kjlmo1204_md0-group",
              "CRM group kjlmo1204_md0-group is already started"
             ],
             "MessageId": "Manager.StartFilesystem Failure"
         }
    ],
    "Name": "start Redundancy kjlmo1204_md0-group",
    "Payload": {},
    "StartTime": "2024-08-09T12:33:04.749543936-06:00",
    "TaskState": "Exception"
}


As seen above, this Task failed because the underlying HA resource group was
already started. Similarly, an Event will be broadcasted indicating this Task has
failed:

    # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
    https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/Events/714b81c2-a882-4cad-96b0-60b345970cd9 | jq
    {
         "@odata.context": "/redfish/v1/$metadata/#Event.Event",
         "@odata.type": "#Event.v1_5_0.Event",
          "Context": "ha-ec",
          "Events": [
           {
                   "Actions": {},
                   "EventId": "714b81c2-a882-4cad-96b0-60b345970cd9",
                   "EventTimestamp": "2024-08-09T12:33:05-06:00",
                   "EventType": "",
                   "MemberId": "0",
                   "MessageArgs": [
                    "kjlmo1204_md0-group",
                    "CRM group kjlmo1204_md0-group is already started"
                   ],
                   "MessageId": "Manager.StartFilesystem Failure"
               }
          ],
          "Events@odata.count": 1,
          "Id": "714b81c2-a882-4cad-96b0-60b345970cd9",
          "Name": "HA Reundancy Event"
      }


      Task failures can also occur if the underlying operation being carried out fails
      along the way for any other reason, and similarly, a GET request to the
      Redundancy resource will return a Task with TaskState Exception and a
      message indicating what failed, and an Event will be broadcasted with a
      message indicating what failed.

      After the Redundancy GET request for a failed operation returns the Task with
      TaskState Exception one time, the failed Task resource will be automatically
      removed and the next GET request will return that Redundancy resource again.




10.3.2 Manager.StopFilesystem Action Request

/redfish/v1/Manager/{ManagerId}/Actions/Manager.StopFilesystem

The Manager.StopFilesystem Action POST request is used to stop a specified set of
Redundancy resources in the request body. This request will instruct the corosync and
pacemaker services to stop the target HA resource group that each Redundancy resource
represents.

Request Body:
Similar to the Manager.StartFileSystem request, the Manager.StopFilesystem POST request
requires that you pass a set of Redundancy resource endpoint(s) to operate on. At least one
Redundancy resource endpoint is required, but multiple can be passed to a single request.

Example of a Manager.StopFilesystem request to stop three Redundancy resources which
represent Lustre OST targets owned by a Manager resource of a given host:

 {
     "Redundancy": [
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group"
         },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md2-group"
         },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md4-group"
         }
     ]
 }


 NOTE: the request body can be derived from the current Redundancy list of the target
 Manager resource:

     # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
     https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A | jq '.Redundancy'
     [
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group"
         },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md2-group"
         },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md4-group"
         }
     ]


 As noted before, Redundancy Manager Action requests can only operate on Redundancy
 resources that a Manager currently owns. For example, if a Manager.StopFilesystem request
 is made to a Manager resource which does not own the Redundancy resource(s) passed in
 the request body, the following error will be seen:

 # cat start_md0_2_4_group.json | jq
 {
   "Redundancy": [
    {
      "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group"
        },
        {
             "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md2-group"
        },
        {
             "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md4-group"
        }
    ]
}

# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B | jq '.Redundancy'
[
  {
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md1-group"
  },
  {
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md3-group"
  },
  {
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md5-group"
  }
]
# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" -d @start_md0_2_4_group.json
https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B/Actions/Manager.StopFilesystem | jq
{
  "error": {
     "code": "400",
     "message": "Unable to forward request to host kjlmo1205. Received invalid response code 400 from request
to endpoint: /redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B/Actions/Manager.StopFilesystem. Failed to find
Redundancy resource by Id kjlmo1204_md0-group. rpc error: code = NotFound desc = Redundancy Resource
kjlmo1204_md0-group is not found in Manager kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B Redundancy list {\n\t\"error\":
{\n\t\t\"code\": \"400\",\n\t\t\"message\": \"Failed to find Redundancy resource by Id kjlmo1204_md0-group.
rpc error: code = NotFound desc = Redundancy Resource kjlmo1204_md0-group is not found in Manager
kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B Redundancy list\"\n\t}\n}"
  }
}


Similar to the example above with Manager.StartFilesystem rqeuests, because Manager
resource kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B did not currently own redundancy resources
kjlmo1204_md0-group, kjlmo1204_md2-group, kjlmo1204_md4-group – the
Manager.StopFilesystem request cannot be handled by kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-B, so a
error response indicating so is returned.

Example of a successful Manager.StopFilesystem request to Manager kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-
36U-A which owns the Redundancy resources passed in request body:

# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A | jq '.Redundancy'
[
  {
    "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group"
 },
 {
      "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md2-group"
 },
 {
      "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md4-group"
 }
]
# cat start_md0_2_4_group.json | jq

When a request is accepted, it begins concurrent redfish Task operations for each of the 3
specified Redundancy groups. NOTE: because more than one Redundancy resource was
specified in the request body, the Task resource of the last Redundancy Task created is
returned as a response. NOTE: All Task resources are created with a TaskState of “New”.
When GET requests are run to each Redundancy resource being operated on while the
underlying operation is still being carried out, a Task resource is returned to indicate the
operation is still in progress:

An Event is an indication that a Task has completed for the associated resource. Upon
successful completion of that Task, the Task resource will be automatically removed and the
next GET request to the associated Redundancy resource will return the Redundancy
resource as expected.

Once the Task completes for each Redundancy resource, the state of the HA resources
groups should be accurately reflected in each Redundancy resource GET request to indicate
that they have been started, as well as the location they are started in, if they are failed over,
etc.:

    # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
    https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-
    group | jq

     "Mode": "",

  Similar to a Manager.StartFilesystem request, if a Manager.StopFilesystem request is sent
  for a Redundancy resource which is already stopped, the same behavior will be expected
  in that:

           ▪    The request will be initially accepted and return a Task resource with a TaskState
                of new
           ▪    The Redundancy resource passed will be checked, and it will be determined that
                the current state of the underlying HA resource group is already stopped
           ▪    The next GET request to that Redundancy resource will return a Task resource
                with a TaskSate of “Exception” indicating the operation failed, with a message as
                to why it failed
           ▪    An Event will be broadcasted indicating this Task has failed

  Task failures can also occur if the underlying operation being carried out fails along the
  way for any other reason and similarly, a GET request to the Redundancy resource will
  return a Task with TaskState Exception and a message indicating what failed, and an
  Event will be broadcasted with a message indicating what failed.

  After the Redundancy GET request for a failed operation returns the Task with TaskState
  Exception one time, the failed Task resource will be automatically removed and the next
  GET request will return that Redundancy resource again.



10.3.3 Manager.MoveFilesystem Action Request

/redfish/v1/Manager/{ManagerId}/Actions/Manager.MoveFilesystem

The Manager.StopFilesystem Action POST request is used to move a a specified set of
Redundancy resources in the request body from one Manager resource (which represents a
hostname in an HA pair) to its HA peer Manager resource. This request will instruct the
corosync and pacemaker services to stop HA resource group(s) specified on the current host
they are started on, and start them on the partner host. This effectively accomplishes a failover
or failback of resources depending on if the destination host is the primary or secondary
location for that HA resource group.

Request body:

Similar to both the Manager.StartFilesystem and Manager.StopFilesystem requests, the
Manager.MoveFilesystem POST request requires that you pass a set of Redundancy resource
endpoint(s) to operate on. At least one Redundancy resource endpoint is required, but multiple
can be passed to a single request. Additionally, the Manager.MoveFilesystem POST request
requires that you specify the current hostname (where the Redundancy resources being
operated on currently are started at) and the destination hostname (where the Redundancy
resources being operated on will be moved to) as the following fields:

     ▪       Location – the current location of the Redundancy resource(s)
     ▪       Destination – the destination location of the Redundancy resource(s)

Example of a Manager.MoveFilesystem request body to move 3 Redundancy resource from
Location to Destination:

 {
     "Redundancy": [
      {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group"
      },
      {
           "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md2-group"
      },
      {
           "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md4-group"
      }
     ],
     "Location": "kjlmo1204",
     "Destination": "kjlmo1205"
 }


 Similar to Manager.StartFilesystem and Manager.StopFilesystem requests,
 Manager.MoveFilesystem can only operate on Redundancy resources that a Manager
 currently owns. A similar error will be seen for Manager.MoveFilesystem if a Redundancy
 set is passed that is not in that current Manager.Redundancy list of that Manager.

 There are also some restrictions regarding the Location and Destination specifications in the
 Manager.MoveFilesystem request body. The Location parameter must be set to the
 hostname of the node which the underlying HA resource groups are currently started on, and
ther Destination parameter must be set to the HA peer hostname. This information can be
determined all within the Manager resource:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
 https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A | jq .'Redundancy'
 [
   {
      "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group"
   },
     {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md2-group"
     },
     {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md4-group"
     }
 ]
 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
 https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A | jq .'Oem'
 {
   "IsPrimary": true,
     "Hostname": "kjlmo1204",
     "HostIP": "172.16.2.7/16",

 jlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A Manager is the current owner of kjlmo1204_md0-group,
 kjlmo1204_md2-group, and kjlmo1204_md4-group Redundancy resources which are to
 be operated on by the Manager.MoveFilesystem request.
Additionally, each Redundancy resource can be checked to see its current Status and
Location. Using kjlmo1204_md0-group as an example:

 The above output indicates that kjlmo1204_md0-group is started at Location kjlmo1204,
 which matches that resource group’s PrimaryLocation. Additionally, it shows that its
 SecondaryLocation is kjlmo1205. Since the Redundancy resource is started in its
 PrimaryLocation we can move it to its SecondaryLocation using the parameters:

           ▪       Location: kjlmo1204
           ▪       Destination: kjlmo1205

If the Location or Destination parameters are not defined at all, in that, neither of them are
defined or just one of them is not defined – the request will not be accepted:

 # cat move_md0_2_4_group.json | jq
 {
   "Redundancy": [
    {
       "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group"
    },
          {
               "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md2-group"
          },
          {
               "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md4-group"
          }
     ],
     "Location": "",
     "Destination": "kjlmo1204"
 }
 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" -d @move_md0_2_4_group.json
 https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Actions/Manager.MoveFilesystem |
 jq
 {
   "error": {
   "code": "400",
   "message": "Unable to forward request to host kjlmo1204. Received invalid response code 400 from
 request to endpoint: /redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Actions/Manager.MoveFilesystem.
 Not enough information passed in /redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-
 A/Actions/Manager.MoveFilesystem request body: . Location, Destination and Redundancy fields must all be
 populated. {\n\t\"error\": {\n\t\t\"code\": \"400\",\n\t\t\"message\": \"Not enough information passed in
 /redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Actions/Manager.MoveFilesystem request body: .
 Location, Destination and Redundancy fields must all be populated.\"\n\t}\n}"
  }
 }




Even if the Location and Destination parameters are both populated, there are still some
restrictions on the values specified that will cause the request body to not be accepted. These
are:

      ▪      The Location and Destination are set to the same hostname
      ▪      The Location or Destination are unknown to the targeted Redundancy resources (i.e.
             not a defined Redundancy.Oem.PrimaryLocation or
             Redundancy.Oem.SecondaryLocation)
      ▪      The Destination hostname is the same as the current Redundancy.Oem.Location

If any of these conditions are not met, similar to a Manager.StartFilesystem or
Manager.StopFilesystem Task action failure – initially, the request will be accepted and
return a Task resource with TaskState new. Next, the request body will be checked against
each specified Redundancy resource to validate Location and Destination fields, if the fields
are deemed invalid, a Task error will be raised and an Event indicating the failure will be
broadcasted. For example:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
 https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A | jq .'Oem.Hostname'
 "kjlmo1204"
 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
 https://10.214.128.240:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A | jq
 .'Oem.PartnerInfo.Hostname'
 "kjlmo1205"
 # cat move_md0_2_4_group.json | jq
 {
   "Redundancy": [
    {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md0-group"
     },
     {

     },

Similar to Manager.StartFilesystem and Manager.StopFilesystem requests, Task failures
can also occur if the underlying operation being carried out fails along the way for any
other reason, and similarly, a GET request to the Redundancy resource will return a Task
with TaskState Exception and a message indicating what failed, and an Event will be
broadcasted with a message indicating what failed.

After the Redundancy GET request for a failed operation returns the Task with TaskState
Exception one time, the failed Task resource will be automatically removed and the next
GET request will return that Redundancy resource again.

Example of a successful request to move kjlmo1204_md0-group, kjlmo1204_md2-group,
kjlmo1204_md4-group Redundancy resources from kjlmo1204 to kjlmo1205:

Manager.Redundancy lists before:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"

 [

     },
     {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md2-group"
     },
     {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Redundancy/kjlmo1204_md4-group"
     }
 ]

 Similar to Manager.StartFileSystem and Manager.StopFilesystem, when a request
 is accepted, it begins concurrent redfish Task operations for each of the 3 specified
 Redundancy groups. NOTE: because more than one Redundancy resource was
 specified in the request body, the Task resource of the last Redundancy Task
 created is returned as a response. NOTE: All Task resources are created with a
 TaskState of “New”.
