10.4 Manager Action Requests Which Operate on Storage
Node Power State
The ClusterStor RFSF API provides some oem extension Action endpoints through all Manager
resources which either provide information on, or operate on a underlying cluster node’s power
state. Each endpoint provides a proxy to a cluster node’s BMC through an IPMI interface in
order to provide this information. By definition of an Action route, each of the routes below
provide POST requests only, some of which require a request body depending on the underlying
operation being caried out.

10.4.1 Manager.GetPowerState Action Request

/redfish/v1/Manager/{ManagerId}/Actions/Manager.GetPowerState

The Manager.GetPowerState request will return the current chassis power state of a cluster node.
It requires no request body, as no parameters to the request will change its behavior.
Example Manager.GetPowerState request:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" -X POST
 https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Actions/Manager.GetPowerState | jq
 {
   "Response": "Chassis Power is on"
 }


 Details of the response:

        ▪    Response: this is the chassis power status response from the BMC indicating the
             current power state of the host




10.4.2 Manager.PowerOn Action Request

/redfish/v1/Manager/{ManagerId}/Actions/Manager.PowerOn

The Manager.PowerOn request will send an ipmi chassis power on to the target cluster node
BMC. It requires no request body, as no parameters to the request will change its behavior.

Example Manager.GetPowerState request:

# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" -X POST
https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Actions/Manager.PowerOn | jq
{
  "Response": "Chassis Power Control: Up/On"
}


Details of the response:

    ▪       Response: this is the chassis power on resposne from the BMC. Up/On indicates that the
            host was powered up.



10.4.3 Manager.PowerOff Action Request

/redfish/v1/Manager/{ManagerId}/Actions/Manager.PowerOff

The Manager.PowerOff request will send an ipmi chassis power off, or ipmi chassis power soft
to the target cluster node BMC. It requires you pass a request body which specifies the type of
PowerOff action to invoke: hard or soft.
The PowerOff action type is specified by passing the following in the request body:

 # cat power_action_type.json | jq
 {
     "Type": "<soft|hard>"
 }


 Where Type can either have a value of “soft” or “hard”.

 Soft power off will run an ipmi chassis power soft – which invokes a “clean” or “soft”
 shutdown, allowing the OS to cleanly shutdown before power down.

 Hard power off will run an ipmi chassis power off – which invokes a “hard” shutdown, similar
 to a physical power pull.

 Example of a soft PowerOff request:

     # cat power_action_type.json | jq
     {
       "Type": "soft"
     }
     # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" -X POST -d @power_action_type.json
     https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Actions/Manager.PowerOff | jq
     {
       "Response": "Chassis Power Control: Soft"
     }




 Example of a hard PowerOff request:

     # cat power_action_type.json | jq
     {
       "Type": "hard"
     }
     # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" -X POST -d @power_action_type.json
     https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Actions/Manager.PowerOff | jq
     {
       "Response": "Chassis Power Control: Off"
     }
10.4.4 Manager.Reset Action Request

/redfish/v1/Manager/{ManagerId}/Actions/Manager.Reset

The Manager.Reset request will send an ipmi chassis power cycle, or ipmi chassis power reset to
the target cluster node BMC. It requires you pass a request body which specifies the type of
Reset action to invoke: hard or soft.

The PowerOff action type is specified by passing the following in the request body:

 # cat power_action_type.json | jq
 {
   "Type": "<soft|hard>"
 }


 Where Type can either have a value of “soft” or “hard”.

 Soft reset will run an ipmi chassis power reset – which invokes a “clean” or “soft” reset,
 allowing the OS to cleanly shutdown before power down.

 Hard power off will run an ipmi chassis power cycle – which invokes a “hard” reset, similar to
 a physical power pull and subsequent power restore.

 Example of a soft Reset request:

  # cat power_action_type.json | jq
  {
    "Type": "soft"
  }
  # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" -X POST -d @power_action_type.json
  https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Actions/Manager.Reset | jq
  {
      "Response": "Chassis Power Control: Reset"
  }




 Example of a hard Reset request:

  # cat power_action_type.json | jq
  {
      "Type": "hard"
  }
     # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" -X POST -d @power_action_type.json
     https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/Managers/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-36U-A/Actions/Manager.Reset | jq
     {
         "Response": "Chassis Power Control: Cycle"
     }




11. Top-Level Lustre FileSystem
The top-level Lustre Filesystem will be represented by a FileSystem resource in
Redfish/Swordfish schema in the same way that individual Lustre target (OST/MDT/MGT)
resources are represented, but at a different StorageService level than the individual Lustre
Target FileSystem resources which reside at the "enclosure" StorageService level. We still want
to use the same /redfish/v1/StorageServices service root for the API to access the Lustre
FileSystem data, however, in the URI /redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}, the
StorageServiceId will be represented a bit differently than the enclosure level StorageServices
which are represented by an enclosure serial number.

StorageServices GET request showing enclosure level and Lustre FileSystem level services
 # curl -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/StorageServices/lustre-kjlmo12 | jq
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                     Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 479 100 479 0 0 233k             0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 233k
 {
     "@odata.context": "StorageService.StorageService",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/lustre-kjlmo12",
     "@odata.type": "StorageService.v1_5_0.StorageService",
     "Description": "Storage Service used to access the top level Lustre FileSystem kjlmo12",
     "FileSystems": {
      "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageServices/lustre-kjlmo12/FileSystems"
     },
     "Id": "lustre-kjlmo12",
     "Identifier": {},
     "Links": {},
     "Name": "Lustre FileSystem kjlmo12 StorageServce",
     "Status": {}
 }


Details of the response:

      ▪    notice the "Lustre Filesystem" entry with a StorageService Id in its OdataId that does not
           look like a serial number

Dynamic Fields:

      ▪    Lustre Filesystem OdataId StorageServiceId may change if the Lustre FS is renamed

11.1. Lustre FileSystem StorageService
/redfish/v1/StorageServices/{StorageServiceId}

      •    StorageServiceId will indicate this StorageService provides access to the Lustre
           FileSystem of name "filesystem name"
      •    Format: <filesystem type>-<filesystem name>
      •    Where:
               o filesystem type == lustre
               o filesystem name == name of the lustre filesystem provided by this cluster
      •    Example: /redfish/v1/StorageServices/lustre-kjlmo12
               o filesystem type == lustre
               o filesystem name = kjlmo12

Unlike enclosure level StorageServices which provide access to StoragePools, Volumes and
FileSystems for that enclosure, the Lustre FileSystem StorageService will only provide access to
FileSystems resources.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/swordfish/StorageService.v1_5_0.json

     ],
     "MembersOdataCount": 1,
     "Name": "kjlmo12 Lustre FileSystemCollection"
 }

Details of the response:

      ▪      Only FileSystems collection is available in the Lustre Filesystem StorageService
      ▪      Id: generated to represent the name of the lustre filesystem and equal to the
             StorageServiceId in the resource endpoint

Dynamic Fields:

      •      Id - may change if the Lustre FS is renamed

           ▪ Statistics: will change as I/O to the top-level Lustre FileSystem changes




12. RFSF API EventService and Events
dp-api-server runs an EventService which receives Events from other gRPC services via gRPC
POST requests. These Events are sent in the form of an Event redfish resource which is then
broadcasted to anyone subscribed to receive Events via a POST request to a subscribers
Destination endpoint. Redfish Events are runtime Events, so we will not persistently store all
Events dp-api receives, but rather store all Events received in memory for the runtime of dp-api-
server. It is up to the subscriber to implement a basic service to receive these POST requests on
the endpoint provided in their EventDestination (this will be detailed later). The subscriber can
then choose to do whatever they would like with the Events the receive, whether that be store
them persistently, send email notifications, etc.

The following list provides a comprehensive summary of all conditions or scenarios that can
trigger an Event in ClusterStor runtime operation:

   ▪   Changes in FRU data, status change, or dropout of a PowerSupply resource
   ▪   Changes in FRU data, status change, or dropout of a Assembly resource
   ▪   Changes in FRU data, status change, or dropout of a Fan resource
   ▪   Changes in hardware or firmware data of a Chassis resource
   ▪   Changes in hardware or firmware data of a ComputerSystem resource
   ▪   Changes in FRU data, status change, or dropout of a physical NetworkInterface resource
   ▪   Changes in bonding or teaming config of a virtual NetworkInterface resource
   ▪   Changes in active vs. passive or members of a virtual bonded or teamd NetworkInterface
       resource
   ▪   Triggers thresholds are exceeded for CPU Usage for a ComputerSystem resource
   ▪   Triggers thresholds are exceeded for Memory Usage for a ComputerSystem resource
   ▪   Triggers thresholds are exceeded for Per CPU Load for a ComputerSystem resource
   ▪   Triggers thresholds are exceeded for Swap Usage for a ComputerSystem resource
   ▪   Triggers thresholds are exceeded for Lack of Available Memory for a ComputerSystem
       resource
   ▪   Manager resources are initialized
   ▪   Manager.Redundancy lists have changed between HA peers (indicating HA resources
       have failedover or failed back)
   ▪   An HA CRM group status change is noticed in Redundancy resource
   ▪   An HA CRM group location change is noticed in Redundancy resource
▪   A Manager.StartFilesystem Action request to start a set of Redudnacy resources succeeds
▪   A Manager.StartFilesystem Action request to start a set of Redudnacy resources fails
▪   A Manager.StopFilesystem Action request to stop a set of Redudnacy resources succeeds
▪   A Manager.StopFilesystem Action request to stop a set of Redudnacy resources fals
▪   A Manager.MoveFilesystem Action request to move a set of Redudnacy resources from
    local to partner Manager resource succeeds
▪   A Manager.MoveFilesystem Action request to move a set of Redudnacy resources from
    local to partner Manager resource fails
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with ComputerSystem resource for node status raise an
    alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with ComputerSystem resource for DIMM status raise
    an alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with ComputerSystem resource for Current Load raise
    an alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with ComputerSystem resource for Current Users raise
    an alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with ComputerSystem resource for RAM usage raise an
    alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with ComputerSystem resource for filesystem space
    raise an alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with ComputerSystem resource for Swap Space raise an
    alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with ComputerSystem resource for CPU usage raise an
    alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with ComputerSystem resource for HW profile
    fingerprint failure raise an alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with StoragePools resource for Array status raise an
    alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with StoragePools resource for Disk status raise an alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with StoragePools resource for NVMe speed and
    connection status raise an alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with Assembly resource for PSU Assembly status raise
    an alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with PowerSupply resource for PSU status raise an alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with Fan resource for Fan status raise an alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with Fan resource for Fan statistics raise an alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with Chassis resource for Enclosure Electronics module
    status raise an alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with Chassis resource for Power statistics raise an alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with Chassis resource for Thermal statistics raise an
    alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with Chassis resource for Voltage statistics raise an
    alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with Chassis resource for Current statistics raise an alert
▪   IcingaServices checks associated with Chassis resource for SAS heatlh raise an alert
▪   A new node has been discovered, adding a ComputerSystem resource to the collection
         ▪      A node has been removed, removing a ComputerSystem resource from the collection
         ▪      A node has been replaced, updating a ComputerSystem resource
         ▪      More Events TBD in future releases



Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/Event.v1_7_0.json

Example of a populated Event resource indicating a status change in a Fan in
enclosure SGFGD190843A3A9:

Event resource example
 {
         "@odata.type": "",
         "Events": [
          {
            "Actions": {},
            "EventId": "054b421a-1266-11ed-9413-00093d0693ca",
            "EventTimestamp": "1659446490",
            "EventType": "Alert",
              "MemberId": "",
              "Message": "Status changed for cooling",
              "MessageId": "",
              "Oem": {
               "Hpe": {
                "attribute": "overall_health",
                "enclosure_serial_number": "SGFGD190843A3A9",
                "index": 3,
                "timestamp": 1659446490,
                "type": "cooling"
               },
               "ResourceId": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/SGFGD190843A3A9/Thermal/Fans/Cooling-0"
              },
              "Severity": "Ok"
          }
         ],
         "Id": "054b421a-1266-11ed-9413-00093d0693ca",
         "Name": "Events"
     }

Details of the response:

         ▪      EventId: unique generated Id to identify a particular Event that occurred
         ▪      EventTimestamp: the time an Event occurred
         ▪      Message: message about the Event
         ▪      Oem.Hpe
                   ▪ attribute: the type of status or sensor reading that changed
                ▪ enclosure_serial_number: the enclosure serial number which the resource the
                  Event occurred on resides in
               ▪ index: the FRU index of the resource
               ▪ type: the FRU type of the resource
       ▪   ResourceId: the Resource OdataId of the resource the Event occurred on
       ▪   Id: Equal to the EventId both in the resource and endpoint




12.1. EventService Resource
The EventService resource lives directly under the ServiceRoot /redfish/v1 and can be seen by
issuing a GET request to /redfish/v1/EventService. It will show all available EventType's for
subscribers, as well as all ResourceType's subscribers can receive Events on. It will also show
the endpoint where a list of active Subscriptions can be seen - which will persist through service
restart or failover.

While most of the EventService resource content is immutable, the EventService resource also
provides some controlling parameters: DeliveryRetryAttempts, DeliveryRetryIntervalSeconds,
RequestMaxEventsToQueue, EventDeliveryRetryQueueSize that can be updated or configured
to preferred values via a PUT or PATCH request to the /redfish/v1/EventService endpoint.
Details of what each of these parameters control can be seen below in the “Details of the
response” of the EventService GET request.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/EventService.v1_8_0.json

EventService GET request
 # curl -k -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN" https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/EventService | jq
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                      Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 884 100 884 0 0 11631            0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 11631
 {
     "@odata.context": "EventService.EventService",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService",
     "@odata.type": "EventService.v1_7_1.EventService",
     "DeliveryRetryAttempts": 100,
     "DeliveryRetryIntervalSeconds": 10,
     "Description": "EventService for RFSF API",
     "EventTypesForSubscription": [
        "Alert",
        "StatusChange",
        "MetricReport"
     ],
     "Id": "EventService",
     "Name": "EventService",
     "Oem": {
          "RequestedMaxEventsToQueue": 1000,
          "EventDeliveryRetryQueueSize": 10
     },
     "ResourceTypes": [
      "PowerSupply",
      "AssemblyData",
      "Cooling",
      "Drive",
      "ComputerSystem",
          "Volume",
          "FileSystem"
     ],
     "SMTP": {},
     "SSEFilterPropertiesSupported": {},
     "Status": {},
     "Subscriptions": {
       "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions"
     }
 }



Details of the response:

          ▪    DeliveryRetryAttempts - The number of times that the POST of an event is retried before
               the subscription terminates. This retry occurs at the service level, which means that the
               HTTP POST to the event destination fails with an HTTP `4XX` or `5XX` status code or
               an HTTP timeout occurs this many times before the event destination subscription
               terminates.
          ▪    DeliveryRetryIntervalSeconds - The interval, in seconds, between retry attempts for
               sending any event.
          ▪    EventTypesForSubscription - shows all possible Event types that subscribers could
               receive
          ▪    Oem.RequestedMaxEventsToQueue: the number of Events the API EventService will
               store in memory before rotating them
          ▪    Oem.EventDeliveryRetryQueueSize – The number of incoming Events or MetricReports
               that each EventDestination thread is allowed to queue up while it is retrying to send to an
               EventDestination and the DeliveryRetryAttempts has not been exceeded. If an attempt to
               resend an Event/MetricReport succeeds within the DeliveryRetryAttempts threshold, the
               entirety of the queue will be sent to the client EventDestination to replay the history of
               Events/MetricReports queued up while thread was attempting to retry reaching the client
               EventDestination endpoint.
          ▪    ResourceTypes - shows all possible API resource types that subscribers could receive
               Event's on
          ▪    Subscriptions - shows list of all active Subscriptions

12.1.1 Updating the EventService resource
As mentioned before, while the EventService resource largely provides informational fields that
are immutable, there are four parameters seen within the EventService resource body that
provide a means of configuring the behavior of the running API EventService. Those four
parameters are:

   ▪   DeliveryRetryIntervalSeconds - The interval, in seconds, between retry attempts for
       sending any event.
   ▪   EventTypesForSubscription - shows all possible Event types that subscribers could
       receive
   ▪   Oem.RequestedMaxEventsToQueue: the number of Events the API EventService will
       store in memory before rotating them
   ▪   Oem.EventDeliveryRetryQueueSize: the number of incoming Events/MetricReports a
       thread for a given EventDestination is allowed to queue up while retrying to send a failed
       Event/MetricReport to a given client EventDestination

The API creates the EventService resource with default values for these parameters on startup,
but one may wish to change the values of these based on the needs and size of the system. The
following two mechanisms provide a way to update the EventService to configure these
parameters.

NOTE: ALL other fields of the EventService resource are immutable, if a PUT or PATCH
request attempts to update any values outside of the three configurable parameters mentioned, a
400 BadRequest response will be received with an error.

For more information on what these configurable parameters control, see sections:
    • 11.2.3 – Retiring of EventDestination subscriptions which no longer receive Events
    • 11.3.3 – Rotating of runtime Event history


12.1.1.1 EventService PUT request

One mechanism that can be used to update the existing EventService resource is to send a PUT
request to the /redfish/v1/EventService. By definition, the HTTP PUT request method creates a
new resource, or replaces a representation of the target resource entirely with the request
payload. For the API /redfish/v1/EventService PUT request implementation, it is expected that
the request payload will replace an existing target resource. Because of this, it is required that the
request body contains a fully populated EventService model with updates to the existing
resource.

For example, if there exists an EventService resource with configurable params with the
following values:
    • "DeliveryRetryAttempts": 100
    • "DeliveryRetryIntervalSeconds": 5
    • "RequestedMaxEventsToQueue": 1000
    • "EventDeliveryRetryQueueSize": 10
That needs to be updated to change the configurable params to updated values of:
   • "DeliveryRetryAttempts": 10
   • "DeliveryRetryIntervalSeconds": 10
   • "RequestedMaxEventsToQueue": 5000
   • "EventDeliveryRetryQueueSize": 100


The PUT request payload must contain the entire existing EventService model with changes to
the params within:

Example PUT request body with above changes to configurable params:
 {
     "@odata.context": "EventService.EventService",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService",
     "@odata.type": "EventService.v1_7_1.EventService",
     "DeliveryRetryAttempts": 10,
     "DeliveryRetryIntervalSeconds": 10,
     "Description": "EventService for RFSF API",
     "EventTypesForSubscription": [
         "Alert",
         "StatusChange",
         "MetricReport"
     ],
     "Id": "EventService",
     "Name": "EventService",
     "Oem": {
        "RequestedMaxEventsToQueue": 5000,
        "EventDeliveryRetryQueueSize": 100,
     },
     "ResourceTypes": [
        "PowerSupply",
         "AssemblyData",
         "Cooling",
         "Drive",
         "ComputerSystem",
         "Volume",
         "FileSystem"
     ],
     "SMTP": {},
     "SSEFilterPropertiesSupported": {},
     "Status": {},
     "Subscriptions": {
         "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions"
     }
 }
Example PUT request to /redfish/v1/EventService with the request body shown above:

12.1.1.2 EventService PATCH request

Another mechanism that can be used to update the existing EventService resource is to send a
PATCH request to the /redfish/v1/EventService. By definition, the HTTP PATCH request
method creates partial changes to an existing resource. For the API /redfish/v1/EventService
PATCH request implementation, , it is expected that the request payload will replace some
number of fields in an existing resource, but not the entire resource like PUT does.
For example, if there exists an EventService resource with the following DeliveryRetryAttempts
value:
    • "DeliveryRetryAttempts": 100

That needs to be updated to change the configurable params to updated a value of:
   • "DeliveryRetryAttempts": 10

The PATCH request payload must contain the field key/value pair to be updatedd:

Example PATCH request body to change only the DeliveryRetryAttempts field:
 {
     "DeliveryRetryAttempts": 10
 }



Example PATCH request to /redfish/v1/EventService with the request body shown above:

12.2. Event Subscriptions
To begin receiving Events from dp-api, you must subscribe to receive Events with a POST
request to dp-api to the /redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} endpoint.
The EventDestinationId should be something unique, generated with a tool such as uuidgen. The
POST request body will contain information used by EventService to send Events to the
Destination specified.

Example POST request body to subscribe to receive events to the following
endpoint: http://172.16.0.1:8082/eventreceiver/

Example EventDestination POST request body
 {
         "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/869291a5-5c0e-44c8-92b8-2efa6799c4cb",
         "Id": "869291a5-5c0e-44c8-92b8-2efa6799c4cb",
         "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:8082/eventreceiver/",
         "HttpHeaders": [
          {
              "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
              "OData-Version": "4.0"
            }
         ],
         "Context": "Public",
     }


More details on the request body can be seen here DP-API /EventService but some details to
highlight:

         ▪      the Destination field species the destination address (or hostname), port, and endpoint to
                receive Events from dp-api on
         ▪      HttpHeaders to pass with request should be set to JSON specific headers
         ▪      @odata.id field must match full endpoint request is sent to
         ▪      Id field must match the last field of the @odata.id field

Example POST request to register for events to the following
endpoint: http://172.16.0.1:8082/eventreceiver/.

This will show:
     ▪    before the POST request when there are 0 subscriptions with a GET request
          to /redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions
     ▪    the POST request itself
     ▪    after the POST request showing the new subscription with a GET request
          to /redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions
     ▪    a GET request to /redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} to show
          subscription details

"Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:8082/eventreceiver/"
via a POST which must implement a request handler to receive the Events, more details on this
below.

12.2.1. Event Resource Filtering

Sometimes when subscribing to receive Events from RFSF API EventService, you may want to
create a subscription that is more focused that a general subscription to receive Events of all
types on all resources the API is tracking. This could be for organizational purposes, to send
Events on different ResourceTypes or different sections of the ResourceTree to different
Destination endpoints, or to track a concerning few resources to a particular Destination endpoint
to watch more closely. RFSF API provides two mechanisms to filter Events based on the
Resources you are interested in, based on the following two EventDestination resource attributes
that can be sent in the request body with a subscription request:

          •   ResoureTypes
          •   OriginResources

The following sub-sections will describe what each is and how they can be used. The Redfish
spec, as well as the EventDestination schema mentioned above, provide more details on these
two attributes and how they can be used. It is worth mentioning that these two attributes are not
mutually exclusive, they can be passed alone or together in the request body.

12.2.1.1 Event Resource Filtering Using EventDestination.ResourceTypes

One mechanism provided by Redfish Eventing to filter the Events a client Destination endpoint
may receive is to specify a list of ResourceTypes in the EventDestination request body.
Example:
 {
         "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types",
         "Id": "filter-on-resource-types",
         "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:9084/eventreceiver/",
         "HttpHeaders": [
          {
            "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
            "OData-Version": "4.0"
          }
         ],
         "Context": "Public",
         "ResourceTypes": [
           "Cooling",
           "PowerSupply"
         ]
     }


The above EventDestination specifies that it wants to receive Events on resources of type
ResourceType “Cooling” and “PowerSupply” only. If the Event the resource occurs on being
processed by the API EventService is not of one of the two of these ResourceTypes, that Event
will not be sent to the this Destination. You may specify as many ResourceTypes as are
supported here. To see a full list of available ResourceTypes you may filter on, see the
/redfish/v1/EventService resource, which contains a list of supported ResourceTypes.




12.2.1.2 Event Resource Filtering Using EventDestination.OriginResources

Another mechanism provided by Redfish Eventing to filter the Events a client Destination
endpoint may receive is to specify a list of OriginResources in the EventDestination request
body. OriginResources are defined as a list of Resource URIs. This can be either a URI which
contains a subsection of the ResourceTree, such as a top-level collection, the URI of one specific
resource, or anything in between.

Example:
 {
         "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-origin-resources",
         "Id": "filter-on-origin-resources",
         "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:9082/eventreceiver/",
         "HttpHeaders": [
           {
             "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
                  "OData-Version": "4.0"
             }
         ],
         "Context": "Public",
         "OriginResources": [
            {
                  "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageSerivces"
             },
             {
                  "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageSystems/kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-38U-B"
             },
             {
                  "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis/SGFGD2044527F7C/Power/PowerSupplies/PSU-0"
             }
         ]
     }


 The above EventDestination specifies three different OriginResource filters. The first defines
 that it wants to receive Events on all resources that exist under the StroageServices collection,
 this can be any resource under this collection or sub collections within the structure. The
 second defines that it wants to receive Events on all resources underneath, and including the
 kjlmo12:Node-R1C1-38U-B ComputerSystem resource. The third defines that it wants to
 receive Events on PSU-0 in Chassis SGFGD2044527F7C only. It may not make sense to
 combine this specific set of OriginResources filters, but this example is meant to show that
 you can specify any number of OriginResource filters here. If the Event the resource occurs on
 being processed by the API EventService is not on or within one of these OriginResources,
 that Event will not be sent to the this Destination.



12.2.2 Updating an Event Subscription

Throughout the lifetime of an EventDestination resource, it is possible to update the subscription
parameters to receive Events by altering the EvenDestination resource initially created with a
PUT or PATCH request to an existing
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} resource. The PUT or PATCH
request body should contain the information to update in the existing EventDestination resource,
that results in a change to the resource. If no new information is contained in the request body,
then a 400 “BadRequest” response will be received.


12.2.2.1 Updating an Event Subscription via a PUT request

One mechanism that can be used to update an existing Event subscription, is to send a PUT
request to the associated EventDestination resource at the
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} endpoint. By definition, the HTTP
PUT request method creates a new resource, or replaces a representation of the target resource
entirely with the request payload. For the
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} PUT request implementation, it is
expected that the request payload will replace an existing target resource. Because of this, it is
required that the request body contains a fully populated EventDestination model with updates to
the existing resource.

For example, say you have an existing Event subscription with EventDestination.Id “filter-on-
resource-types”:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-
 on-resource-types | jq
 {
  "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types",
  "@odata.type": "",
  "Context": "Public",
  "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:9084/eventreceiver/",
  "HttpHeaders": [
   {
       "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
       "OData-Version": "4.0"
   }
    ],
    "Id": "filter-on-resource-types",
    "Name": "",
    "ResourceTypes": [
       "Cooling",
       "PowerSupply"
    ],
    "SNMP": {},
    "Status": {},
    "SubscriptionType": ""
}


And would like to update the Event filtering mechanism to use the OriginResources filter, as
well as the Destination that Events are received on to a new endpoint. To update this
subscription with a PUT request, the request body should contain the entire existing
EventDestination model in the payload, with the changes you’d like to apply contained within.

Example PUT request payload:
    {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types",
        "Id": "filter-on-resource-types",
        "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:9099/storagesystems-eventreceiver/",
        "HttpHeaders": [
          {
            "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
            "OData-Version": "4.0"
           }
        ],
        "Context": "Public",
        "OriginResources": [
           {
             "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageSystems"
            }
        ]
    }


    Details of the PUT request payload:
       • The EventDestination.Id is the same as the target resource: “filter-on-resource-types”
       • The EventDestination.@odata.id is the same as the target resource:
            "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types"
       • The Destination endpoint has changed to http://172.16.0.1:9099/storagesystems-
            eventreceiver/
       • The Event filtering mechanism has changed from ResourceTypes to
            OriginResources

    The PUT request when sent, if all requirements are met, will then entirely update and
    replace the target resource.
Example successful PUT request using payload above:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" -d @events/test_subscription_filter_resource_types_put_update.json -
 X PUT https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types | jq
 {
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types",
   "@odata.type": "",
   "Context": "Public",
     "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:9099/storagesystems-eventreceiver/",
     "HttpHeaders": [
      {
        "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
        "OData-Version": "4.0"
      }
     ],
     "Id": "filter-on-resource-types",
     "Name": "",
     "OriginResources": [
        {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageSystems"
      }
     ],
     "SNMP": {},
     "Status": {},
     "SubscriptionType": ""
 }


Now, a GET request to the same filter-on-resource-types EventDestination resource will
reflect the updates taken from the PUT request body:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types | jq
 {
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types",
   "@odata.type": "",
   "Context": "Public",
     "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:9099/storagesystems-eventreceiver/",
     "HttpHeaders": [
        {
          "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
          "OData-Version": "4.0"
        }
     ],
     "Id": "filter-on-resource-types",
     "Name": "",
     "OriginResources": [
           {
               "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageSystems"
           }
       ],
       "SNMP": {},
       "Status": {},
       "SubscriptionType": ""
   }


   As mentioned before, there are a couple requirements in order for a PUT request to
   /redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} to be successful. The main
   ones are:
       • The EventDestination.Id in the request payload must match the
           EventDestinaton.Id of the target resource
       • The request payload must update the target EventDestination resource

   Examples of some “BadRequest” responses received if these conditions are not met:

       # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" -d
       @events/test_subscription_filter_resource_types_put_update.json -X PUT
       https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types | jq
       {
         "error": {
          "code": "400",
          "message": "Requested URI uuid filter-on-resource-types does not match EventDestination.Id filter-on-
       resource-types2 in request body."
           }
       }
       # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" -d
       @events/test_subscription_filter_resource_types_put_update.json -X PUT
       https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types | jq
       {
        "error": {
          "code": "400",
          "message": "Request body does not differ from saved resource:
       /mnt/mgmt/var/lib/xyratex/rfsf_resources//Events/Destinations/filter-on-resource-types.json"
        }
       }




12.2.2.1 Updating an Event Subscription via a PATCH request

Another mechanism that can be used to update an existing Event subscription, is to send a
PATCH request to the associated EventDestination resource at the
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} endpoint. By definition, the HTTP
PATCH request method creates partial changes to an existing resource. For the
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} PATCH request implementation, it
is expected that the request payload will replace some number of fields in an existing resource,
but not the entire resource like PUT does.

For example, say you have an existing Event subscription with EventDestination.Id “filter-on-
resource-types”:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-
 on-resource-types | jq
 {
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types",
     "@odata.type": "",
     "Context": "Public",
     "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:9099/storagesystems-eventreceiver/",
     "HttpHeaders": [
        {
          "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
          "OData-Version": "4.0"
        }
     ],
     "Id": "filter-on-resource-types",
     "Name": "",
     "OriginResources": [
       {
         "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageSystems"
       }
     ],
     "SNMP": {},
     "Status": {},
     "SubscriptionType": ""
 }


 And you’d like to update just a single field, OriginResources, to add another URI endpoint to
 filter on. This can be done by sending a PATCH request to the existing resource endpoint with
 a request payload containing changes to just the OriginResources field:

 Example request payload:

 {
     "OriginResources": [
      {
         "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageSystems"
      },
      {
             "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis"
         }
     ]
}


Details of the PATCH request payload
   • This adds an additional OriginResources filter on /redfish/v1/Chassis to the existing
        OriginResources field
   • This payload updates OriginResources only
Example successful PATCH request using payload above:

    # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" -d @events/test_subscription_filter_resource_types_patch_update.json -
    X PATCH https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types | jq
    {
      "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types",
      "@odata.type": "",
      "Context": "Public",
        "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:9099/storagesystems-eventreceiver/",
        "HttpHeaders": [
         {
           "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
           "OData-Version": "4.0"
         }
        ],
        "Id": "filter-on-resource-types",
        "Name": "",
        "OriginResources": [
           {
             "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageSystems"
         },
         {
              "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis"
         }
        ],
        "SNMP": {},
        "Status": {},
        "SubscriptionType": ""
    }



 Now, a GET request to the same filter-on-resource-types EventDestination resource will
reflect the updates taken from the PATCH request body:

    # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
    https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types | jq
    {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types",
        "@odata.type": "",
        "Context": "Public",
        "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:9099/storagesystems-eventreceiver/",
     "HttpHeaders": [
      {
        "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
           "OData-Version": "4.0"
        }
     ],
     "Id": "filter-on-resource-types",
     "Name": "",
     "OriginResources": [
      {
           "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/StorageSystems"
      },
      {
           "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/Chassis"
      }
     ],
     "SNMP": {},
     "Status": {},
     "SubscriptionType": ""
 }



PATCH requests are a bit more flexible than a PUT request in terms of allowed requests since
it is only a partial update of a resource. The main restriction is as follows:
     • The request payload must update the target EventDestination resource

If the resulting resource is not changed by the PATCH request payload, a “BadResposne” is
received. Example of a “BadRequest” response received when payload does not update the
resource:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" -d @events/test_subscription_filter_resource_types_patch_update.json -
 X PATCH https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/filter-on-resource-types | jq
 {
  "error": {
    "code": "400",
    "message": "Request body does not differ from saved resource:
 /mnt/mgmt/var/lib/xyratex/rfsf_resources//Events/Destinations/filter-on-resource-types.json"
  }
 }




12.2.3 – Retiring of EventDestination subscriptions which no longer receive
Events

As mentioned in section 11.1 – the EventService resource contains the following configurable
values:
    •    DeliveryRetryAttempts - The number of times that the POST of an event is retried
         before the subscription terminates. This retry occurs at the service level, which means
         that the HTTP POST to the event destination fails with an HTTP `4XX` or `5XX`
         status code or an HTTP timeout occurs this many times before the event destination
         subscription terminates.
    •    DeliveryRetryIntervalSeconds - The interval, in seconds, between retry attempts for
         sending any event.

These parameters are global values for all EventDestination subscriptions that define behavior
in the API EventService related to sending Events to subscribers that do not go through. For
example, if an subscription exists where the API cannot reach the target
EventDestination.Destination endpoint, it will be allowed up to, but not more than
DeliveryRetryAttempts number of attempts to resend the Event with a period of
DeliveryRetryIntervalSeconds in between each attempt. If the number of attempts goes over
the DeliveryRetryAttempts configured value, than the API will automically terminate this
description with a DELETE operation for the associated
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} endpoint.



Example logs where this occurs from dp-api service:

 Once this happens, clients will have to re-subscribe via a POST request in order to begin

 12.2.4 – Restricting the Number of Queued Events/MetricReports During
 Delivery Retry
As mentioned in section 11.1 – the EventService contains the following configurable
parameter:

   ▪   Oem.EventDeliveryRetryQueueSize: the number of incoming Events/MetricReports
       a thread for a given EventDestination is allowed to queue up while retrying to send a
       failed Event/MetricReport to a given client EventDestination

This parameter was introduced as an Oem extension the redfish EventService to control the
number of incoming Events/MetricReports that a given thread is allowed to queue up while
it is in a DeliveryRetry loop. If a client EventDestination endpoint stops listening for Event /
MetricReport POST requests from the API EventService, something in the network
topology causes the Destination endpoint to become unreachable, or anything else that may
prevent API EventService from reaching a given client EventDestination occurs, a given
EventDestination thread will enter a “DeliveryRetry” loop. When an EventDestination
thread enters this DeliveryRetry loop, it will attempt to resend a failed Event/MetricReport
at an interval of time in seconds defined by the EventService.DeliveryRetryIntervalSeconds
parameter until either:


   ▪   The client EventDestination becomes reachable again
   ▪   The EventService.DeliveryRetryAttempts threshold is succeed


While a given EventDestination thread is in a DeliveryRetry loop, more Events or
MetricReports may come in. In an effort to maintain history, each EventDestination thread
maintains a queue of incoming Events / MetricReports. If the client EventDestination never
becomes reachable, and many Events or MetricReports start to get queued up, the memory
consumption of each thread can start to grow large, particularly on a large system. In an
effort to control this and reduce the resource consumption of dp-api-server, the
EventService.Oem.EventDeliveryRetryQueueSize can be set accordingly to control the
number of items allowed in each of these queues.

This parameter controls the queue size as follows: as incoming Events / MetricReports are
queued up, if the number of items in a given queue exceeds the
EventDeliveryRetryQueueSize defined, items will be popped off the queue until the queue
size is below this threshold before allowing another item to be placed on the queue. This
means that the number of Events or MetricReports in a given queue will sit right around the
EventDeliveryRetryQueueSize defined until a client EventDestination becomes reachable
again and the queue is unloaded, or the EventServiceDeliveryRetryAttempts threshold is
exceeded, and the subscription is automatically terminated.

The default value of the EventService.Oem.EventDeliveryRetryQueueSize is 10, but this
parameter can be configured via a PUT or PATCH request to /redfish/v1/EventService to fit
the behavior desired for a given system. It is important to consider the size of a system when
configuring this parameter, more nodes in a given cluster means that more Events and
MetricReports can be generated, which can fill up these queues during an DeliveryRetry
  loop quicker and quicker. It is better to maintain a stable resource consumption for dp-api-
  server during these Event DeliveryRetry loops, and determine the root of the problem why a
  given client EventDestination cannot be reached, rather than allow for larger queue sizes to
  try to retain history.




12.3. Runtime Event History
Events in the Redfish spec are intended to be runtime occurrences. Because we realize that
people may want to track history of Events, or recall information of a specific Event, we have
implemented runtime in memory storage of Events to track history. If the subscriber wants to
persistently store Events they receive, they must do so on their Destination host described above.

The following GET requests can be used to track runtime Event history:

12.3.1. EventCollection Resource /redfish/v1/Events

To see the collection of all runtime Events that the API EventService has been tracking, you can
run a GET request to /redfish/v1/Events. It is important to note that this resource collection
is runtime only. If dp-api service is stopped, restarted, or failed over for any reason, the runtime
collection will be lost. It is up to the client running an EventReceiver service that dp-api
EventService broadcasts Events to, to save the Event history persistently if they choose to.
GET /redfish/v1/Events example (output truncated)

      ▪      Members@odata.count: the total number of Events send to dp-api EventService since it

12.3.2. Event resource /redfish/v1/Events/{EventId}

The Event resource is used to capture the details of s single Event. Details of the Event resource
fields will be shown below. Each Event will contain a unique EventId.

EventId:

      ▪      a unique Id that is generated by the monitoring service that sends the Event to dp-api.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/Event.v1_7_0.json

Details of the response:

      ▪             EventTimestamp: the timestamp the Event occurred
      ▪             EventType: the type of Event sent
                       ▪ the supported Event types can be seen in the EventService resource via a GET
                          request to /redfish/v1/EventService

      ▪             Oem.Hpe
                       ▪ attribute: the type of alert received from the backend monitoring service that sent
                          the event
                       ▪ enclosure_serial_number: the enclosure which contains the resource this Event
                          came from
                     ▪  this would map to a specific ChassisId - /redfish/v1/Chassis/{ChassisId}
                        where enclosure_serial_number == ChassisId
             ▪ index: the FRU index of the resource the Event was sent against
                    ▪ this is applicable to Events on FRU type resources only, i.e. Drive, PSU,
                        PAB, Fan
             ▪ type: the FRU type of the resource the Event was sent against
                    ▪ this is applicable to Events on FRU type resources only, i.e. Drive, PSU,
                        PAB, Fan
   ▪    ResourceId: the OdataId of the resource this Event was sent against
             ▪ this is intended to allow clients to quickly parse the Event response body and run
                a GET request to the ResourceId to see the change in data reflected
   ▪    Severity: this reflects the status of the resource the Event occurred on after it occurred
   ▪    Id: the unique Id to identify this Event
             ▪ matches EventId in /redfish/v1/Events/{EventId}
             ▪ generated by the sender

12.3.3 Rotating of runtime Event History

As mentioned in section 10.1 – the EventService resource contains the following configurable
value
    • Oem.RequestedMaxEventsToQueue: the number of Events the API EventService will
      store in memory before rotating them

This parameter defines the number Events that API EventService will retain before rotating them
out. Since all Events in runtime history are stored in memory and not persistenly, by Redfish
spec definition, when Events history gets rotated, Events are then lost. This is an effort to help
prevent the memory foot print of the API from becoming too large.

Events should be stored externally to the cluster if persistent storage is required. The
EventService.Oem.RequestedMaxEventsToQueue parameter can be changed in
/redfish/v1/EventService to an appropriate value for that system via a PATCH or PUT request.

Example logs from dp-api showing runtime Event history being rotated:
 Apr 04 11:46:47 kjlmo1200 dp-api-server[1124914]: INFO[2023-04-04T11:46:47-06:00] In memory EventCollection
 has reached maximum
 length of 1000! Rotating EventCollection...

any other Event. Here is a list of all Icinga2 services which may invoke Events and which
resources the occur on. Please see existing ClusterStor Manager and Monitoring documentation
for more details on each of these Icinga2 services.

NOTE: most all of these services reside in the ComputerSystem resource, as they are all node
specific. We may choose to break them out into other Redfish/Swordfish resources in the future.

12.5. Types of Events
The Redfish specification specifies the types of Events that EventService can receive and
Broadcast as the following (please see the Redfish Specification for more details):

   ▪   StatusChange
      ▪    ResourceUpdated
      ▪    ResourceAdded
      ▪    ResourceRemoved
      ▪    Alert
      ▪    MetricReport
      ▪    Other

For initial delivery, the NEO RFSF API EventService will support 3 types of Events. These are
defined in the EventService resource. To see this, look at the
EventService.EventTypesForSubscription field.

Supported Event Types

12.7. Subscribers Receiving Events
As mentioned above, dp-api only provides the capability for users to subscribe to receive Events,
as well as forward any Events it receives from other API services to all subscriber destinations. It
is then up to the describer to implement a simple service to listen on some port at some endpoint
for POST requests from dp-api. Once the subscriber receives these POST request each time an
Event occurs, they can choose to do whatever they want with these Events - such as:

    ▪     persistently store all Event json somewhere
    ▪     send email notifications about the Event
    ▪     schedule service related to Event
    ▪     whatever

Example simple python service to receive events
on http://172.16.0.1:8082/eventreceiver/ forwarded via POST requests from dp-api as
EventService receives them. This service simply logs information about the request, including
the request body which contains the Event itself.

NOTE: This is not my code, it is a slightly modified example taken
from https://gist.github.com/mdonkers/63e115cc0c79b4f6b8b3a6b797e485c7

Event receiver POST request handler service
 #!/usr/bin/env python3.9
 """
 Very simple HTTP server in python for logging requests
 Usage::
    ./server.py [<port>]
 """
 from http.server import BaseHTTPRequestHandler, HTTPServer
 import logging


 class S(BaseHTTPRequestHandler):
    def _set_response(self):
       self.send_response(200)
       self.send_header('Content-type', 'text/html')
       self.end_headers()


   def do_POST(self):
     content_length = int(self.headers['Content-Length']) # <--- Gets the size of data
     post_data = self.rfile.read(content_length) # <--- Gets the data itself
     logging.info("Received Event:\nDestination: %s\nHeaders:\n%s\n\nBody:\n%s\n",
          str(self.path), str(self.headers), post_data.decode('utf-8'))


        self._set_response()
        self.wfile.write("POST request for {}".format(self.path).encode('utf-8'))
 def run(server_class=HTTPServer, handler_class=S, port=8080):
   logging.basicConfig(level=logging.INFO)
   server_address = ('', port)
   httpd = server_class(server_address, handler_class)
   logging.info('Starting httpd...\n')
   try:
      httpd.serve_forever()
   except KeyboardInterrupt:
      pass
   httpd.server_close()
   logging.info('Stopping httpd...\n')


 if __name__ == '__main__':
     from sys import argv


   if len(argv) == 2:
       run(port=int(argv[1]))
   else:
       run()

12.8 Deleting EventDestinationId subscription
Events at some EventDestination

Sometimes administrators may want to stop receiving Events at some specific
EventDestinationId that was earlier subscribed for. The proper way to do this is to send a
DELETE request to the EventDestination endpoint the subscription was created with:
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId}. This will remove dp-api
EventService’s knowledge of the EventDestination resource, so Events will no longer be
broadcasted there.

Example:

Send the DELETE request to unsubscribe the “test-event-subscription” EventDestination
resource:

 [root@kjlmo17-oem ~]# curl -k -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" -X DELETE
 https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-event-subscription | jq
 {
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-event-subscription",
     "@odata.type": "",
     "Context": "Public",
     "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:8082/eventreceiver/",
     "HttpHeaders": [
      {
       "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
       "OData-Version": "4.0"
        }
     ],
     "Id": "test-event-subscription,
     "Name": "",
     "SNMP": {},
     "Status": {},
     "SubscriptionType": ""
 }


Now that the “test-event-subscription” EventDestination resource was deleted, EventService will
no longer send Events to the “http://172.16.0.1:8082/eventreceiver/" destination.
13. MetricReport data Streaming Subscriptions
MetricReport data streaming subscriptions are a special type of subscription where clients
subscribe to receive a certain set of Metric data at a specified interval. Similar to a generic Event
subscription, clients must send a POST request to the
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} endpoint where
EventDestinationId must be unique. Also similar to general Event subscriptions, an Event
Receiver service must be setup to handle POST request from dp-api which will come in the form
of a MetricReport Redfish resource. To designate a particular subscription request as a
MetricReport subscription, EventDestination.EventTypes must be set to “MetricReport”, and
EventDestination.MetricReportDefinitions must be defined. See below for more details.

MetricReport Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/MetricReport.v1_5_0.json

Each MetricReport contains an array of MetricValue resources, which provide individual Metric
names, values, and other metadata. The schema for MetricValues can be seen within the
MetricReport schema above.

13.1 Available MetricReport Data Sets
To view the available data sets which a client can subscribe to receive, clients must run a GET
request to the /redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions endpoint to view the
MetricDefinitions collection. Examplel GET request to view the MetricDefinitions collection:

 [root@kjlmo12-oem rest_api]# curl -k -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions | jq
 {
   "@odata.context": "MetricDefinitionCollection.MetricDefinitionCollection",
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions",
   "@odata.type": "MetricDefinitionCollection.v1_0_0.MetricDefinitionCollection",
  "Description": "MetricDefinitionCollection defines the collection of supported MetricDefinition resources, which
 describe all supported API Metrics available.",
  "Members": [
   {
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LustreStats"
   },
   {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LinuxStats"
   },
   {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/JobStats"
   },
   {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats"
   },
         {
             "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/TieringStats"
         }
        ],
        "Members@odata.count": 5,
        "Name": "MetricDefinitionCollection"
    }




The MetricDefinitions collection defines the individual MetricDefinition resources which
represent a particular data set that a client can subscribe to receive. The
EventDestination.MetricReportDefinitions field must be set to a valid
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/{MetricReportDefinitionId} endpoint
which provides the desired MetricDefinition in its MetricReportDefinition.Metrics list in order to
be considered a valid request. To find more info on each individual MetricDefinition resource, a
GET request to the particular
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/{MetricDefinitionId} resource endpoint can be
made. To find more info on each individual MetricReportDefinition resource, a GET request to
the particular
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/{MetricReportDefinitionId} resource
endpoint can be made. Section 14 contains more details about the /redfish/v1/TelemetryService,
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions,
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions,
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/{MetricReportDefinitionId} and
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/{MetricDefinitionId} endpoints and resources
and their relationships.

13.1.1 LustreStats Data Set
The LustreStats data set defined by the
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LustreStats MetricDefinition resource provides a
data set of all Lustre filesystem statistics, both at the top-level Filesystem and individual Lustre
target levels. The default LustreStats MetricReportDefinition:
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/LustreStats Provides the LustreStats
MetricDefinition in its Metrics list and can be used to subscribe to receive the data. The
following attributes are collected for each individual Lustre target (MDTs and OSTs), as well as
the top-level Lustre filesystem.

NOTE: The LustreStats MetricDefinition is of Implementation type: “Reported”, meaning data is
collected from external components and aggregated to a single location accessible to grp-rfsf-api
HA group services on the mgmt. nodes only.

Individual MDT and OST statistics:

13.1.4 EnvironmentalStats Data Set
The EnvironmentalStats data set defined by the
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition resource
provides a data set of all “environmental” metrics available from the system, i.e. any sort of
metric to represent energy consumption from the system. The default EnvironmentalStats
MetricReportDefinition:
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats Provides the
EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition in its Metrics list and can be used to subscribe to receive
the data. These metric readings largely come from various IPMI and SES sensors available to
ClusterStor nodes, depending on the HW config and attached enclosures available. Information
may include the current sensor reading, units, and thresholds for each sensor, as well as any other
information they may uniquely provide. The sensor “types” collected at a high level are listed for
each enclosure type below.

NOTE: The EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition is of Implementation type: “Sensor”, meaning
data is gathered from internal API services / components, accessible to those API services /
components running directly on cluster nodes.

IPMI:

   •    Temperature
   •    Voltage
   •    Current
   •    Power Supply
   •    Fan

SES:

   •    PSU
   •    Cooling
   •    Temperature
   •    Enclosure_Electronics
   •    Enclosure
   •    Voltage_Sensor
   •    Current_Sensor
   •    Enclosure_Electronics_Power
   •    Enclosure_Electronics_Diagnostics

13.2. MetricReport Event Subscriptions
As mentioned above, in order to receive MetricReport streaming data for one of the defined
MetricDefinition data sets from RFSF API EventService, clients must send a special
EventDestination subscription POST request to the same endpoint used to subscribe for general
Events: /redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId}. The details of what makes
this EventDestination POST request "special" or different from a general Event subscription
request are contained within the request body:

Example MetricReport EventDestination POST request body:
 {
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metric-report",
     "Id": "test-metric-report",
     "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:8082/metricsreceiver/",
     "HttpHeaders": [
       {
         "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
       "OData-Version": "4.0"
        }
     ],
     "Context": "Public",
     "EventTypes": [
        "MetricReport"
     ],
     "MetricReportDefinitions": [
        {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LustreStats"
        }
     ]
 }




Details of the request body that differentiate a MetricReport EventDestination subscription from
a generate EventDestination subscription request:

      •    EventTypes - this Array must contain the EventType of "MetricReport"
           o   RFSF API EventService keys off this EventTypes field to kick off some special
               setup for the MetricReport data stream
   •   MetricReportDefinitions - This must contain a single valid
       /redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/{MetricReportDefinitionId}
       endpoint
           o Only one MetricReportDefinition resource may be subscribed to at a time
           o The data set received is defined by the MetricReportDefinition.Metrics list, which
               must contain a valid MetricDefinition endpoint
           o The rate at which data is received by the client is defined by the
               MetricReportDefinition.Schedule

13.2.1 MetricReport Event Subscriptions –
EventDesetination.MetricReportDefinitions
As mentioned above, part of what makes a subscription request to
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} endpoint unique compared to
generic Event subscriptions, is the MetricReportDefinitions specified in the EventDestination
request body payload. The request body must contain a MetricReportDefinitions list with:

   •   A single valid odata.id endpoint of an existing
       /redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/{MetricReportDefinitionId}
       resource

13.3. MetricReport Subscription Restrictions and Behavior
MetricReport Subscription requests do have some rules surrounding when a request is considered
valid or not, checked both against the request endpoint, request body, and certain conditions on
the system related to a data source being available or not. There are both generic restrictions that
apply to MetricReport subscription request for all MetricReportDefintions’s, as well as more
specific restrictions for certain MetricReportDefintions’s. The following sections will highlight
both. It will also highlight some behavior that can occur when subscribing to receive certain
MetricReportDefinitions’s that depends on the activity related to the collection / propagation of
the MetricDefinition data that MetricReportDefinition provides in its Metrics list on going on the
cluster.

13.3.1 MetricReport Subscription Generic Restrictions
The following list highlights MetricReport subscription request restrictions that apply to all
MetricReportDefinition’s:

   ▪   Each MetricReport Subscription can only be for one target MetricReportDefinition
       endpoint
   ▪   There is no limit to the number of client subscribers subscribed to receive that
       MetricReportDefinition
    ▪    The rate at which clients receive data when subscribed is specified by the associated
         MetricReportDefinition.Schedule in the MetricReportDefinition resource passed in the
         request body
    ▪    The MetricReportDefinition.Schedule.RecurrenceInterval is set by the associated
         MetricDefinition.SensingInterval by default, but can be updated to change the rate at
         which data is received via a PUT or PATCH request to that MetricReportDefinition
         resource
    ▪    MetricReport Events are only sent to a EventDestinations subscribed to receive that
         MetricReportDefinition

13.3.2 MetricReport Subscription
MetricReportDefinition/MetricDefinition specific Restrictions
and Behavior
Some MetricReportDefinition’s that may be requested in a MetricReport subscription request
have some more rules surrounding whether or not a request is allowed to proceed or not. Most of
these rules regard the capability or availability of the data source that pulls the MetricDefinition
data specified by the MetricReportDefinition.Metrics list in the request body. Additionally,
certain subscriptions for certain MetricReportDefinition’s come with some expectations
surrounding the behavior of the system in terms of when data may become available or not
without terminating the subscription. The following sub-sections highlight restrictions and
special behavior for each MetricReportDefinition subscription that has them.

13.3.2.1 JobStats MetricReportDefinition Subscription specific
Restrictions and Behavior
When subscribing to receive JobStats data from the API, there are certain system conditions that
must be satisfied in order for the request to be accepted.

First, jobstats collection must be enabled. The command to check and enable jobstats collection
on the system is the following (see the CSCLI command reference document for more
information on the cscli command):

 [root@kjlmo1200 ~]# cscli lustre jobstats collection -h
 usage: cscli lustre jobstats collection [-h] (--enable | --disable) [--fs FILESYSTEM]


 optional arguments:
  -h, --help   show this help message and exit.
  --enable     Enable Lustre Job Statistics collection
  --disable    Disable Lustre Job Statistics collection.
   --fs FILESYSTEM [optional] Specify the filesystem Default:kjlmo12
 [root@kjlmo1200 ~]#
To check the current status of jobstats collection on the system, you can run “cscli lustre
jobstats list”:

 [root@kjlmo1200 ~]# cscli lustre jobstats list
 ----------------------------------------------------
  FSName Collection Frequency(in sec) Scheduler
 ----------------------------------------------------
  kjlmo12 Disabled        -            -
 ----------------------------------------------------
 [root@kjlmo1200 ~]#


 If “cscli lustre jobstats list” shows as disabled, and a client tries to make a request to
 subscribe to receive JobStats MetricReport data, an error response such as the following
 may be seen:
  {
   "error": {
    "code": "400",
    "message": "JobStats Collection is not enabled on the system! Please enable with \"cscli lustre jobstats
  collection --enable\" before subscribing to receive JobStats MetricReports!"
      }
  }



Unique behaviors of JobStats MetricReport subscription:

      •   If jobstats collection is enabled, and the request succeeds to create a subscription to
          receive JobStats MetricReport data, it is still possible that no data will come back to the
          client if there are no active jobs running on the system.
      •   If jobstats collection is disabled or any other dropped connection interrupts the data
          flow while a JobStats MetricReport subscription is active, a failed thread callback
          Event will automatically be sent to the client which will cancel the subscription (see
          section 13.3.3 for more details on this)

13.3.2.1 TieringStats MetricReportDefinition Subscription
specific Restrictions and Behavior
When subscribing to receive TieringStats data from the API, there are certain system
conditions that must be satisfied in order for the request to be accepted.

First, lustre tiering must be enabled. The command to check and enable lustre tiering on the
system is the following (see the CSCLI command reference document for more information on
the cscli command):

 [root@kjlmo1200 ~]# cscli lustre tiering -h
    usage: cscli lustre tiering [-h] {show,enable,disable} ...


    Manage the Clusterstor tiering service


    positional arguments:
     {show,enable,disable}
       show          Displays the current state of the Clusterstor tiering service
       enable        Enable the Clusterstor tiering service
       disable       Disable the Clusterstor tiering service


    optional arguments:
     -h, --help     show this help message and exit.


    In order to validate the lustre tiering is both enabled, and active – “cscli lustre tiering show”
    command output must show the following:

        [root@kjlmo700 ~]# cscli lustre tiering show
        State: Enabled
        Status: Active
        Client mount: Active
        Lustre: Active
        [root@kjlmo700 ~]#




The above output indicates that not only was the Lustre filesystem started with “cscli mount”
(Lustre: Active) – but “cscli lustre tiering enable” has been run in order to activate auto-tiering
(State: Enabled, Status: Active, Client mount: Active). If output of “cscli lustre tier show”
does not show that it is both Enabled State and Active Status , and a client tries to make a
request to subscribe to receive TieringStats MetricReport data, an error response such as the
following may be seen:


 {
  "error": {
   "code": "400",
   "message": "Lustre Tiering is not enabled on the system! Please enable with \"cscli lustre tiering enable\" before
subscribing to receive TieringStats MetricReports!"
    }
}



Unique behaviors of TieringStats MetricReport subscription:

         •    If lustre tiering is enabled, and the request succeeds to create a subscription to receive
              TieringStats MetricReport data, it is still possible that no data will come back to the
              client if there is no on-going data movement or tiering operations against the filesystem
    •    If lustre tiering is disabled or any other dropped connection interrupts the data flow
         while a TieringStats MetricReport subscription is active, a failed thread callback Event
         will automatically be sent to the client which will cancel the subscription (see section
         13.3.3 for more details on this)




13.3.3 MetricReport subscription failed thread callback
Events
As mentioned above, throughout the lifetime of a MetricReport subscription for any
MetricReportDefinition, it is possible that due to some system event or administrative action
on the cluster, that the backend data source may be disabled, fail, or go away for some other
reason. When this occurs, the backend EC which is the component collecting data from that
data source will trigger a “failed thread callback” Event, indicating to the API and client that
the subscription is being automatically removed and that clients will need to re-subscribe at a
later time to receive data again for that MetricReportDefinition. This “failed thread callback”
Event, will remove all subscribers for that MetricReportDefinition, no matter how many there
are, and all client EventDestination endpoints will receive the Event indicating their
subscription has been cancled.

An example of the Event body send to clients when a “failed thread callback” exception is hit,
may look like the following:

 Destination: /metricsreceiver/
 Headers:
 Host: 172.16.0.1:8083
 User-Agent: Go-http-client/1.1
 Content-Length: 655
 Accept-Encoding: gzip




 Body:
 "{\"Id\": \"e494d23a-3df6-11ee-a743-b4969102730c\", \"Events\": [{\"EventId\": \"e494d23a-3df6-11ee-a743-
 b4969102730c\", \"EventType\": \"Alert\", \"EventTimestamp\": \"1692384110.127196\", \"Message\":
 \"TieringStats thread FAILED! This thread exited unexpectedly for EventDestination: test-metrics-report-tier. ALL
 subscribers for this DataSet will be removed. Clients must re-subscribe to receive data again.\", \"Severity\":
 \"Critical\", \"Oem\": {}, \"OriginOfCondition\": {\"e494d23a-3df6-11ee-a743-b4969102730c\":
 \"/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metrics-report-tier\"}}], \"OdataType\": \"#Event.1.0.0.Event\",
 \"Name\": \"Events\"}"
     As the message in the Event payload indicates, the EventDestination resource has been
     removed, and the associated client must re-subscribe to start receiving this data again.




13.4. MetricReport Subscription Example
The following example will show the full setup of a MetricReport EventDestination subscription,
which is setup to receive the default LustreStats MetricReportDefinition, at a default
Schedule.RecurrentInterval of 10 seconds, at the client side Destination:
http://172.16.0.1:8082/metricsreceiver/. It will show the details of the request body, the POST
request being executed by, and the client side EventReceiver service that will parse and print the
data each time it receives a MetricReport Event:

Request body:

MetricReport EventDestination POST request body
 {
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metric-report",
     "Id": "test-metric-report",
     "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:8082/metricsreceiver/",
     "HttpHeaders": [
       {
         "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
       "OData-Version": "4.0"
        }
     ],
     "Context": "Public",
     "EventTypes": [
        "MetricReport"
     ],
     "MetricReportDefinitions": [
        {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LustreStats"
        }
     ]
 }



Request Body MetricReport details:

      ▪    "EventTypes": ["MetricReport"] – specifies this is a subscription for MetricReports
      ▪    "MetricReportDefinitions": [{"@odata.id":
           "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/LustreStats"}] – specifies the
           MetricReportDefinitiont the client is subscribing to receive
       ▪     NOTE: for more information about the MetricReportDefinition endpoint passed in the
             MetricReportDefinitionsList, a GET request can be run to the resource to see the
             details




POST request sent to dp-api:

MetricReport EventDestination POST request
 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" -H "Content-Type: application/json-rpc" -d
 @rest_api/events/metrics_subscription.json https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-
 metrics-report | jq
 {
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metrics-report",
   "@odata.type": "",
     "Context": "Public",
     "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:8082/metricsreceiver/",
     "EventTypes": [
        "MetricReport"
     ],
     "HttpHeaders": [
      {
          "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
          "OData-Version": "4.0"
        }
     ],
     "Id": "test-metrics-report",
     "MetricReportDefinitions": [
        {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LustreStats"
        }
     ],
     "Name": "",
     "SNMP": {},
     "Status": {},
     "SubscriptionType": ""
 }




If the POST request was successfully received, the client Event Receiver running
at http://172.16.0.1:8082/metricsreceiver/ will receive the data every
MetricReportDefinition.Schedule.RecurrenceInteval seconds. See the following example of
client Event Receiver code parsing and printing all MetricValues from the MetricReport each
time it receives a MetricReport Event

Event Receiver service receives MetricReport every RecurrenceInteval and parses and
outputs the MetricValues (truncated below):
