13.5. Updating MetricReport Subscriptions
Similar to updating generic Event subscriptions in section 12.2.2, throughout the lifetime of an
MetricReport EventDestination resource, it is possible to update the subscription parameters to
receive MetricReports by altering the EvenDestination resource initially created with a PUT or
PATCH request to an existing /redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId}
resource. The PUT or PATCH request body should contain the information to update in the
existing EventDestination resource, that results in a change to the resource. If no new
information is contained in the request body, then a 400 “BadRequest” response will be received.


13.5.1 Updating MetricReport Subscription via a PUT request



One mechanism that can be used to update an existing MetricReport subscription, is to send a
PUT request to the associated EventDestination resource at the
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId}endpiont. By definition, the HTTP
PUT request method creates a new resource, or replaces a representation of the target resource
entirely with the request payload. For the
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} PUT request implementation, it is
expected that the request payload will replace an existing target resource. Because of this, it is
required that the request body contains a fully populated EventDestination model with updates to
the existing resource.

For example, say you have an existing MetricReport subscription with EventDestination.Id “test-
metrics-report-linux”

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-
 metrics-report-linux | jq
 {
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metrics-report-linux",
   "@odata.type": "",
   "Context": "Public",
   "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:8085/metricsreceiver/",
  "EventTypes": [
     "MetricReport"
  ],
  "HttpHeaders": [
     {
       "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
       "OData-Version": "4.0"
   }
  ],
  "Id": "test-metrics-report-linux",
  "MetricReportDefinitions": [
     {
       "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LinuxStats"
   }
  ],
  "Name": "",
    "SNMP": {},
    "Status": {},
    "SubscriptionType": ""
}


And would like to update the MetricReportDefinitions endpoint to a MetricReportDefinition
which as a lower RecurrenceInterval in order to receive LinuxStats metrics at a higher
frequency, as well as update the Destination endpoint at which you’d like to receive them. To
update this subscription with a PUT request, the request body should contain the entire
existing EventDestination model in the payload, with the changes you’d like to apply
contained within.

Example PUT request payload:

    {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metrics-report-linux",
        "Id": "test-metrics-report-linux",
        "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:8085/metricsreceiver-slower/",
        "HttpHeaders": [
          {
                 "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
                 "OData-Version": "4.0"
             }
        ],
        "Context": "Public",
        "EventTypes": [
           "MetricReport"
        ],
        "MetricReportDefinitions": [
           {
             "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LinuxStats120s"
           }
        ],
    }


    Details of the request payload:
       • The EventDestination.Id is the same as the target resource: test-metrics-report-linux
       • Destination has been updated to: http://172.16.0.1:8085/metricsreceiver-slower/
       • MetricReportDefinitions has been updated to a new MetricReportDefinition
            endpoint, which has a 120s RecurrenceInterval defined (to see this run a GET
            request to the /redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LinuxStats120s endpoint)

    The PUT request when sent, if all requirements are met, will then entirely update and
    replace the target resource.

    Example successful PUT request using payload above:
 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" -d @events/metrics_subscription_linux_stats_put_update.json -X PUT
 https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metrics-report-linux | jq
 {
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metrics-report-linux",
     "@odata.type": "",
     "Context": "Public",
     "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:8085/metricsreceiver-slower/",
     "EventTypes": [
      "MetricReport"
     ],
     "HttpHeaders": [
        {
          "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
          "OData-Version": "4.0"
        }
     ],
     "Id": "test-metrics-report-linux",
     "MetricReportDefinitions": [
        {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LinuxStats120s"
        }
     ],
     "Name": "",
     "SNMP": {},
     "Status": {},
     "SubscriptionType": ""
 }


Now, a GET request to the same test-metrics-report-linux EventDestination resource will
reflect the updates taken from the PUT request body:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metrics-report-linux | jq
 {
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metrics-report-linux",
   "@odata.type": "",
   "Context": "Public",
   "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:8085/metricsreceiver-slower/",
     "EventTypes": [
        "MetricReport"
     ],
     "HttpHeaders": [
        {
          "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
              "OData-Version": "4.0"
          }
     ],
           "Id": "test-metrics-report-linux",
           "MetricReportDefinitions": [
             {
             "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LinuxStats120s"
              }
           ],
           "Name": "",
           "SNMP": {},
           "Status": {},
           "SubscriptionType": ""
       }


  This means, that the client will now be receiving LinuxStats MetricReport Events at the
  http://172.16.0.1:8085/metricsreceiver-slower/ Destination at a slower interval of 120s,
  defined by the LinuxStats120s MetricReportDefinition resource.



13.5.2 Updating MetricReport Subscription via a PATCH request

Another mechanism that can be used to update an existing MetricReport subscription, is to send a
PATCH request to the associated EventDestination resource at the
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId}endpiont. By definition, the HTTP
PATCH request method creates partial changes to an existing resource. For the
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} PATCH request implementation, it
is expected that the request payload will replace some number of fields in an existing resource,
but not the entire resource like PUT does.

For example, say you have an existing MetricReport subscription with EventDestination.Id “test-
metrics-report-linux” :

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-
 metrics-report-linux | jq
 {
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metrics-report-linux",
   "@odata.type": "",
  "Context": "Public",
  "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:8085/metricsreceiver-slower/",
  "EventTypes": [
     "MetricReport"
  ],
  "HttpHeaders": [
     {
           "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
           "OData-Version": "4.0"
       }
  ],
     "Id": "test-metrics-report-linux",
     "MetricReportDefinitions": [
       {
       "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LinuxStats"
        }
     ],
     "Name": "",
     "SNMP": {},
     "Status": {},
     "SubscriptionType": ""
 }


And would like to update the MetricReportDefinitions send_interval to increase the interval at
which you receive LinuxStats metrics. To update this subscription with a PATCH request, the
request body can contain only the EventDestination.MetricReportDefintions structure in the
payload with the changes you’d like to apply contained within:

Example PATCH request payload:

 {
     "MetricReportDefinitions": [
       {
         "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LinuxStats30s"
       }
     ]
 }


Details of the request payload:
   • Only the MetricReportDefintions endpoint is updated to LinuxStats30s endpoint, which
        specifies a RecurrenceInterval of 30s within.

Example PATCH request using the payload above:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" -d @events/metrics_subscription_linux_stats_patch_update.json -X PATCH
 https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metrics-report-linux | jq
 {
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metrics-report-linux",
   "@odata.type": "",
     "Context": "Public",
     "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:8085/metricsreceiver-slower/",
     "EventTypes": [
        "MetricReport"
     ],
     "HttpHeaders": [
      {
       "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
       "OData-Version": "4.0"
      }
     ],
     "Id": "test-metrics-report-linux",
     "MetricReportDefinitions": [
        {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LinuxStats30s"
        }
     ],
     "Name": "",
     "SNMP": {},
     "Status": {},
     "SubscriptionType": ""
 }


Now, a GET request to the same test-metrics-report-linux EventDestination resource will reflect
the updates taken from the PATCH request body:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://10.214.132.158:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-
 metrics-report-linux | jq
 {
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metrics-report-linux",
     "@odata.type": "",
     "Context": "Public",
     "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:8085/metricsreceiver-slower/",
     "EventTypes": [
      "MetricReport"
     ],
     "HttpHeaders": [
        {
          "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
          "OData-Version": "4.0"
        }
     ],
     "Id": "test-metrics-report-linux",
     "MetricReportDefinitions": [
        {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LinuxStats30s"
        }
     ],
     "Name": "",
     "SNMP": {},
     "Status": {},
     "SubscriptionType": ""
 }
This means, that the client will now be receiving LinuxStats MetricReport Events at the
http://172.16.0.1:8085/metricsreceiver-slower/ Destination at a quicker interval of 30s, defined
by the LinuxStats30s MetricReportDefinition resource.




13.6. Canceling MetricReport Subscriptions
Sometimes administrators may want to stop receiving MetricReport data once they are
subscribed to do so. The proper way to do this would be to send a DELETE request to the
EventDestination endpoint the subscription was created with:
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestination}. This will remove dp-api
EventService's knowledge of the EventDestination resource.

Example:

Send the DELETE request for test-metric-report EventDestination:

DELETE request to cancel MetricReport subscription

 # curl -k -X DELETE -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://172.26.137.72:8081/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metrics-report | jq
  % Total % Received % Xferd Average Speed Time Time Time Current
                      Dload Upload Total Spent Left Speed
 100 785 100 785 0 0 46176              0 --:--:-- --:--:-- --:--:-- 46176
 {
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-metrics-report",
     "@odata.type": "",
     "Context": "Public",
     "Destination": "http://172.16.0.1:8082/metricsreceiver/",
     "EventTypes": [
      "MetricReport"
     ],
     "HttpHeaders": [
        {
          "Content-Type": "Application/JSON",
       "OData-Version": "4.0"
        }
     ],
     "Id": "test-metrics-report",
     "MetricReportDefinitions": [
        {
          "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LustreStats"
        }
     ],
     "Name": "",
     "SNMP": {},
     "Status": {},
     "SubscriptionType": ""
 }



Once the EventDestination resource has been removed, the client will no longer receive data at
the specified EventDestination.Destination endpoint, and must re-subscribe in order to start
receiving data again.


14. TelemetryService Resource
The TelemetryService resource lives directly under the ServiceRoot /redfish/v1 and can be seen
by issuing a GET request to /redfish/v1/TelemetryService. It provides an entry point to the
MetricDefinitions, MetricReportDefinitions, and Triggers resource collections that provide
various implementations of Telemetry and metric data from the system. The initial use of the
TelemetryService in the NEO RFSF API will be focused on MetricDefinitions, which will
provide the set of supported Metrics available via the API.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/TelemetryService.v1_3_2.json

Example TelemetryService GET request:

 [root@kjlmo12-oem rest_api]# curl -k -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService | jq
 {
     "@odata.context": "TelemetryService.TelemetryService",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService",
     "@odata.type": "TelemetryService.v1_3_1.TelemetryService",
     "Description": "TelemetryService for RFSF API",
     "Id": "TelemetryService",
     "MetricDefinitions": {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions"
     },
     "Name": "TelemetryService",
     "Status": {}
 }


 Details of the response: There is not much detail provided in the response output. The
 important thing to note, is that it provides the path to the MetricDefinitions collection resource,
 which is initially the only TelemetryService collection implemented by the NEO RFSF API.
14.1 MetricDefinitions Collection Resource
The MetricDefinition Collection resource provides a collection of all supported
MetricDefinition resources. Each MetricDefinition resource is intended to provide a
description of a data set that one can subscribe to receive MetricReports from via the
MetricReport data streaming subscriptions described in section 13. The MetricDefintion
collection resource is also used to check against subscription request, that the
EventDestination.MetricReportDefinitions “data_set” a client is subscribing for, is in fact a
supported MetricDefinition. This means, that each MetricDefinition.Id seen in this collection,
represents the name of an actual supported data set available from the API.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/MetricDefinitionCollection.json

Example MetricDefinitions GET request:

 [root@kjlmo12-oem rest_api]# curl -k -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions | jq
 {
   "@odata.context": "MetricDefinitionCollection.MetricDefinitionCollection",
  "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions",
  "@odata.type": "MetricDefinitionCollection.v1_0_0.MetricDefinitionCollection",
  "Description": "MetricDefinitionCollection defines the collection of supported MetricDefinition resources, which
 describe all supported API Metrics available.",
  "Members": [
   {
           "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LustreStats"
      },
      {
           "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LinuxStats"
      },
      {
           "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/JobStats"
      },
      {
           "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats"
      },
      {
           "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/TieringStats"
      }
     ],
     "Members@odata.count": 5,
     "Name": "MetricDefinitionCollection"
 }


 Details of the response:
         •    The Members field of this resource holds the collection of all supported
              MetricDefinition resource endpoints
         •    The Members@odata.count shows how many total MetricDefinition resources exist
              the the collection




14.2 MetricDefinition Resource
The MetricDefinition resource contains the definition, metadata, or characteristics for a metric.
For the purposes of Metrics available via the NEO RFSF API, each MetricDefinition resource
will provide a description and metadata of the data sets contained in MetricReports, which
available for streaming via subscription requests to receive that data. Each MetricDefinition
resource is currently only required to provide a Description and SensingInterval field, where the
description field contains a high-leveled description of the data set provided by that
MetricDefinition, and the SensingInterval contains the metadata of how often the data is
collected on the backend. In some cases, the SensingInterval may be configurable.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/MetricDefinition.v1_3_2.json

Example MetricDefintion GET request:

 [root@kjlmo12-oem rest_api]# curl -k -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStat
 s | jq
 {
  "@odata.context": "MetricDefinition.MetricDefinition",
  "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats",
  "@odata.type": "MetricDefinition.v1_2_0.MetricDefinition",
  "Description": "Stastics for all measurable components that cover any Environmental factors such as Power,
 Current, Voltage, etc. SensingInterval of 1800 seconds (30 minutes) by default.",
     "Id": "EnvironmentalStats",
     "Name": "EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition",
     "SensingInterval": "1800"
 }


 Details of the response:

        •    Description: this provides a high level description of the full data set provided by this
             MetricDefinition resource
        •    Id: this provides a unique Id to define the data set provided by this MetricDefinition –
             when subscribing to receive this data set, the
             EventDestination.MetricReportDefinitions “data_set” field in the request body must
             contain a valid MetricDefinition.Id that exists
       •   SensingInterval: The time interval between when a metric is updated – this represents
           the backend interval at which data is collected, which is configurable for certain
           MetricDefinition resources and is not configurable for others. The unit is in seconds.

14.2.1 Updating MetricDefinition Resources
As mentioned above, there are certain MetricDefinition resources in the supported
MetricDefinitions collection that are configurable and some that are not configurable. For the
current set of MetricDefinition resources in the MetricDefinitions collection, the only resource
which is configurable, is the EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition resource. The other three
MetricDefinition resources, LustreStats, LinuxStats, JobStats, are not configurable.

When configuring a MetricDefinition resource, there is really only one field that has any
functional affect on the system when changed, and that is: MetricDefinition.SensingInterval.
As mentioned above, the SensingInterval field represents the interval at which a data set is
collected. Each MetricDefinition resource has a default SensingInterval value, which for the
EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition resource, can be updated within a minimum value
restriction.

14.2.1.1 Updating MetricDefinition Resource via a PUT
request
One mechanism to update an existing MetricDefinition resource, if it is configurable, is to
send a PUT request to the resource with updates in the Request body. By definition, the HTTP
PUT request method creates a new resource, or replaces a representation of the target resource
entirely with the request payload. For the
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/{MetricDefinitionId} PUT request
implementation, it is expected that the request payload will replace an existing target resource.

Example GET request to resource before updates:

[root@kjlmo12-oem rest_api]# curl -k -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStat
s | jq
{
 "@odata.context": "MetricDefinition.MetricDefinition",
 "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats",
 "@odata.type": "MetricDefinition.v1_2_0.MetricDefinition",
 "Description": "Stastics for all measurable components that cover any Environmental factors such as Power,
Current, Voltage, etc. SensingInterval of 1800 seconds (30 minutes) by default.",
 "Id": "EnvironmentalStats",
    "Name": "EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition",
    "SensingInterval": "1800"
}
Example Request body payload:

 {
  "@odata.context": "MetricDefinition.MetricDefinition",
  "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats",
  "@odata.type": "MetricDefinition.v1_2_0.MetricDefinition",
  "Description": "Stastics for all measurable components that cover any Environmental factors such as Power,
 Current, Voltage, etc. SensingInterval of 1800 seconds (30 minutes) by default.",
     "Id": "EnvironmentalStats",
     "Name": "EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition",
     "SensingInterval": "300"
 }


 Note: the SensingInterval field is in the request body payload has been changed from the
 existing resource.

 Example PUT request to the resource:


 [root@kjlmo12-oem rest_api]# curl -k -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" -X PUT -d
 @envstats_metric_definition_put.json
 https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalSt
 ats | jq
 {
   "@odata.context": "MetricDefinition.MetricDefinition",
  "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats",
  "@odata.type": "MetricDefinition.v1_2_0.MetricDefinition",
  "Description": "Stastics for all measurable components that cover any Environmental factors such as Power,
 Current, Voltage, etc. SensingInterval of 1800 seconds (30 minutes) by default.",
  "Id": "EnvironmentalStats",
  "Name": "EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition",
     "SensingInterval": "300"
 }




Example GET request to resource after updates:

 [root@kjlmo12-oem rest_api]# curl -k -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalSt
 ats | jq
 {
   "@odata.context": "MetricDefinition.MetricDefinition",
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats",
     "@odata.type": "MetricDefinition.v1_2_0.MetricDefinition",
     "Description": "Stastics for all measurable components that cover any Environmental factors such as Power,
    Current, Voltage, etc. SensingInterval of 1800 seconds (30 minutes) by default.",
        "Id": "EnvironmentalStats",
        "Name": "EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition",
        "SensingInterval": "300"
    }


The SensingInterval of the EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition has now been updated from
1800 to 300, changing the rate at which the data set is collected from the system from 30
minutes (1800s) default, to a 5 minute (300s) interval.




14.2.1.2 Updating MetricDefinition Resource via a PATCH
request
Another mechanism to update an existing MetricDefinition resource, if it is configurable, is to
send a PATCH request to the resource with updates in the Request body. By definition, the
HTTP PATCH request method creates partial changes to an existing resource. For the
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/{MetricDefinitionId} PATCH request
implementation, it is expected that the request payload will replace some number of fields in
an existing resource, but not the entire resource like PUT does.

Example GET request to resource before updates:

[root@kjlmo12-oem rest_api]# curl -k -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStat
s | jq
{
 "@odata.context": "MetricDefinition.MetricDefinition",
 "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats",
 "@odata.type": "MetricDefinition.v1_2_0.MetricDefinition",
 "Description": "Stastics for all measurable components that cover any Environmental factors such as Power,
Current, Voltage, etc. SensingInterval of 1800 seconds (30 minutes) by default.",
 "Id": "EnvironmentalStats",
    "Name": "EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition",
    "SensingInterval": "1800"
}


Example Request body payload:

    {
        "SensingInterval": "300"
    }
 Note: the SensingInterval field is in the request body payload has been changed from the
 existing resource, and is the only field being updated with the PATCH request

 Example PUT request to the resource:


 [root@kjlmo12-oem rest_api]# curl -k -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" -X PATCH -d
 @envstats_metric_definition_patch.json
 https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalSt
 ats | jq
 {
   "@odata.context": "MetricDefinition.MetricDefinition",
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats",
  "@odata.type": "MetricDefinition.v1_2_0.MetricDefinition",
  "Description": "Stastics for all measurable components that cover any Environmental factors such as Power,
 Current, Voltage, etc. SensingInterval of 1800 seconds (30 minutes) by default.",
  "Id": "EnvironmentalStats",
  "Name": "EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition",
  "SensingInterval": "300"
 }




Example GET request to resource after updates:

 [root@kjlmo12-oem rest_api]# curl -k -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalSt
 ats | jq
 {
   "@odata.context": "MetricDefinition.MetricDefinition",
  "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats",
  "@odata.type": "MetricDefinition.v1_2_0.MetricDefinition",
  "Description": "Stastics for all measurable components that cover any Environmental factors such as Power,
 Current, Voltage, etc. SensingInterval of 1800 seconds (30 minutes) by default.",
  "Id": "EnvironmentalStats",
  "Name": "EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition",
     "SensingInterval": "300"
 }


The SensingInterval of the EnvironmentalStats MetricDefinition has now been updated from
1800 to 300, changing the rate at which the data set is collected from the system from 30
minutes (1800s) default, to a 5 minute (300s) interval.
14.2.1.2 Restrictions for Updating MetricDefinition
Resources
There are a few basic restrictions for updating MetricDefinition resources via a PUT or
PATCH request. If any of these conditions are broken, the request will not be successful and
the appropriate error message and response code will be returned:

    •   Update request must be to an existing resource
    •   Update requests cannot update resources which are deemed not configurable (see
        above)
    •   Update request body must actually contain fields that update the existing resource
        (PUT or PATCH which results in no updates to existing resource is invalid)
    •   The MetricReport.Description field cannot be empty in the update request body
        payload
    •   The MetricDefinition.Id must match the {MetricDefinitionId} in the request endpoint
    •   The MetricDefintion.SensingInterval must be in seconds
    •   The MetricDefinition.SensingInterval cannot be < 60 seconds for EnvironmentalStats

14.2.2 Creating MetricDefinition Resources
MetricDefinition resources can be created to add to the MetricDefintions collection via a
POST request to the /redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/{MetricDefintionId}
endpoint where the request body payload defines the new MetricDefinition resource content.
The MetricDefinition.Id should have a meaningful value that represents the data set that this
MetricDefinition may represent, as well as a meaningful description of the data set that this
MetricDefinition would represent. The MetricDefinition.SensingInterval should also be
provided to set a backend collection interval of that data set.

Currently, clients may only decide to create a new MetricDefinition resources if they are
planning to add their own backend data collector element controller to the API. Creation of
this new MetricDefinition would be one of the steps that allows clients to subscribe to receive
some new custom data set, which ties API knowledge of the new data set to the custom data
collector. All of this is described more detail in another document, but the follow shows the
actual creation of the new MetricDefinition resource via a POST request:

Example GET request to MetricDefinitions Collection resource before creating a new
resource:

 [root@kjlmo12-oem rest_api]# curl -k -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
 https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions | jq
 {
  "@odata.context": "MetricDefinitionCollection.MetricDefinitionCollection",
  "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions",
  "@odata.type": "MetricDefinitionCollection.v1_0_0.MetricDefinitionCollection",
 "Description": "MetricDefinitionCollection defines the collection of supported MetricDefinition resources, which
describe all supported API Metrics available.",
 "Members": [
        {
             "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LustreStats"
        },
        {
             "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LinuxStats"
        },
        {
             "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/JobStats"
        },
        {
             "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats"
        }
    ],
    "Members@odata.count": 4,
    "Name": "MetricDefinitionCollection"
}

    {

      "Description": "Network throughput and performance statistics from high speed network on the system.
    SensingInterval of 300 seconds by default.",

               •   Id: provides a new unique Id to define this MetricDefinition, cannot previously
                   exist

               •   SensingsInterval: cannot be empty

      SensingInterval of 300 seconds by default.",

        "SensingInterval": "300"
      }

 14.2.2 Removing MetricDefinition Resources
MetricDefinition resources can be removed by sending a DELETE request to the target
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/{MetricDefinitionId} resource you’d like to
remove. DELETE requests do not require a request body. Removing a MetricDefinition resource
can only be done on MetricDefinition resources that were created, beyond the default supported
set of resources in the MetricDefinitions collection, i.e. – you cannot remove a MetricDefinition
in the supported set of: JobStats, LustreStats, LinuxStats, EnvironmentalStats, but you can
remove a MetricDefinition that was created and no longer needed.

Example GET request to MetricDefinitions Collection resource before removing the created
NetworkStats MetricDefinition resource:

   "Description": "MetricDefinitionCollection defines the collection of supported MetricDefinition resources, which
 describe all supported API Metrics available.",

          {
               "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/NetworkStats"

     "Members@odata.count": 5,
     "Name": "MetricDefinitionCollection"

14.3 MetricReportDefinition Resources
In the TelemetryService resource, the MetricReportDefinitions collection holds
MetricReportDefinition resources which define how and when MetricReports for data in a
given MetricDefinition data set are generated by the API. A MetricReport which is
created by a redfish service, can be transmitted using the Redfish EventService, stored
locally for retrieval, or both. A MetricReport may be created periodically and propagated
at a given Recurrence Interval, when a given reading value changes, or upon GET request.
MetricReportDefinition resources provide the means to define and configure all of these
details, and have a coupled relationship with MetricDefinition resources and MetricReport
resources.

14.3.1 MetricReportDefinitionCollection Resource

The MetricReportDefinition Collection resource provides a collection of all supported
MetricReportDefinition resources. Each MetricReportDefinition resource is intended to
provide a definition of how and when MetricReports for the MetricDefinition in the given
MetricReportDefinition.Metrics list are generated, as well as how these MetricReports are
propagated or made available to clients. The MetricReportCollection resource is also used
to check against subscription request, that the EventDestination.MetricReportDefinitions
endpoint a client is subscribing for exists and is valid.

By default, dp-api TelemetryService will generate a MetricReportDefinition for each
native MetricDefinition resource that is “bound” by that MetricDefintion resource, see
section 14.5.1 “Default MetricReportDefinitions” below for more details.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/MetricReportDefinitionCollection.json

Example GET request response:

 ]# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
 https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions | jq
 {
   "@odata.context": "MetricReportDefinitionCollection.MetricReportDefinitionCollection",
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions",
  "@odata.type": "MetricDefinitionCollection.v1_0_0.MetricDefinitionCollection",
  "Description": "MetricReportCollection defines the collection of supported MetricReportDefinition
 resources, which describe propagation of MetricReports generated by API services",
  "Members": [
    {
      "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/LustreStats"
   },
   {
        "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/LinuxStats"
   },
      {
           "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/JobStats"
      },
      {
           "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats"
      },
      {
           "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/TieringStats"
      }
     ],
     "Members@odata.count": 5,
     "Name": "MetricReportCollection"
 }




Details of the response:

       •      The Members field of this resource holds the collection of all supported
              MetricReportDefinition resource endpoints
       •      The Members@odata.count shows how many total MetricReportDefinition
              resources exist in the collection



14.3.2 MetricReportDefinition resource

As mentioned before, MetricReportDefinition resources are intended to provide a
definition of how and when MetricReports for the MetricDefinition in the given
MetricReportDefinition.Metrics list are generated, as well as how these MetricReports are
propagated or made available to clients. The following fields in the
MetricReportDefinition must be defined in order to configure this:

       •      MetricReportDefinitionEnabled – Indicates whether generation of the defined
              MetricReport is enabled or not
       •      MetricReportDefinitionType – Indicates when the defined MetricReport is
              generated
       •      Metrics – Contains the list of Metrics this MetricReport will provide (this is set by
              a valid MetricDefinition endpoint)
       •      ReportActionsEnum – contains the set of actions for the service to perform when
              the defined MetricReport is generated
       •      ReportUpdates – defines the handling of subsequent MetricReports when a
              MetricReport of the same Id already exists
       •      Schedule – defines the recurrence interval of each MetricReport generation
Each of these properties will be further detailed for the ClusterStor Redfish/Swordfish
API implementation in sub-sections below.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/MetricReportDefinition.v1_4_7.json

Example GET response for a default MetricReportDefinition resource:

 ]# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
 https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/LustreStats | jq
 {
     "@odata.context": "MetricReportDefinition.MetricReportDefinition",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReportDefinitions/LustreStats",
     "@odata.type": "MetricReportDefinition.v1_4_1.MetricReportDefinition",
     "Description": "Default MetricReport resource definition for propagation of the LustreStats data set to the
 /redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReports collection to be consumed",
  "Id": "LustreStats",
  "Links": {},
  "MetricReportDefinitionEnabled": true,
  "MetricReportDefinitionType": "Periodic",
  "Metrics": [
      {
          "MetricId": "LustreStats",
          "MetricProperties": [
            "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LustreStats"
          ]
      }
     ],
     "Name": "LustreStats MetricReportDefinition",
     "ReportActions": [
        "RedfishEvent"
     ],
     "ReportUpdates": "Overwrite",
     "Schedule": {
        "Name": "default",
        "RecurrenceInterval": "5"
     },
     "Status": {}
 }


 Details of the response:

          •    MetricReportDefinitionEnabled – set to true, this means MetricReports defined
               in this resource will be generated
          •    MetricReportDefinitionType – set to “periodic”, this means that MetricReports
               defined in this resource will be generated at a periodic time interval, specified in
               the Schedule property
    •     Metrics – the Metrics list contains one Metric, defined by the LustreStats
          MetricDefintion resource, which will be provided in the generated reports
    •     ReportActions – set to “RedfishEvent” indicating EventService will send an
          Event message containing the MetricReport
    •     ReportUpdates – set to “Overwrite” indicating this MetricReport will be
          overwritten in the /redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReports collection on
          each generation
    •     Schedule – has a Name of “default” indicating it is the “default”
          MetricReportDefinition that is bound by the associated MetricDefinition it
          provides, and RecurrenceInterval of 5 (set my LustreStats.SensingInterval from
          the MetricDefintion)

14.3.2.1 MetricReportDefinition.MetricReportDefinitionEnabled Property

The MetricReportDefinitionEnabled property is a boolean property that controls
whether or not MetricReports defined by this MetricReportDefinition should be
generated or not. For all default MetricReportDefinitions (which are bound by the
associated MetricDefinition) – this is set to true on startup, but can be disabled with a
PUT or PATCH request to the resource. For any subsequently created
MetricReportDefinitons which are not part of the default set, this can be set to true or
false depending on the desired behavior.

When MetricReportDefinitionEnabled is set to true, the MetricReports defined by this
resource will be generated each Schedule period and propagated to the
/redfish/v1/Telemetry/MetricRerports collection – if it is set to false, this report
generation will stop.

14.3.2.2 MetricReportDefinition.MetricReportDefinitionType Property

TheMetricReportDefinitionType property defines when, or the conditions under which,
the MetricReport defined by the MetricReportDefinition is generated. It is an enum with
the following types available. From the MetricReport Schema:


 "MetricReportDefinitionType": {
   "description": "Indicates when the metric report is generated.",
   "enum": [
        "Periodic",
        "OnChange",
        "OnRequest"
   ],
   "enumDescriptions": {
        "OnChange": "The metric report is generated when any of the metric values change.",
        "OnRequest": "The metric report is generated when a HTTP GET is performed on the specified
 metric report.",
      "Periodic": "The metric report is generated at a periodic time interval, specified in the Schedule
 property."
   },
          "longDescription": "This type shall specify when the metric report is generated.",
          "type": "string"
 }


 At this time, the ClusterStor Redfish/Swordfish API implements
 MetricReportDefinitions with a MetricReportDefinitionType of “Periodic” – which
 indicates that these reports will be generated at a periodic time interval defined by the
 Schedule property. Other types are currently not supported.



14.3.2.3 MetricReportDefinition.Metrics Property

The Metrics property specifies the set of Metrics which this report will provide. Each
item in the list should be that of the Metric scheam which defines:

              •   MetricId – the Id of the Metric
              •   MetricProperties – the Properties of the Metric

At this time, only a single Metric may be specified in the Metrics list, and the
MetricProperties list should contain a valid MetricDefinition endpoint which describes
the data that this report will provide. For example:

     "Metrics": [
      {
        "MetricId": "LustreStats",
        "MetricProperties": [
         "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LustreStats"
              ]
          }
     ],




The above Metrics specification states that MetricReports generated by this
MetricReportDefinition will contain data from the data set defined by the LustreStats
MetricDefinition only. In the future, we may support allowing multiple Metrics to be
defined in a single MetricReportDefinition, and part of a single MetricReport.

14.3.2.4 MetricReportDefinition.ReportActions Property
The ReportActions field specifies actions that will be performed when a MetricReport
is generated. From the MetricReportDefinition Schema, the field is an enum with the
following allowable values:

 "ReportActionsEnum": {
   "description": "Actions to perform when a metric report is generated.",
   "enum": [
     "LogToMetricReportsCollection",
     "RedfishEvent"
      ],
      "enumDescriptions": {
         "LogToMetricReportsCollection": "Record the occurrence to the metric report collection.",
         "RedfishEvent": "Send a Redfish event message containing the metric report."
      },
      "enumLongDescriptions": {
      "LogToMetricReportsCollection": "This value shall indicate the service records the occurrence to the
 metric report collection found under the telemetry service. The service shall update the metric report
 based on the setting of the ReportUpdates property.",
      "RedfishEvent": "This value shall indicate the service sends a Redfish event of type MetricReport to
 subscribers in the event subscription collection of the event service."
      },
      "longDescription": "This type shall specify the actions to perform when a metric report is generated.",
      "type": "string"
 },


 At this time, the ClusterStor Redfish/Swordfish API implements the ReportActions of
 type “RedfishEvent”, such that, an Event is sent so subscribed clients with the content
 of the MetricReport as each one is generated.



14.3.2.5 MetricReportDefinition.ReportUpdates Property

The ReportUpdates property specifies the handling of subsequent MetricReports when a
MetricReport exists. From the MetricReportDefinition Schema, the field is an enum
with the following allowable values:


 "ReportUpdatesEnum": {
   "description": "Handling of subsequent metric reports when a metric report exists.",
   "enum": [
     "Overwrite",
     "AppendWrapsWhenFull",
        "AppendStopsWhenFull",
        "NewReport"
      ],
      "enumDescriptions": {
       "AppendStopsWhenFull": "New information is appended to the metric report. The service stops
  adding entries when the metric report has reached its maximum capacity.",
       "AppendWrapsWhenFull": "New information is appended to the metric report. The metric report
  entries are overwritten with new entries when the metric report has reached its maximum capacity.",
       "NewReport": "A new metric report is created, whose resource name is the metric report resource
  name concatenated with the timestamp.",
       "Overwrite": "Overwrite the metric report."
    },
    "enumLongDescriptions": {
        "AppendStopsWhenFull": "This value shall indicate the service appends new information to the
  metric report referenced by the MetricReport property. The service shall stop adding entries when the
  metric report has reached its maximum capacity. The State property within Status should be set to
  `Disabled` and the MetricReportDefinitionEnabled property should be set to `false` when the append
  limit is reached.",
        "AppendWrapsWhenFull": "This value shall indicate the service appends new information to the
  metric report referenced by the MetricReport property. The service shall overwrite entries in the metric
  report with new entries when the metric report has reached its maximum capacity.",
       "NewReport": "This value shall indicate the service creates a new metric report resource, whose
  resource name is the metric report resource name concatenated with the timestamp.",
       "Overwrite": "This value shall indicate the service overwrites the metric report referenced by the
  MetricReport property."
     },
     "longDescription": "This type shall indicate how the service handles subsequent metric reports when a
  metric report exists.",
     "type": "string"
  },


  At this time, the ClusterStor Redfish/Swordfish API implements the ReportUpdates
  type of “overwrite”, such that, when a MetricReport is generated by and API service,
  it will overwrite the MetricReport resource in the
  /redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReports collection which matches its
  MetricReport.Id. This overwrite occurs every Schedule Recurrence interval, such
  that, the latest published MetricReport is always available in the collection. At this
  time this is the only ReportUpdates value supported, but we may consider others in
  the future.



 14.3.2.6 MetricReportDefinition.Schedule Property

The Scheule property defines a Schedule at which a MetricReport is generated. The
Schedule should be populated with a name which identifies that Schedule, such that, it can
be re used between multiple MetricReportDefinitions, as well as, a RecurrenceInterval
which defines the interval of time between each report generation. For initial
implementation, it is expected that the RecurrenceInterval be specified in seconds, but in
the future, we plan to accept any such time format.
By default, on startup, the API will generate a “default” MetricReportDefinition for each
“default MetricDefinition, such that, the MetricReportDefinition has a Schedule.Name of
“default” and a Schedule.RecurrenceInterval set to the MetricDefinition.SensingInterval
which the report provides (this way the MetricReport is generated each time the Metric
data is collected on the backend). If users would like to receive data at a different rate, it is
possible to create another MetricReportDefinition which specifies a different schedule.
More support for this will be available in the future.




14.4 MetricReport Resources
In the TelemetryService resource, the MetricReports collection holds MetricReport
resources which contain Metric information generated as a report by API services. If a
MetricReport is propagated to the MetricReportCollection resource:
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReports, it is then available to be consumed via GET
request to the /redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReports/{MetricReportId} resource
which contains the information a client is interested in, or, can be subscribed to via an
EventDestination subscription with EventTypes of MetricReport, which specifies the
MetricReportDefinition resource that describes the reports a client wishes to receive.



14.4.1 MetricReportCollection Resource

The MetricReports Collection resource provides a collection of all generated
MetricReport resources. If a MetricReportDefinition contains the
“LogToMetricReportsCollection” value in its ReportActions list, the MetricReport it
generates will be propagated to the /redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReports
collection, and will be persistently stored, and updated as defined by the
MetricReportDefinition which generates it.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/MetricReportCollection.json

Example GET request to the MetricReportCollection resource:

 ]# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"
 https://localhost:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReports | jq
 {
   "@odata.context": "MetricReportCollection.MetricReportCollection",
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReports",
   "@odata.type": "MetricReportCollection.v1_0_0.MetricReportCollection",
  "Description": "MetricReportCollection published by API services",
  "Members": [
   {
      "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReports/kjlmo17n000-IPMI-MXE3000018VVS001-
 EnvironmentalStats"
   },
       {
            "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReports/kjlmo17n000-LinuxStats"
       },
 ...
       {
            "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReports/kjlmo17n008-LinuxStats"
       },
       {
            "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricReports/kjlmo17n009-LinuxStats"
        }
     ],
     "Members@odata.count": 26,
     "Name": "MetricReportCollection"
 }


 Details of the response:

            •    The Members field of this resource holds the collection of all supported
                 MetricReport resource endpoints
            •    The Members@odata.count shows how many total MetricReport resources exist
                 in the collection




14.4.2 MetricReport Resource

The MetricReport resource contains a report of a set of Metrics defined by an associated
MetricReportDefinition resource. It will contain a MetricReportDefinition field which
defines that MetricReportDefinition which generated the MetricReport, as well as a
MetricValues list which contains all of the individual Metrics contained within the report
in the form of MetricValue schemas (as seen in the MetricReport Schema below). Each
MetricValue will have:

            •   MetricId – the name or identifier of the metric
            •   MetricValue – the value of the Metric
            •   Oem – section containing units and other miscellaneous data or metadata about
                the metric

MetricReport.Id – the MetricReport.Id must identify the hostname which generated the
report, and the MetricDefintion the report contains. It will be of the form: “<hostname>-
<metric definition id>”, for most MetricDefinitions, with the exception of
EnviromentalStatus MetricDefinition, which will have the form: “<hostname>-<enclosure
type>-<enclosure serial number>-<MetricDefinition>”

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/MetricReport.v1_5_2.json



Example GET request of a LinuxStats MetricReport from a single hostname:

 ]# curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: $RFSF_API_TOKEN"

 14.6 Triggers Resources
 The Triggers resource provides a centralized way to define and manage the threshold
 rules for monitoring specific metric properties, i.e.
 TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/{MetricDefinitionId}. These triggers allow you to
 set upper or lower limits on metric values and define automated actions when those limits
 are reached. For example, In ClusterStor when a threshold is exceeded, the system can
 generate an alert via the Event Service. Instead of configuring thresholds individually
 within each resource that contains a metric, you can create a common set of triggers and
 apply them to multiple metric properties. This approach simplifies configuration, ensures
 consistency, and reduces duplication across resources.




14.6.1 TriggersCollection Resource
The Triggers Collection resource contains all supported Triggers resources. Each Triggers
resource describes thresholds and the actions that subscribers will receive when those
thresholds are exceeded. Currently, only the GET method is supported for the Triggers
Collection and Triggers are created only for the LinuxStats MetricDefinition resource. The
TriggerId follows the format <MetricDefinitionId>-<TriggerName>-<NodeRole>. For
example: LinuxStats-CpuUsage-All.
Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/TriggersCollection.json



Example TriggersCollection GET request:

[root@kjlmo12-oem rest_api]# curl -k -H “X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}”
https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/Triggers | jq
{
  “@odata.context”: “MetricDefinitionCollection.MetricDefinitionCollection”,
  “@odata.id”: “/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions”,
  “@odata.type”: “MetricDefinitionCollection.v1_0_0.MetricDefinitionCollection”,
  “Description”: “MetricDefinitionCollection defines the collection of supported MetricDefinition resources,
which describe all supported API Metrics available.”,
  “Members”: [
     {
        “@odata.id”: “/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LustreStats”
     },
     {
        “@odata.id”: “/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LinuxStats”
     },
     {
        “@odata.id”: “/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/JobStats”
     },
     {
        “@odata.id”: “/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/EnvironmentalStats”
     },
     {
        “@odata.id”: “/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/TieringStats”
     }
  ],
  “Members@odata.count”: 5,
  “Name”: “MetricDefinitionCollection”
}


Details of the response:

    •    The Members field of this resource holds the collection of all supported Triggers
         resource endpoints
    •    The Members@odata.count shows how many total Triggers resources exist in the
         collection




14.6.2 Triggers Resources
The Triggers resource includes the NumericThresholds property, which defines the
thresholds for a numeric trigger to activate. Currently, four numeric thresholds are
supported: LowerCaution, LowerWarning, UpperCaution, and UpperWarning. When a
trigger is activated, a Redfish event is sent to the subscribers.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/Triggers.v1_3_2.json

Example Triggers GET request:

[root@kjlmo12-oem rest_api]# curl -k -H “X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}”
https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/Triggers/LinuxStats-CpuUsage-All
 | jq
{
   “@odata.context”: “Triggers.Triggers”,
   “@odata.id”: “/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/Triggers/LinuxStats-CpuUsage-All”,
   “@odata.type”: “Triggers.v1_1_4.Triggers”,
   “Id”: “LinuxStats-CpuUsage-All”,
   “Links”: {},
   “MetricType”: “Numeric”,
   “Name”: “LinuxStats-CpuUsage-All”,
   “NumericThresholds”: {
      “LowerCaution”: {},
      “LowerCautionUser”: {},
      “LowerCritical”: {},
      “LowerCriticalUser”: {},
      “LowerFatal”: {},
      “UpperCaution”: {
         “DwellTime”: “300”,
         “Reading”: 80
      },
      “UpperCautionUser”: {},
      “UpperCritical”: {
         “DwellTime”: “300”,
         “Reading”: 90
      },
      “UpperCriticalUser”: {},
      “UpperFatal”: {}
   },
   “Status”: {},
   “TriggerActions”: [
      “RedfishEvent”
   ]
}


Details of the response:

    •    UpperCaution: is the reading is above normal range.
    •    UpperCritical: is the reading is above normal range and requires attention
    •    LowerCaution: is the reading is below normal range
    •    LowerCritical: is the reading is below normal range and requires attention
    •    Reading: value of the threshold
       •   DwellTime: is the duration in Seconds that value must be over the threshold before
           the trigger is tripped.



 Example Event when a Triggers resource is tripped:

15. UpdateService Resource
The UpdateService resource lives directly under the ServiceRoot /redfish/v1 and can be seen by
issuing a GET request to /redfish/v1/UpdateService. It provides an entry point to the
SoftwareInventory Collection to see version information about various API software
components, as well as top-level API version information.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/UpdateService.v1_11_2.json
Example UpadateService GET request:

 # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}" https://kjlmo1200:8081/redfish/v1/UpdateService | jq
 {
     "@odata.context": "UpdateService.UpdateService",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/UpdateService",
     "@odata.type": "UpdateService.v1_9_0.UpdateService",
     "Description": "UpdateService for RFSF API",
     "HttpPushUriOptions": {
        "HttpPushUriApplyTime": {}
     },
     "Id": "UpdateService",
     "Name": "UpdateService",
     "ServiceEnabled": true,
     "SoftwareInventory": {
      "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/UpdateService/SoftwareInventory"
     },
     "Status": {}
 }


 Details of the response: There is not much detail provided to see in the response output. The
 important thing to note is that it provides the path to the SoftwareInventory Collection to work
 further down the resource tree to discover the software version information of the top-level
 API as well as all API service components.


 15.1 SoftwareInventoryCollection Resource
 The SoftwareInventory Collection resource provides a collection of individual
 SoftwareInventory resource odata.ids in the SoftwareInventory.Members field. This holds the
 endpoints of all SoftwareInventory resources that contain Software version information about
 the API.

 Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/SoftwareInventoryCollection.json

15.2 SoftwareInventory Resource
The SoftwareInventory resource contains version information about a particular piece of
Software that makes up the RFSF API. In this implementation, there is a SoftwareInventory
resource for each rpm installedd on the system to make up the API, as well as a resource that
contains top-level version information about the API as a whole. There is not aton of detail in
these resources, but can be useful to examine them to know which versions of the components
of the API are running on the system, as well as the top-level API version.

Schema: https://redfish.dmtf.org/schemas/v1/SoftwareInventory.v1_9_0.json
 Example SoftwareInventory GET request for individual API component:

  # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
  https://kjlmo1200:8081/redfish/v1/UpdateService/SoftwareInventory/rfsf-dp-api | jq
  {
    "@odata.context": "SoftwareInventory.SoftwareInventory",
    "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/UpdateService/SoftwareInventory/rfsf-dp-api",
    "@odata.type": "SoftwareInventory.v1_4_0.SoftwareInventory",
   "Description": "A RESTful API server that provides routers to redfish/swordfish endpoints, as well as request
  handlers to populate certain higher level redfish/swordfish models to represent clusters, nodes, and enclosures",
   "Id": "rfsf-dp-api",
   "Manufacturer": "HPE",
   "Name": "rfsf-dp-api SoftwareInventory",
   "Status": {},
      "Version": "1.0.x.6.9.999-11.733b7284"
  }



 Details of the response:
    • Description: description of the rpm package
    • Id: Resource Id that matches the rpm package name name
    • Manufacturer: producer of the rpm package
    • Name: resource name that contains rpm package name
    • Version: combination of rpm package version and release fields
 Example SoftwareInventory GET request for top-level API

  # curl -Ssk -H "X-Auth-Token: ${AUTH}"
  https://kjlmo1200:8081/redfish/v1/UpdateService/SoftwareInventory/api | jq
  {
    "@odata.context": "SoftwareInventory.SoftwareInventory",
    "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/UpdateService/SoftwareInventory/api",
   "@odata.type": "SoftwareInventory.v1_4_0.SoftwareInventory",
   "Description": "Top level RFSF API version information. Holds the over-arching API version info to represent the
  API as a whole.",
   "Id": "api",
   "Manufacturer": "HPE",
      "Name": "api SoftwareInventory",
      "Status": {},
      "Version": "v1.0.0"
  }



Details of the response: the details of the response are the same as the previous example,
however the information doesn’t derive directly from rpm packages, but rather describes API as
a whole.
16. rfsf-api-client: Client-side libraries to
interact with the RFSF API
The rfsf-api-client package provides a set of client-side libraries, examples, config files, etc. that
can be used for programmatic setup and interaction with the RFSF API on any given target
system. It is a python-based library that facilitates much of the manual setup described above, by
providing libraries to:

    •   Define a user and API destination to target throughout the monitoring life cycle
    •   Authenticate that user with prompt for user password and internally store the token for all
        future requests
    •   Discover the full resource tree that exists in the API, including all endpoints of all sub-
        trees
    •   Subscribe to receive general Events at a specified EventDestination
    •   Subscribe to receive MetricReport Events at a specified EventDestination for:
        LustreStats, LinuxStatus and JobStats metrics.
    •   Example EventReceiver services
    •   Event based monitoring example
    •   Periodic Interval of resources monitoring example

The following sections will step through the code, config files, and runtime examples setup and use the
rfsf-api-client libraries as described in the above bullets.


16.1. Populating the base config file to setup API destination
and API user

The rfsf-api-client package provides a “base” config file in order to specify both the destination
hostname or ip address of the Cluster where the API you’d like to interact with is running, as
well as the API user you’d like to authenticate to use the API. The config file is located here:
/etc/rfsf-api-client-base.config

By default the fields are empty, and must be populated:

 [root@kjlmo17-oem hpc-sp-rfsf-api-client]# cat /etc/rfsf-api-client-base.config
 # RFSF API setup configuration file


 ## specify information about target cluster here
 [system]
 # FQDN or IP address to connect to API on
 destination =
 ## specify information about user to authenticate here
 [authentication]
 # username to authenticate for API use
 user =



Example population of the rfsf-api-client-base.config file for destination:
kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net, user: dmatthews

 [root@kjlmo17-oem hpc-sp-rfsf-api-client]# cat /etc/rfsf-api-client-base.config
 # RFSF API setup configuration file


 ## specify information about target cluster here
 [system]
 # FQDN or IP address to connect to API on
 destination = kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net


 ## specify information about user to authenticate here
 [authentication]
 # username to authenticate for API use
 user = dmatthews




The RfsfClient object initialization will read this file in to populate both the user and destination
fields for the remainder of its lifetime, so they can be referenced and used in later steps.
Example:

 from rfsf_api_client.client.rfsf_api_client import RfsfClient, CONFIG_FILE_BASE
    rfsf_client = RfsfClient()
    print("Initialized base RfsfClient from config file: {0}".format(CONFIG_FILE_BASE))
    print("API destination...{0}".format(rfsf_client.destination))
    print("API user...{0}".format(rfsf_client.user))




16.2 Authenticate a user
Using the rfsf_api_client.authentication library
Once the RfsfClient object is initialized, you can then use the rfsf_api_client.authentication library to
authenticate the RfsfClient.user which was previously defined and loaded from the base config file. To
authenticate a user successfully, they must already be an existing cscli admins user on the cluster. See
section 3 “Token based API Authentication” for more details. To perform the authentication, the
rfsf_api_client.authentication.Auth object must be initialized with the RfsfClient.user from before. Once
initialized, the “authenticate()” method may be called on the object. If successful, a token attribute will be
populated automatically on the Auth object, this token attribute can then be assigned to the top-level
RfsfClient.token field for user for the remainder of the lifetime of the RfsfClient object. As indicated in
the comments, the below code assumes you have already initialized the RfsfClient object for a target user
and API destination.

Code example:

 import sys
 from rfsf_api_client.authentication.auth import Auth
    # note, the below assume you have already initialized the RfsfClient object as seen above
    # note, the below assumes you have already authenticated the rfsf_client.user and received a valid
 rfsf_client.token
    response_content = None
    err_msg = None
    auth = Auth(rfsf_client.user)
    response_content, err_msg = auth.authenticate()
    if err_msg:
      print("Failed to authenticate user: {0}. {1}... exiting".format(rfsf_client.user, err_msg))
      sys.exit(1)
   else:
      print("Successfully authenticated user: {0} ".format(rfsf_client.user))
      print(response_content)
   # Assign auth token to top-level rfsf_client object
   rfsf_client.token = auth.token


The authenticate() method seen above, will prompt the user for a password to be entered to
generate a Session request to send to the API. The username and password will be checked
against local cluster LDAP instance to validate an existing admins user, for more details, again
see section 3 “Token based API Authentication”. The authenticate method will either return a
successful response or an error message. If request it sends is successful, the response will be the
/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/{SessionId} resource it created. If it is not successful, the
error message will contain a description.

Here are some examples of running the code above and output you’d expect to see.

Example output when username / password cannot be validated – as implied before, the output
is shown to initialize RfsfClient:

 Initilized base RfsfClient from config file: /etc/rfsf-api-client-base.config
 API destination...kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net
 API user...dmatthews
 Password for user dmatthews:
 Failed to authenticate user: dmatthews. "Bad response code 401 from
 https://kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net:8081/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions! {'error': {'code': '401',
 'message': 'Failed to authorize Session for user: dmatthews. LDAP Result Code 49 \"Invalid Credentials\": '}}"...
 exiting


Example output when username / password are valid and a Session resource is returned – as
implied before, the output is shown to initialize RfsfClient as well:
 Initialized base RfsfClient from config file: /etc/rfsf-api-client-base.config
 API destination...kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net
 API user...dmatthews
 Password for user dmatthews:
 Successfully authenticated user: dmatthews
 {
   "@odata.context": "Session.Session",
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/K6NzwzgpkskbwHT8t9yCVV",
     "@odata.type": "Session.v1_3_0.Session",
     "Description": "Session for user dmatthews",
     "Id": "K6NzwzgpkskbwHT8t9yCVV",
     "Name": "dmatthews Session",
     "Oem": {
        "StartTime": "Mon Feb 13 19:26:31 UTC 2023",
       "ExpirationTime": "Tue Feb 14 07:26:31 UTC 2023",
       "TimeLeft": "11h59m59.999973521s"
     },
     "UserName": "dmatthews"
 }



The above output indicates that the user ‘dmatthews’ has been authenticated to use the API and
received a token to pass with future requests, details of the session are also returned as seen
above.


16.3 Rfsf_api_client.inventory resource_tree discovery

Once a user is authenticated as seen above, one of the next important things to do is to discover
the full resource tree that the API is tracking. To do this, the rfsf_api_client.inventory library
provides a ResourceTree object which provides a get_resource_tree() method used to send
several requests to the API to discover and build out a full tree of endpoints, such that every
resource tree endpoint known to the API is discovered and tracked in the ResourceTree object.
The ResourceTree object provides a tree field to hold the entire resource tree structure, but also
provides fields for some of the “sub-tree” structures to make indexing into the tree to find a
particular resource easier. The entire populated resource_tree object should then be assigned to
the top-level RfsfClient.resource_tree field to be used throughout the monitoring lifecycle. The
following code shows an example of initializing the ResourceTree object, populating it with
get_resource_tree, and assigning that to the top-level RfsfClient object. As indicated in the
comments, the below code assumes you have already initialized the RfsfClient object for a target
user and API destination, as well as authenticated that user and received a valid token:

 import sys
 from rfsf_api_client.inventory.resource_tree import ResourceTree
    # note, the below assume you have already initialized the RfsfClient object as seen above
    # note, the below assumes you have already authenticated the rfsf_client.user and received a valid
 rfsf_client.token
    resource_tree = ResourceTree(rfsf_client.token)
     err_msg = resource_tree.get_resource_tree()
     if err_msg:
         print("Failed to discover API resource tree with error: {0}... exiting".format(err_msg))
         sys.exit(1)
     else:
         print("Successfully discovered API resource tree!")
     # resource tree object assigned here
     # can now reference rfsf_client.resource_tree attributes
     rfsf_client.resource_tree = resource_tree


If successful, the rfsf_client.resource_tree can then be used for monitoring in various ways,
some examples will be shown below.

Example output when resource_tree discovery is successful – as implied before, the output is
shown to initialize RfsfClient and authenticate a user as well:

 Initialized base RfsfClient from config file: /etc/rfsf-api-client-base.config
 API destination...kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net
 API user...dmatthews
 Password for user dmatthews:
 Successfully authenticated user: dmatthews
 {
   "@odata.context": "Session.Session",
     "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/K6NzwzgpkskbwHT8t9yCVV",
     "@odata.type": "Session.v1_3_0.Session",
     "Description": "Session for user dmatthews",
     "Id": "K6NzwzgpkskbwHT8t9yCVV",
     "Name": "dmatthews Session",
     "Oem": {
       "StartTime": "Mon Feb 13 19:26:31 UTC 2023",
       "ExpirationTime": "Tue Feb 14 07:26:31 UTC 2023",
       "TimeLeft": "11h59m59.999973521s"
     },
     "UserName": "dmatthews"
 }
 Successfully discovered API resource tree!




16.4 Event Subscription with rfsf_api_client.subscription
library
Another important piece of functionality to setup for monitoring using the RFSF API is to
subscribe to receive Events from the API EventService. For more details on the EventService
and Events in RFSF API, please see section 10 “RFSF API EventService and Events”.

The rfsf_api_client.subscription library provides an EventSubscription object that can be used to
subscribe for events and metric reports. After initialization, it must load a config file with
information about the subscription requirements in order to generate and send a Subscription
request to API EventService. For generic Event subscription, this information is specified in the
“/etc/rfsf-api-client-event-subscription.config” file.

By default, the file comes un-populated:

 [root@kjlmo17-oem hpc-sp-rfsf-api-client]# cat /etc/rfsf-api-client-event-subscription.config
 ## specify general Event subscription specific information here:
 [eventsubscription]
 # EventReceiver service EventDestination endpoint to receive Events broadcasted from dp-api EventService
 event_destination =
 # Unique ID for EventDestination
 event_destination_id =




The file must be populated with an event_destination, which is the target destination endpoint
you would like RFSF API to send events to, as well as a unique event_destination_id, which
provides a unique id to the EventDestination resource the subscription request will create.
Example which will create a subscription to receive events on event_destination:
http://172.16.0.1:8082/eventreceiver/, with event_destination_id: “test-event-receiver":

 [root@kjlmo17-oem hpc-sp-rfsf-api-client]# cat /etc/rfsf-api-client-event-subscription.config
 ## specify general Event subscription specific information here:
 [eventsubscription]
 # EventReceiver service EventDestination endpoint to receive Events broadcasted from dp-api EventService
 event_destination = http://172.16.0.1:8082/eventreceiver/
 # Unique ID for EventDestination
 event_destination_id = test-event-receiver



Once the request is sent to subscribe to receive events, a client side EventReceiver service must
be setup to listen for Events sent to the target event_destination by RFSF API EventService.
Please see section ”10.7 Subscribers Receiving Events” for more details.

As mentioned previously, the rfsf_api_client.subscription.EventSubscription must load a config
file after initialization, so once the /etc/rfsf-api-client-event-subscription.config file is populated,
the next step is to initialize the EventSubscription object, and call the
load_event_subscription_config(<file>) with this file passed in. Once the object is initialized and
config is loaded, you may use it to call the subscribe_to_events() method which will build and
send a subscription request to the API. If the request is successful, the resulting
EventSubscription.destination_id should be added to the rfsf_client.event_subscriptions list for
tracking. The following code example does all of this. As indicated in the comments, the below
code assumes you have already initialized the RfsfClient object for a target user and API
destination, as well as authenticated that user and received a valid token:

 import sys
 from rfsf_api_client.subscription.subscribe import EventSubscription, CONFIG_FILE_EVENT_SUBCRIPTION
    # note, the below assume you have already initialized the RfsfClient object as seen above
    # note, the below assumes you have already authenticated the rfsf_client.user and received a valid
 rfsf_client.token
    response_content = None
    err_msg = None
    event_subscription = EventSubscription(rfsf_client.token)
    event_subscription.load_event_subscription_config(CONFIG_FILE_EVENT_SUBCRIPTION)
    response_content, err_msg = event_subscription.subscribe_to_events()
    if err_msg:
        print("Failed to subscribe for Event Destination: {0}. {1}... exiting".format(event_subscription.event_destination,
 err_msg))
       sys.exit(1)
    else:
       print("Successfully subscribed to receive Events on destination: {0}, Id:
 {1}".format(event_subscription.event_destination, event_subscription.destination_id))
       print(response_content)
    # Track event subscription endpoint in top-level rfsf_client object
   rfsf_client.event_subscriptions.append(event_subscription.destination_id)



The subscribe_to_events() method will either return a valid response or an error message. If the
request it sends is successful, the response content will be that of the
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} resource that was created. If it is
not successful, the error message will indicate why.

Here is an example of a EventDestination response from a successful subscribe_to_events() call -
as implied, the output is shown to initialize RfsfClient and authenticate a user as well:

 Initilized base RfsfClient from config file: /etc/rfsf-api-client-base.config
 API destination...kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net
 API user...dmatthews
 Password for user dmatthews:
 Successfully authenticated user: dmatthews
 {
   "@odata.context": "Session.Session",
   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/men84q38zDVourFj6V4YgY",
   "@odata.type": "Session.v1_3_0.Session",
   "Description": "Session for user dmatthews",
     "Id": "men84q38zDVourFj6V4YgY",
     "Name": "dmatthews Session",
     "Oem": {
       "StartTime": "Mon Feb 13 19:23:11 UTC 2023",
       "ExpirationTime": "Tue Feb 14 07:23:11 UTC 2023",
       "TimeLeft": "11h59m59.999964083s"
     },
     "UserName": "dmatthews"
 }
 Successfully subscribed to receive Events on destination: http://172.16.0.1:8082/eventreceiver/, Id:
 /redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-event-receiver
 {
    "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/test-event-receiver",
