16.5 LustreStats MetricReport Events Subscription
Using the rfsf_api_client.subscription library

Another important piece of functionality to setup for monitoring using the RFSF API is to
subscribe to receive MetricReport Events from the API EventService, which provides a data
streaming capability for various system Metrics. For more details on the MetricReport Events in
RFSF API, please see section 11 “MetricReport Event Subscriptions for Metric data Streaming”.

The same rfsf_api_client.subscription library and EventSubscription object is used to subscribe
to receive MetricReport Events in the same way that it is to subscribe for generic Events, the
difference comes in the specific config file that is loaded after object initialization. To receive
LustreStats MetricReport Events, the config file used is: “/etc/rfsf-api-client-lustrestats-metric-
report-subscription.config”.

By default, the file comes un-populated, except for the data_set – which is predefined to
LustreStats and event_types – which is predefined to MetricReport:
 [root@kjlmo17-oem hpc-sp-rfsf-api-client]# cat /etc/rfsf-api-client-lustrestats-metric-report-subscription.config
 ## specify general Event subscription specific information here:
 [eventsubscription]
 # EventReceiver service EventDestination endpoint to receive Events broadcasted from dp-api EventService
 event_destination =
 # Unique ID for EventDestination
 event_destination_id =


 ## Next specify MetricReport specific information
 [metricreport]
 # Type of events to subscribe to, MetricReport value is required here for dp-api MetricReport setup
 event_types = MetricReport
 # Number of seconds which dp-api will send MetricReport events to EventDestination.Destination endpoint
 send_interval =
 # Type of MetricReport data to be sent, options are: LustreStats, JobStats, LinuxStats. Only one may be specified at
 a time
 data_set = LustreStats


The file must be populated with an event_destination, and event_destination_id the same as the
generic event subscription config file, however, some additional metric report specific fields
exist that must be populated or are pre-populated in the [metricreport] section of the config file.

event_types: must be set to MetricReport and is pre-populated

send_interval: must specify the interval client would like to receive these Events in seconds.

data_set: specifies the target data_set for the MetricReport events, and is pre-populated to
LustreStats in this file. The following example will subscribe to receive MetricReports on
event_destination: http://172.16.0.1:8082/metricsreceiver/, with event_destinaton_id: lustre-stats-
metric-receiver, at a send_interval of 5 seconds:

 [root@kjlmo17-oem hpc-sp-rfsf-api-client]# cat /etc/rfsf-api-client-lustrestats-metric-report-subscription.config
 ## specify general Event subscription specific information here:
 [eventsubscription]
 # EventReceiver service EventDestination endpoint to receive Events broadcasted from dp-api EventService
 event_destination = http://172.16.0.1:8082/metricsreceiver/
 # Unique ID for EventDestination
 event_destination_id = lustre-stats-metric-receiver


 ## Next specify MetricReport specific information
 [metricreport]
 # Type of events to subscribe to, MetricReport value is required here for dp-api MetricReport setup
 event_types = MetricReport
 # Number of seconds which dp-api will send MetricReport events to EventDestination.Destination endpoint
 send_interval = 5
 # Type of MetricReport data to be sent, options are: LustreStats, JobStats, LinuxStats. Only one may be specified at
 a time
 data_set = LustreStats



Once the request is sent to subscribe to receive MetricReport events, a client side EventReceiver
service must be setup to listen for Events sent to the target event_destination by RFSF API
EventService. Please see section ”10.7 Subscribers Receiving Events” for more details.

As mentioned previously, the rfsf_api_client.subscription.EventSubscription must load a config
file after initialization, so once the /etc/rfsf-api-client-lustrestats-metric-report-
subscription.config” file is populated, the next step is to initialize the EventSubscription object,
and call the load_event_subscription_config(<file>) with this file passed in. Once the object is
initialized and config is loaded, you may use it to call the subscribe_to_events() method which
will build and send a subscription request to the API. If the request is successful, the resulting
EventSubscription.destination_id should be added to the rfsf_client.event_subscriptions list for
tracking. The following code example does all of this. As indicated in the comments, the below
code assumes you have already initialized the RfsfClient object for a target user and API
destination, as well as authenticated that user and received a valid token:
 import sys
 from rfsf_api_client.subscription.subscribe import EventSubscription,
 CONFIG_FILE_LUSTRESTATS_METRIC_REPORT_SUBSCRIPTION
    # note, the below assume you have already initialized the RfsfClient object as seen above
    # note, the below assumes you have already authenticated the rfsf_client.user and received a valid
 rfsf_client.token
    response_content = None
   err_msg = None
   lustrestats_subscription = EventSubscription(rfsf_client.token)


 lustrestats_subscription.load_event_subscription_config(CONFIG_FILE_LUSTRESTATS_METRIC_REPORT_SUBSCRIPTI
 ON)
    response_content, err_msg = lustrestats_subscription.subscribe_to_events(metric_report=True)
   if err_msg:
       print("Failed to subscribe for {0} MetricReport Event Destination: {1}. {2}...
 exiting".format(lustrestats_subscription.data_set, lustrestats_subscription.event_destination, err_msg))
       sys.exit(1)
   else:
       print("Successfully subscribed to receive {0} MetricReport Events on destination: {1}, Id:
 {2}".format(lustrestats_subscription.data_set, lustrestats_subscription.event_destination,
 lustrestats_subscription.destination_id))
       print(response_content)
    # Track event subscription endpoint in top-level rfsf_client object
    rfsf_client.event_subscriptions.append(lustrestats_subscription.destination_id)
The subscribe_to_events() method will either return a valid response or an error message. If the
request it sends is successful, the response content will be that of the
/redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions/{EventDestinationId} resource that was created. If it is
not successful, the error message will indicate why.

Here is an example of a EventDestination response from a successful subscribe_to_events() call -
as implied, the output is shown to initialize RfsfClient and authenticate a user as well:

 Initialized base RfsfClient from config file: /etc/rfsf-api-client-base.config

 API user...dmatthews
 Password for user dmatthews:
 Successfully authenticated user: dmatthews
 {

   "@odata.id": "/redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions/i4n3CYMZx5TuKjZJvhA3BP",

16.6 LinuxStats MetricReport Events Subscription
rfsf_api_client.subscription library

Same as the mechanism to subscribe to receive LustreStats MetricReport Events, you can also
subscribe to receive MetricReport Events on other data sets, one of which being: LinuxStats.
LinuxStatus MetricReport subscriptions and Events work the same as MetricReports for other
data sets, just provide different data. For more details on the MetricReport Events in RFSF API,
please see section 11 “MetricReport Event Subscriptions for Metric data Streaming”.

The same rfsf_api_client.subscription library and EventSubscription object is used to subscribe
to receive MetricReport Events in the same way that it is to subscribe for generic Events, the
difference comes in the specific config file that is loaded after object initialization. To receive
LinuxStats MetricReport Events, the config file used is: “/etc/rfsf-api-client-linuxstats-metric-
report-subscription.config”.

By default, the file comes un-populated, except for the data_set – which is predefined to
LinuxStats and event_types – which is predefined to MetricReport:

 [root@kjlmo17-oem ~]# cat /etc/rfsf-api-client-linuxstats-metric-report-subscription.config
 ## specify general Event subscription specific information here:
 [eventsubscription]
 # EventReceiver service EventDestination endpoint to receive Events broadcasted from dp-api EventService

 # Unique ID for EventDestination

 # Number of seconds which dp-api will send MetricReport events to EventDestination.Destination endpoint
 send_interval =
 # Type of MetricReport data to be sent, options are: LustreStats, JobStats, LinuxStats. Only one may be specified at
 a time
 data_set = LinuxStats



The file must be populated with an event_destination, and event_destination_id the same as the
generic event subscription config file, however, some additional metric report specific fields
exist that must be populated or are pre-populated in the [metricreport] section of the config file.

event_types: must be set to MetricReport and is pre-populated

send_interval: must specify the interval client would like to receive these Events in seconds.

data_set: specifies the target data_set for the MetricReport events, and is pre-populated to
LustreStats in this file. The following example will subscribe to receive MetricReports on
event_destination: http://172.16.0.1:8082/metricsreceiver/, with event_destinaton_id: linux-stats-
metric-receiver, at a send_interval of 15 seconds:

16.8 Resource Tree Iteration Examples

Once the entire resource tree that the RFSF API tracks has been discovered and populated in the
top-level RfsfClient object, it is important to understand the structure of the tree and how to
iterate in order to reach all available API resource endpoints and use them for some sort of
periodic monitoring via GET requests to each endpoint. As stated in section 4
“Redfish/Swordfish API ServiceRoot” - all resources live underneath the service root:
/redfish/v1, thus – this is the entry point to begin iterating through the structure of the tree. Then,
as suggested in section various sub-sections of section 2 “High level usage”, the next level to
traverse down the tree is the top-level resource collection endpoints seen just underneath the
ServiceRoot. From there, you look at each resource within the collections to determine additional
resource collections within that, and so on.

The following shows a couple of code examples that can be used to traverse into the resource
tree, starting both at the service root, as well as various service collection entry points, to
discover and print all resource endpoints within.

First, we will look at the rfsf_client.resource_tree object attributes that hold the service root
endpoint, as well as all top-level service entry point endpoints:

 rfsf_client.resource_tree.service_root # /redfish/v1
 rfsf_client.resource_tree.event_service_uri # /redfish/v1/EventService
 rfsf_client.resource_tree.subscriptions # /redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions
 rfsf_client.resource_tree.event_collection_uri # /redfish/v1/Events
 rfsf_client.resource_tree.session_service_uri # /redfish/v1/SessionService
 rfsf_client.resource_tree.session_collection_uri # /redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions
 rfsf_client.resource_tree.chassis_collection_uri # /redfish/v1/Chassis
 rfsf_client.resource_tree.storage_service_collection_uri # /redfish/v1/StorageServices
 rfsf_client.resource_tree.storage_system_collection_uri # /redfish/v1/StorageSystems




Next, we’ll look at how to pull out the service root tree from the full rfsf_client.tree structure.
This service root tree, can then be used to further index into the structure with the top-level
URIs:

# pull ServiceRoot and below out of full ResourceTree
service_root_tree = rfsf_client.resource_tree.tree[rfsf_client.resource_tree.service_root]

The following will then show examples of either: 1) indexing into the top-level service_root_tree
or 2) indexing into a starting resource collection substructure, to print out all collected resource
endpoints that the API tracks. Since the output can be very long, only code examples will be
shown. Please see rfsf_api_client.monitoring.rfsf_api_monitoring library for a full set of
examples to run.


/redfish/v1/EventService and /redfish/v1/EventService/Subscriptions
   ## 1) index into full resource_tree to pull it out
   print("########## EventService Resource (Subscriptions) {0} FROM FULL TREE
 ##########".format(rfsf_client.resource_tree.event_service_uri))
   event_service_tree = service_root_tree[rfsf_client.resource_tree.event_service_uri]
   print(json.dumps(event_service_tree, indent=4))
   ## 2) reference the collection attribute collected directly
   print("########## Subscriptions Collection Resource ##########")
   print(json.dumps(rfsf_client.resource_tree.subscriptions, indent=4))


/redfish/v1/SessionService and /redfish/v1/SessionService/Sessions
   ## 1) index into full resource_tree to pull it out
   print("########## SessionService Resource (Sessions) {0} FROM FULL TREE
 ##########".format(rfsf_client.resource_tree.event_service_uri))
   session_service_tree = service_root_tree[rfsf_client.resource_tree.session_service_uri]
   print(json.dumps(session_service_tree, indent=4))
   ## 2) reference the collection attribute collected directly
   print("########## Sessions Collection Resource ##########")
   print(json.dumps(rfsf_client.resource_tree.sessions, indent=4))



/redfish/v1/Events
   ## 1) index into full resource_tree to pull it out
   print("########## Event Collection Resource {0} FROM FULL TREE
 ##########".format(rfsf_client.resource_tree.event_collection_uri))
   event_collection_tree = service_root_tree[rfsf_client.resource_tree.event_collection_uri]
   print(json.dumps(event_collection_tree, indent=4))
   ## 2) reference the collection attribute collected directly
   print("########## Event Collection Resource ##########")
   print(json.dumps(rfsf_client.resource_tree.event_collection_members, indent=4))



/redfish/v1/Chassis
  ## 1) index into full resource_tree to pull it out
  print("########## Chassis Collection Resource Tree {0} FROM FULL TREE
##########".format(rfsf_client.resource_tree.chassis_collection_uri))
  # pull ChassisCollection and below out of full ResourceTree
  chassis_tree = service_root_tree[rfsf_client.resource_tree.chassis_collection_uri]
  for chassis_member in rfsf_client.resource_tree.chassis_members:
     for k, v in chassis_member.items():
        print("Chassis: {0}".format(v))
        chassis_resources = chassis_tree[v]
        print(json.dumps(chassis_resources, indent=4))
  ## 2) reference the collection attribute collected directly
  print("########## Chassis Collection Resource Tree ##########")
  print(json.dumps(rfsf_client.resource_tree.chassis_resources, indent=4))



/redfish/v1/StorageServices
   ## 1) index into full resource_tree to pull it out
   print("########## StorageService Collection Resource Tree {0} FROM FULL TREE
 ##########".format(rfsf_client.resource_tree.storage_service_collection_uri))
   # pull StorageServiceCollection and below out of full ResourceTree
   storage_service_tree = service_root_tree[rfsf_client.resource_tree.storage_service_collection_uri]
   for storage_service_member in rfsf_client.resource_tree.storage_service_members:
     for k, v in storage_service_member.items():
        print("StorageService: {0}".format(v))
        storage_service_resources = storage_service_tree[v]
        print(json.dumps(storage_service_resources, indent=4))
   ## 2) reference the collection attribute collected directly
   print("########## StorageService Collection Resource Tree ##########")
   print(json.dumps(rfsf_client.resource_tree.storage_service_resources, indent=4))



/redfish/v1/StorageSystems
   ## 1) index into full resource_tree to pull it out
   print("########## StorageSystem Collection Resource Tree {0} FROM FULL TREE
 ##########".format(rfsf_client.resource_tree.storage_system_collection_uri))
   # pull StorageSystem Collection and below out of full ResourceTree
   storage_systems_tree = service_root_tree[rfsf_client.resource_tree.storage_system_collection_uri]
   for storage_system_member in rfsf_client.resource_tree.storage_system_members:
      for k, v in storage_system_member.items():
         print("StorageSystem: {0}".format(v))
        storage_system_resources = storage_systems_tree[v]
        print(json.dumps(storage_system_resources, indent=4))
   ## 2) reference the collection attribute collected directly
   print("########## StorageSystem Collection Resource Tree ##########")
   print(json.dumps(rfsf_client.resource_tree.storage_system_resources, indent=4))




16.9 Example Event based monitoring setup

Once you have subscribed to receive generic Events on resources at some destination that was
appended to the rfsf_client.event_subscriptions list, you can programmatically start up an
EventReceiver service as a background thread to listen for Events broadcasted from RFSF API
EventService. This example starts the POST request handler in a daemon thread, and in the main
loop receives Events from the thread off of a queue. Once it receives and event off the queue, it
will parse the resource id which the Event occurred and check the state of the Event with a GET
request to that Event. For more details on the event receiver started in the thread, please see
rfsf_api_client.event_receiver.generic_event_receiver library.

The following code shows the example described above.
   """
      Example to start EventReceiver and process / react to Events:
      The following code shows an example use case of how to start up an EventReceiver, listening on the
 EventDestination endpoint specified in
      the generic Event subscription config file: /etc/rfsf-api-client-event-subscription.config. It relies on the
 event_subscription object previously
      created to track to start and track a daemon thread that will start the EventReceiver service. A Queue is then
 used to process Events received
      from the API on the EventDesitnation endpoint the receiver is listening on and react to them in some way.


     This particular example, will parse out the Event.Oem.ResourceId field from the Event resource body. This
 ResourceId field indicates which resource
        in the RfsfClient.resource_tree the Event occurred on. Since an event was received on this ResourceId, a GET
 request is issued to the resource endpoint
        in an atttempt to see what changed in the resource. The functionality can be expanded to do as the client sees
 fit to react to Events on resources.
     """
      # setup event Queue for communication with event receiver threads
   rfsf_client.event_queue = queue.Queue()
   # create thread for event receiver
   generic_event_receiver_thrd = threading.Thread(target=start_event_receiver,
 name=event_subscription.destination_id, args=(event_subscription.event_destination, rfsf_client.event_queue))
generic_event_receiver_thrd.daemon = True
# Track event_destination to start event receiver on
rfsf_client.event_receivers[event_subscription.event_destination] = generic_event_receiver_thrd
generic_event_receiver_thrd.start()
while True:
  event_dict = {}
  resources = []
  if not rfsf_client.event_queue.empty():
     event_str = rfsf_client.event_queue.get()
     # TODO add try/except here
     try:
        event_dict = json.loads(event_str)
        print("Received Event {0}, type: {1}".format(event_dict, type(event_dict)))
        event_list = event_dict.get("Events", [])
        for event in event_list:
          event_oem = event.get("Oem", {})
          resource_id = event_oem.get("ResourceId")
          if resource_id:
              resources.append(resource_id)
       for rsrc in resources:
          print("Checking Status Event Resource {0}".format(rsrc))
          response_content, err_msg = check_resource(rsrc, rfsf_client.destination, rfsf_client.token)
          if err_msg:
              print(err_msg)
          else:
              print(response_content)
     except Exception as e:
       print("Failed to process Event. {0}".format(e))
Appendix 1.                    Client Notes
Client location on ClusterStor
So to start, the “rfsf-api-client” package is available on the local cluster repo, and can be
downloaded from either mgmt node and then scp’d off of the system to wherever they’d like to
run it.

n00 # ~ dnf download rfsf-api-client

^^ this should download the rpm to the CWD and they should be able to copy it off of the system
over the EAN network on pub0 to another server or location in their lab.

Once the rpm is copied to another server, so long as python3 is available on that server, they
should be able to install it without any dependency issues.

Next step would be to correctly populate the config files they’d like to use, I will show an
example of the two required (which they already noted) with comments – first the base.config
file:

[root@c5ftc03-oem ~]# cat /etc/rfsf-api-client-base.config

# RFSF API setup configuration file
## specify information about target cluster here

[system]

# FQDN or IP address to connect to API on

destination = kjlmo1200.hpc.amslabs.hpecorp.net # <-- destination FQDN or IP address of
mgmt=primary host on EAN (login IP or FQDN)



## specify information about user to authenticate here

[authentication]

# username to authenticate for API use

user = dmatthews # <-- user to authenticate to use the API with (previously created with cscli
admins add as documentation describes)



Next, the linuxstats-metric-report-subscription.config file:
[root@c5ftc03-oem ~]# cat /etc/rfsf-api-client-linuxstats-metric-report-subscription.config

## specify general Event subscription specific information here:

[eventsubscription]

# EventReceiver service EventDestination endpoint to receive Events broadcasted from dp-api
EventService

event_destination = http://172.16.0.1:9085/metricsreceiver/ # <-- example client endpoint that
EventReceiver service is listening on



# Unique ID for EventDestination

event_destination_id = test-linux-stats # <-- some unique Id for the Subscription



## Next specify MetricReport specific information

[metricreport]



# Type of events to subscribe to, MetricReport value is required here for dp-api MetricReport
setup

event_types = MetricReport



# Number of seconds which dp-api will send MetricReport events to
EventDestination.Destination endpoint

send_interval = 60 # <-- 60s is the default SensingInterval for LinuxStats defined by
/redfish/v1/TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions/LinuxStats resource, this can be changed or
updated with a PUT or PATCH request to that resource, but subscription request requires that the
send_interval is equal to or greater than the SensingInterval time defined in
TelemetryService/MetricDefinitions for each data set
# Type of MetricReport data to be sent, options are: LustreStats, JobStats, LinuxStats. Only one
may be specified at a time

data_set = LinuxStats




Once those two files are in place, then the example code they provided is pretty close to what
would be required to create the subscription. I’ll share an example derived from “/usr/share/rfsf-
api-client/examples/monitoring/rfsf_api_monitoring.py”:



import sys

import json

from rfsf_api_client.client.rfsf_api_client import RfsfClient, CONFIG_FILE_BASE

from rfsf_api_client.authentication.auth import Auth

from rfsf_api_client.subscription.subscribe import EventSubscription,
CONFIG_FILE_LINUXSTATS_METRIC_REPORT_SUBSCRIPTION



rfsf_client = RfsfClient()

print("Initilized base RfsfClient from config file: {0}".format(CONFIG_FILE_BASE))

print("API destination...{0}".format(rfsf_client.destination))

print("API user...{0}".format(rfsf_client.user))



response_content = None

err_msg = None

auth = Auth(rfsf_client.user)

response_content, err_msg = auth.authenticate()
if err_msg:

  print("Failed to authenticate user: {0}. {1}... exiting".format(rfsf_client.user, err_msg))

  sys.exit(1)

else:

  print("Successfully authenticated user: {0} ".format(rfsf_client.user))

  print(json.dumps(response_content, indent=4))

# Assign auth token to top-level rfsf_client object

rfsf_client.token = auth.token



response_content = None

err_msg = None

linuxtats_subscription = EventSubscription(rfsf_client.token)

linuxtats_subscription.load_event_subscription_config(CONFIG_FILE_LINUXSTATS_METRI
C_REPORT_SUBSCRIPTION)

response_content, err_msg = linuxtats_subscription.subscribe_to_events(metric_report=True)

if err_msg:

   print("Failed to subscribe for {0} MetricReport Event Destination: {1}. {2}...
exiting".format(linuxtats_subscription.data_set, linuxtats_subscription.event_destination,
err_msg))

  sys.exit(1)

else:

   print("Successfully subscribed to receive {0} MetricReport Events on destination: {1}, Id:
{2}".format(linuxtats_subscription.data_set, linuxtats_subscription.event_destination,
linuxtats_subscription.destination_id))

  print(json.dumps(response_content, indent=4))
# Track event subscription endpoint in top-level rfsf_client object

rfsf_client.event_subscriptions.append(linuxtats_subscription.destination_id)




The above code simply creates the subscription, prints the response, and exists – whether that is
successful or not. The next piece is setting up a client receiver. Using the example above where
the EventDestination.Destination was set as “http://172.16.0.1:9085/metricsreceiver/” – I’ll show
starting an EventRecevier listing on port 9085 using the rfsf-api-client examples:



[root@kjlmo17-oem ~]# python3 /usr/share/rfsf-api-
client/examples/metrics_receiver/test_metrics_receiver.py 9085

INFO:root:Starting httpd...



The above is now setup to receive MetricReport’s from dp-api EventService in the form of a
POST request from dp-api-server -> the client Destination EventRecevier. I’ll note that
“/usr/share/rfsf-api-client/examples/monitoring/rfsf_api_monitoring.py” also provides an
example of setting up an event receiver thread and processing Events received on a queue that
they could take a look at to expand the basic example receiver, code is starting here:



  """

     Example to start EventReceiver and process / react to Events:

     ...



With all of this being said, I’d like to emphasize that rfsf-api-client is largely only intended to
provide examples. There are few uses of it in production by cscli, but at a very limited capacity.
The goal was to provide base libraries to authenticate, discover the resource tree, subscribe to
receive events, and objects to store info in. The /usr/share/rfsf-api-client/examples in the package
are intended to show examples of using the libraries, but are meant to be expanded upon, i.e. we
do not provide a fully capable client side library, just enough to get people started and exposed to
programmatically interacting with the API.
